1201 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kevin S. (In re K.S.)


No. 2-02-0861


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


365 Ill. App. 3d 566; 850 N.E.2d 335; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 517; 302 Ill. Dec. 898



June 6, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 14, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Kevin S. (In re K.S.), 221 Ill. 2d 638, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1609 (Ill., Sept. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 02--JA--14. Honorable Valerie Boettle Ceckowski, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Kevin S. (In re K.S.), 343 Ill. App. 3d 177, 796 N.E.2d 215, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1132, 277 Ill. Dec. 500 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A circuit court adjudicated the child neglected, made the child a ward of the court, and placed the child under the legal guardianship of the Department of Children and Family Services. The appellate court reversed and ordered that guardianship and custody of the child be placed with respondent father. The Illinois Supreme Court denied the State's petition for leave to appeal but directed the appellate court to vacate its judgment and reconsider.


OVERVIEW: The father contended that the trial court erred when it adjudicated the child a neglected minor. The appellate court found no error, noting that the mother stipulated to allegations that the mother failed to protect the child by failing to follow the safety plan of the Department of Children and Family Services and the father failed to present any rebuttal evidence. The father also contended that the trial court erred in ordering the father to complete a sexual offender evaluation and follow the resulting recommendations because there was no law or fact to support such an order. The appellate court agreed, noting that the complete lack of evidence against the father led to the conclusion that the trial court's actions were both an abuse of discretion and against the manifest weight of the evidence. The mother's stipulation stating that allegations of sexual molestation had been made was the only "evidence" that the trial court heard. The trial court could not order such an evaluation based only upon uncharged, unsubstantiated, and unproved allegations that were misconstrued as evidence; the State was required to prove the allegations by a preponderance of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The finding of neglect was affirmed. The trial court's dispositional order was reversed and the case was remanded for a new dispositional hearing.

 

1202 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Whitfield


No. 1-05-0751


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


366 Ill. App. 3d 448; 851 N.E.2d 730; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 483; 303 Ill. Dec. 543



June 2, 2006, Decided  
June 2, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 4, 2006.
Appeal granted by People v. Whitfield, 221 Ill. 2d 670, 857 N.E.2d 683, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1590, 306 Ill. Dec. 284 (2006)
Reversed by People v. Whitfield, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1706 (Ill., Dec. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 14628. The Honorable Thomas M. Davy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Remand; mittimus corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) convicted defendant upon finding him guilty of possession of a motor vehicle, and sentenced him as a Class X offender to eight years in prison. Defendant appealed based on his claims that he should have received credit for probation time, for time he spent in a mandatory work program, and for time he served prior to sentencing, and asked that the mittimus be corrected.


OVERVIEW: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and sentenced as a Class X offender to eight years in prison. He appealed, and contended that the trial court erred in not considering, as a sentencing credit, time he served under probation, and whether his mandatory Sheriff's Work Alternative Program (SWAP) time was creditable as well. He also contended that his mittimus had to be corrected to reflect a one-day credit for time served prior to sentencing and to reflect the proper conviction. He also asked that his case be remanded for a determination as to crediting with respect to his probation and SWAP time. The appellate court found that the State had conceded that defendant was entitled to a one-day credit for presentence time that he spent in custody and that the mittimus should be corrected to reflect that his conviction was for Class 2 offense of simple possession rather than a greater offense. It also found that it did not to consider his SWAP claim because the record did not show that he reported for it, and whether he should receive a credit for the probation, imposed due to a mistake by the State, had to be reconsidered.


OUTCOME: The appellate court ordered that the case be remanded to the trial court and that specified corrections to the mittimus be made.

 

1203 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


McGinley v. Madigan


No. 1-04-3517


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


366 Ill. App. 3d 974; 851 N.E.2d 709; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 437; 303 Ill. Dec. 522



June 1, 2006, Decided  
June 1, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 4, 2006.
Appeal denied by McGinley v. Madigan, 222 Ill. 2d 575, 861 N.E.2d 656, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1734, 308 Ill. Dec. 325 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03COIT7. The Honorable Raymond L. Jagielski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee executors sued appellant state and county officials in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), alleging that the Illinois Legislature did not intend for 1993 Ill. Laws 30 to apply retroactively to their estates, that retroactive application violated Illinois constitutional law, and that 1993 Ill. Laws 30 was invalid. The court entered summary judgment in favor of the executors on the issue of retroactivity. The parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the parties contested the retroactive application and constitutionality of 1993 Ill. Laws 30, which amended 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2 (2002) (amended 2004), and 1994 Ill. Laws 419, which enacted 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/3(c) (2004) during the pendency of the appeal, and whether the executors were entitled to attorney fees. The court found that the Illinois Legislature expressed its clear intent that the amendments to 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2 were to be applied retroactively to the estates of people dying on or after January 1, 2003. Further, 1994 Ill. Laws 419 was clearly enacted to deal with the constitutional problem of out-of-state taxation associated with 1993 Ill. Laws 30. Thus, the retroactive application of 1993 Ill. Laws 30 was not barred by Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, the Illinois due process clause. Furthermore, the taxing scheme set out in 1994 Ill. Laws 419 did not violate federal notions of due process under U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV. Finally, 1993 Ill. Laws 30 was not enacted in violation of the Illinois Constitution's three-readings rule under Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d). Accordingly, the executors were not entitled to attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for an accounting of the amount of refund due to one of the estates.

 

1204 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Seigles, Inc. v. City of St. Charles


No. 2-05-0547


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


365 Ill. App. 3d 431; 849 N.E.2d 456; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 431; 302 Ill. Dec. 664



May 25, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 23, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 05--CH--8. Honorable Michael J. Colwell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that declared defendant city's lumber tax ordinance unconstitutional and granted summary judgment to plaintiff lumber company. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The lumber company sold lumber and other building materials. It sold its products in two ways: (1) on-site sales generated at its retail centers, one of which was located within the city's corporate limits; and (2) off-site sales accepted at its central sales office. The lumber company and the village entered into an economic development agreement whereby the lumber company agreed to build a central sales office within the village in exchange for the village's promise to rebate to the lumber company a portion of its tax on the sales generated by the central sales office. All of the lumber company's off-site sales were accepted and processed at the village's office. The city promulgated an ordinance that would impose a tax on off-site sales of lumber accepted and processed at the village's office. After the lumber company filed a motion for summary judgment, the trial court granted that motion and declared the lumber tax unconstitutional. On appeal, the appellate court found that the ordinance operated extraterritorially because it taxed activity in the village and that the legislature had not expressly authorized such extraterritorial tax activity.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1205 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dunn


NO. 4-04-0995


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


365 Ill. App. 3d 292; 849 N.E.2d 148; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 419; 302 Ill. Dec. 533



May 22, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 16, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Dunn, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1473 (Ill., Sept. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 03CF1564. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed after the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) denied his motion to reconsider the 30-year sentence he was given after he pled guilty to one count of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child, a violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14.1(a)(1) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that he was entitled to a new sentencing hearing because the punishment applicable to predatory criminal sexual assault of a child violated the proportionate-penalties clause. He contended that the penalty for violation of § 12-14.1(a)(1) was harsher than the penalties for offenses with identical elements, namely, predatory criminal sexual assault of a child while armed with a firearm, § 12-14.1(a)(1.1) and predatory criminal sexual assault of a child involving the discharge of a firearm, § 12-14.1(a)(1.2). Examining the elements of the three crimes, the court found that the latter two crimes clearly included an element not found in § 12-14.1(a)(1), and therefore, the elements of the crimes were not identical. As a result, defendant failed to prove the punishment for predatory criminal sexual assault of a child violated the proportionate-penalties clause under the identical-elements test.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1206 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Harvey


No. 1-04-3030


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


366 Ill. App. 3d 119; 851 N.E.2d 182; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 403; 303 Ill. Dec. 284



May 17, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 28, 2006.
Appeal granted by People v. Harvey, 221 Ill. 2d 654, 857 N.E.2d 677, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1525, 306 Ill. Dec. 278 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Frank Zelezinski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), following a bench trial, was found guilty of both armed robbery/discharging a firearm and causing great bodily harm, and aggravated battery with a firearm, regarding the first victim. Defendant was also convicted of armed robbery/armed with a firearm regarding the second victim. He was then sentenced on those convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The first victim and the second victim were sitting in a car when defendant approached. Defendant pointed a gun in the second victim's face, and demanded his wallet and money. Defendant then ordered the first victim to put his money on top of the car. The first victim saw an opportunity to get away and accelerated the vehicle. As the first and second victims pulled away, defendant fired into the vehicle, and struck the first victim in the stomach. The first victim was driven to a hospital where he had to undergo surgery. Following a bench trial, defendant was found guilty of armed robbery/discharging a firearm and causing great bodily harm, as well as aggravated battery with a firearm for robbing and shooting the first victim. He was found guilty of armed robbery/armed with a firearm for shooting the second victim. He was then sentenced in each case. On appeal, the appellate court found that the two convictions regarding the first victim violated the one act, one crime rule, that his sentence for armed robbery violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois constitution, and that his sentence for armed robbery regarding the second victim was proper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court, in remanding the case, instructed the trial court to vacate defendant's sentence on his armed robbery conviction regarding the first victim and resentence him as the appellate court directed. In addition, the appellate court held that defendant's conviction for aggravated battery regarding the first victim was vacated. However, the appellate court affirmed defendant's sentence for armed robbery regarding the second victim.

 

1207 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Youngblood


No. 2-04-0987


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


365 Ill. App. 3d 210; 849 N.E.2d 423; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 410; 302 Ill. Dec. 631



May 17, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 16, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 03--CF--2687. Honorable Michael J. Burke, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of the delivery of one gram or more but less than 15 grams of a substance containing cocaine. The trial court sentenced defendant to six years' imprisonment, imposed a $ 2,000 drug assessment, and ordered defendant to submit a blood sample for deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) analysis. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) denied defendant's motion to reconsider sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/110-14 (2002), defendant was entitled to a $ 5-per-day credit toward the statutory drug assessment for the time defendant spent in custody prior to sentencing. The appellate court agreed, concluding that the $ 2,000 drug assessment, payable to the public treasury, was a fine. The appellate court noted that the assessment did not fall within the definition of a fee and more closely resembled a pecuniary punishment imposed as part of a sentence. The fact that § 110-14 allowed defendant to perform public service in lieu of monetary payment or that the payment of the assessment may be suspended if the offender entered a substance-abuse program did not detract from the punitive nature of the assessment. As for defendant's contention that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (Supp. 2003), which required defendant to submit specimens of blood, saliva, or tissue for entry into a computer database, was unconstitutional because it violated defendant's right to be free from unreasonable searches, the appellate court noted that the supreme court had already rejected such an argument.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was modified to reflect a credit of $ 1,710 against the $ 2,000 drug assessment. As modified, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1208 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Beard


No. 1-04-2157


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


366 Ill. App. 3d 197; 851 N.E.2d 141; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 389; 303 Ill. Dec. 243



May 12, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 28, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Beard, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1220 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Stanley J. Sacks, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment after it found defendant guilty on three counts of aggravated kidnapping for ransom. As a result of the conviction, defendant was required to register as a sex offender under two laws. He was also order to give a blood sample for DNA identification. Defendant appealed the ruling that he had to register as a sex offender and the order that he give a blood sample.


OVERVIEW: After a bench trial, defendant Keith Beard was convicted of three counts of aggravated kidnapping for ransom and was sentenced to 30 years in prison. As a result of his conviction for aggravated kidnapping, defendant was required to register as a sex offender pursuant to the Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/1 et seq. (2002) (Registration Act) and the Sex Offender and Child Murderer Community Notification Law, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 152/101 et seq. (2002) (Notification Act). Defendant appealed and claimed that the Registration Act and Notification Law were unconstitutional as applied to him because his crime did not have a sexual motivation or component. He also contended that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002), which requires a blood sample for persons convicted of sexual offenses or found sexually dangerous, violated his constitutional rights against unreasonable search and seizure. The appellate court affirmed. It found that neither his due process, equal protection, or privacy rights were violated by the order that he register as a sex offender. It also found that the order that he provide a blood sample was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1209 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Salinas


No. 2-04-0660


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


365 Ill. App. 3d 204; 848 N.E.2d 624; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 384; 302 Ill. Dec. 325



May 9, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 9, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 02--CF--2575. Honorable Patricia Piper Golden, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of two counts of concealment of a homicidal death. The trial court then sentenced defendant and ordered him to give a blood sample for genetic testing pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002). Defendant appealed his conviction and the order to provide the blood sample.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of two counts of concealment of a homicidal death in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3.1 (2002) based on his assistance in setting a car on fire to cover up the shooting death of two people. He was then sentenced; he was also ordered to give a blood sample for genetic marker testing pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002). On appeal, he argued that he was not convicted beyond a reasonable doubt of one of the counts of concealment, that of the first victim, because the evidence showed that the victim was still alive when the concealment occurred. He additionally argued that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002), regarding the provision of a blood sample for genetic marker testing, was unconstitutional. The appellate court agreed that evidence in the case showed that the first victim was not dead at the time the fire was set and, thus, the concealment conviction as to the first victim had to be reversed. However, the appellate court also found that the order requiring him to provide a blood sample for genetic marker testing was proper since 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of conviction was affirmed as to count 13 that charged defendant with concealing the homicide of the first victim and reversed as to count 12 that charged the defendant with concealing the homicide of the second victim. Also, the trial court's order to provide a blood sample.

 

1210 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Standley


NO. 4-03-0872


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


364 Ill. App. 3d 1008; 848 N.E.2d 195; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 359; 302 Ill. Dec. 195



May 1, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 5, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 03CF574. Honorable Katherine M. McCarthy, Judge Presiding.
People v. Standley, 359 Ill. App. 3d 1096, 835 N.E.2d 945, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 945, 296 Ill. Dec. 592 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of home invasion. Defendant appealed, and the instant court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The Supreme Court of Illinois vacated the judgment and remanded the cause to the instant court to reconsider its judgment. Accordingly, the court again addressed defendant's arguments.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court vacated and remanded the cause to reconsider the instant court's judgment in light of People v. Sharpe and People v. Guevara. Defendant first asserted the State's evidence was insufficient to prove him guilty of home invasion beyond a reasonable doubt since he presented four alibi witnesses and the State's eyewitness testimony was "suspect." The instant court found there was more than one witness who identified defendant as the perpetrator, and the Neil factors did not weigh in his favor. Since the perpetrator was in their home 20 to 25 minutes, the victims had many opportunities to view him. Defendant also argued that his 15-year sentence enhancement for home invasion while armed with a firearm was unconstitutional because it violated the proportionate-penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution (Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970)). The court disagreed. Like the defendants in Guevara, defendant argued the 15-year sentence enhancement for home invasion while armed with a firearm violated this clause under the cross-comparison analysis when compared to aggravated battery with a firearm. However, in Sharpe, the supreme court had abandoned the cross-comparison test.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1211 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Homeward Bound Servs. v. Ill. Dep't of Ins.


No. 3-04-0982


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


365 Ill. App. 3d 267; 848 N.E.2d 589; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 350; 302 Ill. Dec. 290



April 28, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 5, 2006.
Appeal denied by Homeward Bound Servs. v. Ill. Dep't of Ins., 219 Ill. 2d 565, 852 N.E.2d 239, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1061, 303 Ill. Dec. 832 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 04--MR--161. Honorable John Barra Judge, Presiding.
Homeward Bound Servs. v. Ill. Dep't of Ins., 363 Ill. App. 3d 1213, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1560 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Illinois Department of Insurance determined that appellant corporation was thus subject to the Illinois Insurance Code, 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/121 et seq. (2002), but did not have the requisite insurance certificate. The Department issued a cease and desist order. The corporation sought review. The Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County (Illinois) upheld the Department's determination. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation claimed that the Department erred because it had no administrative rule outlining a definition of insurance, and that the Department applied an improperly promulgated rule when it used the common law definition. The appellate court concluded that the common law was an acceptable means of providing the definition. The appellate court also concluded that, contrary to the corporation's contention, the Illinois Insurance Code was not void for vagueness because it gave an ordinary person no notice of what conduct was forbidden. Next, the appellate court concluded that the Department did not err in concluding that the corporation's activities constituted insurance business, subjecting it to the requirements of the Code. The corporation's Assisted Living Service Agreement clearly satisfied the first three elements of the definition of insurance in that it had a specified ending date, each customer paid a specified amount under the contract, and each customer acquired an interest in the care prescribed in the contract. As for the assumption of risk element, the appellate court found that the risk was shifted in a contingent manner, which was the essence of insurance.


OUTCOME: The Department's decision was affirmed.

 

1212 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lee


No. 1-04-2258


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 339



April 27, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by People v. Lee, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 810 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 17, 2007)
Substituted opinion at, Remanded by People v. Lee, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 963 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Aug. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honable Kenneth J. Wadas, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after it found defendant guilty of one count of armed robbery and three counts of aggravated unlawful restraint. The trial court then sentenced him to concurrent prison terms of 19 years for armed robbery and 10 years for each conviction of aggravated unlawful restraint. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly accosted a man, his wife, and their 11-year-old son and demanded that the man give him money lest the man be shot. The man gave defendant money. Defendant fled. Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of armed robbery and three counts of aggravated unlawful restraint. He was then sentenced to concurrent prison terms of 19 years for armed robbery and 10 years for each aggravated unlawful restraint conviction. On appeal, he contended that the State failed to prove him guilty of armed robbery and that his convictions for aggravated unlawful restraint violated the one-act, one-crime doctrine. He also contended that the armed robbery statute under which he was convicted was void because its penalty provision violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution. The appellate court found that the armed robbery conviction was sufficiently supported. However, it found that one of the unlawful restraint convictions had to be vacated since it involved the same conduct as the armed robbery of the man, that the proportionate penalties clause had not been violated, and that a 15-year enhancement had to be imposed on his armed robbery sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the defendant's convictions for armed robbery and for two of the three convictions for aggravated unlawful restraint. It vacated the third conviction for aggravated unlawful restraint, vacated his sentence for armed robbery, and remanded his case to the trial court for resentencing on the armed robbery conviction.

 

1213 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Murray


NO. 4-03-0632


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


364 Ill. App. 3d 999; 848 N.E.2d 160; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 348; 302 Ill. Dec. 160



April 25, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 23, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Murray, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1407 (Ill., Sept. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County No. 02CF385. Honorable Elizabeth A. Robb, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed after he was convicted in the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) on a charge of home invasion. He asserted that the trial court misstated the law when answering a question by the jury during deliberations. He also asserted a claim that his enhanced sentence under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(c) (2002) was unconstitutionally disproportionate to the penalty for another crime with identical elements.


OVERVIEW: Defendant left the victim's home after an argument about a drug transaction. He later returned and entered the home. The victim was shot during a further altercation. The court reversed. The jury instruction on home invasion indicated that defendant's entry into the victim's home was "without authority" if, at the time of entry, defendant had an intent to commit a criminal act within the home. But, if defendant entered the home without criminal intent, his entry was "with authority" regardless of what happened afterward. The jury's question was whether the "criminal act" that would destroy the authority to enter could include a drug deal. The trial court's response was that the instruction did not limit the type of crime. Because the victim was willing to let defendant into the home to complete the drug deal, the trial court's response resulted in conflicting instructions on whether defendant's entry was "with" or "without" authority. The response at least implied that defendant's intent to engage in the drug deal with the victim made his entry into the home "without authority." But the victim had specifically authorized defendant to enter so that the drug deal could be completed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial. Because it resolved the appeal on the instruction issue, it did not reach the constitutional issue.

 

1214 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lambert


No. 2-03-0808


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


364 Ill. App. 3d 488; 847 N.E.2d 136; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 284; 301 Ill. Dec. 477



April 10, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 12, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Lambert, 221 Ill. 2d 657, 857 N.E.2d 679, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1385, 306 Ill. Dec. 280 (2006)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Lambert, 2017 IL App (2d) 140425-U, 2017 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 371 (2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 94--CF--148. Honorable Gerald F. Grubb, Judge Presiding.
People v. Lambert, 322 Ill. App. 3d 1051, 798 N.E.2d 427, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1328, 278 Ill. Dec. 325 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which denied defendant's motion to reconsider the 60-year sentence imposed on defendant for first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he should receive a new hearing on the motion because he had not been properly admonished under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 605(a) and that he was denied the right to be present at the hearing on the motion to reconsider. Defendant, who acted pro se at the sentencing hearing and in filing the motion, failed to appear at the hearing. The trial court denied the motion without further input from the State or defendant. The court affirmed. Defendant was deprived of his right to be present when the trial court ruled on his motion in open court, however, the error was harmless. Defendant had not attempted to show how his presence at the hearing would have improved his chances of persuading the trial court that his motion was meritorious. Further, defendant's right to present oral argument was extremely limited and did not extend to the motion for reconsideration. Additionally, although defendant was not properly admonished under Rule 605, he actually did file a post-sentencing motion. Moreover, he had not suggested any additional issues that he would have raised in the motion had he received proper admonishments. Thus, defendant suffered no prejudice.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed.

 

1215 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Webb v. White


NO. 4-05-0237


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


364 Ill. App. 3d 650; 850 N.E.2d 233; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 413; 302 Ill. Dec. 796



April 7, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 19, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 04MR378. Honorable Leo J. Zappa, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After plaintiff licensee's driver's license was suspended for 12 months pursuant to 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-206(a)(38) (2002), she filed an action against defendant Illinois Secretary of State in which she sought administrative review of the Secretary's decision denying her petition for rescission or modification of the suspension. The Sangamon County Circuit Court (Illinois) affirmed the Secretary's decision. The licensee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The licensee, who was 20 at the time, went to an establishment to dance. After dancing, she took two or three gulps of a friend's drink and then realized that it was mixed with alcohol. About 30 minutes later, police "raided" the establishment to catch underage drinkers. The licensee registered a 0.005 blood-alcohol concentration and was charged with violating a municipal code prohibiting the purchase or possession of alcohol by persons under 21. She pleaded guilty, and her license was suspended. After the licensee paid her fine and court costs, her case was dismissed. The court held that the Secretary abused his administrative discretion in not rescinding or substantially modifying the suspension. Ill. Admin. Code tit. 92, § 1001.460(d) allowed the period of a discretionary suspension to be reduced for good cause shown. Here, the licensee had no prior revocations or suspensions and had voluntarily submitted to testing. Furthermore, the penalty imposed on the licensee was harsher than she would have received under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-208.2(a) (2002) had she violated the zero-tolerance statute, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501.8 (2002), by drinking and driving.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment.

People v. McNeal


No. 1-04-2047


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


364 Ill. App. 3d 867; 847 N.E.2d 842; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 247; 301 Ill. Dec. 832



March 31, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 24, 2006.
Vacated by People v. McNeal, 223 Ill. 2d 662, 863 N.E.2d 263, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 457, 309 Ill. Dec. 33 (2007)
Substituted opinion at, Decision reached on appeal by People v. McNeal, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 3495 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., May 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 CR 16996. Honorable Victoria A. Stewart, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) judgment convicting him of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. He was ordered to pay a $ 1,000 drug assessment under § 411.2(a)(3) (720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/411.2(a)(3) (2002)) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act and $ 5 toward the Spinal Cord Injury Paralysis Cure Research Trust Fund pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-9-1.1(c) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed his confrontation rights were violated because the record lacked any indication that his attorney informed him of the legal consequences of entering a stipulation as to the composition of the recovered substances and as to the chain of custody. However, defendant did not object to the stipulation as to the chain of custody and chemical composition of the recovered items. The decision to stipulate to a forensic chemist's testimony was a matter of trial strategy. In accordance with People v. Fort, defendant's $ 1,000 drug assessment pursuant to § 411.2(a)(3) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/411.2(a)(3) (2002), was a fine for which he was entitled to $ 5-per-day credit for the three days he was incarcerated pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/110-14 (2002). Defendant's due process rights were violated when the trial court ordered him to pay the $ 5 fee for the Fund pursuant to § 5-9-1.1 of the Unified Code of Corrections, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-9-1.1 (2002); the relationship between his crime of possession of a controlled substance and the Fund was too attenuated to survive his due process challenge.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed but the costs and fees order was amended to reflect a credit of $ 15 against the $ 1,000 "Assessment Controlled Substance," and the $ 5 fee for the "Trauma Fund Spinal Cord" was stricken from the order.

Brown v. Jaimovich


No. 1-05-0146


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


365 Ill. App. 3d 329; 847 N.E.2d 870; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 253; 301 Ill. Dec. 860



March 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 24, 2006.
Appeal denied by Brown v. Javeed Akhter, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1296 (Ill., Sept. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Michael J. Hogan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a doctor and health care entities, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which converted them from respondents in discovery (RIDs) to defendants under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-402 (2004) in a medical malpractice action by plaintiff mother, individually, and plaintiff father, individually and as administrator of his deceased son's estate. The trial court certified a question to the court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' eight-year-old son died as a result of the alleged negligence of various health care entities and individuals. Plaintiffs filed suit against multiple parties as RIDs. Prior to the expiration of the six-month conversion window of § 2-402, plaintiffs' motions to extend the time for discovery and for conversion of RIDs were granted. Thereafter, the Robinson case was decided and several RIDs sought termination of their RID status. Plaintiffs moved to convert certain RIDs to defendants. The trial court granted plaintiffs' request and denied the RIDs' motions, as well as their motion for reconsideration, although the conversion occurred nine months after the Robinson modified decision. However, the trial court certified a question for appeal on the applicability of extending the conversion period. On appeal, the court interpreted the key phrases of the Robinson modified decision. It found that the case was filed prior to the date range of prospective application, and as defendants were named as RIDs prior to that date, the six-month period did not commence after the Robinson decision. The extension and conversion practice in place prior to Robinson was applicable.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question by holding that the trial court had discretion to extend the six-month statutory window for conversion of RIDs to defendants after the initial statutory window had expired. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Moore


No. 1-05-0948


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


365 Ill. App. 3d 53; 847 N.E.2d 829; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 257; 301 Ill. Dec. 819



March 31, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 24, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Moore, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1197 (Ill., Sept. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 CR 15878. Honorable Victoria A. Stewart, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; mittimus modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a joint bench trial, both defendant and co-defendant were acquitted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver within 1,000 feet of a park but found guilty of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to six years' imprisonment in the Department of Corrections. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the evidence established that defendant had constructive possession of the cocaine. The evidence showed that defendant intended to aid co-defendant in the sale and delivery of cocaine. Co-defendant would engage in a conversation with a buyer and then direct the buyer across the street to give defendant the money. Co-defendant would then retrieve an item for a leaf pile and hand the item to the buyer. Defendant also contended that his Sixth Amendment right to confrontation was violated by counsel's stipulation to the chain of custody and to the chemical composition of the recovered substance. The appellate court disagreed because the stipulation was not tantamount to a guilty plea and defendant was present in the courtroom at the time of the stipulation and failed to raise an objection. Finally, defendant contended that his Class X sentence was unconstitutional and violated Apprendi. The appellate court found no error, noting that the record was sufficient to establish defendant's eligibility for Class X sentencing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed, and it was ordered that the mittimus be modified to reflect the offense of which defendant was convicted.

 

1219 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Phillip C. (In re Phillip C.)


1-04-1109


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


364 Ill. App. 3d 822; 847 N.E.2d 801; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 254; 301 Ill. Dec. 791



March 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 24, 2006.
Appeal denied by In re Phillip C., 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1228 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Terrence V. Sharkey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile was convicted of the aggravated kidnapping of a minor. The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, imposed an indeterminate juvenile sentence and a 20-year adult sentence under the Illinois Extended Juvenile Jurisdiction Prosecutions Act, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5-810 (2002), and required him to register as a sex offender under the Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, 16, car-jacked a 17-year-old at knife-point and took his wallet. He argued that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/2(B)(1.5) of the Registration Act was unconstitutional as applied to him. He claimed that as there was no evidence he had a sexual motive for the kidnapping, requiring him to register as a sex offender violated his rights to privacy and to substantive and procedural due process under the state and U.S. Constitutions. The appellate court disagreed. The state supreme court had held that the Registration Act did not implicate the right to privacy under either Constitution. As to substantive due process, the legislature could have rationally concluded that kidnappers of children posed such a threat to sexually assault those children as to warrant their inclusion in the sex offender registry. His procedural due process rights were not violated, since he was able to contest the kidnapping charges at trial. The 20-year adult sentence, which would be executed only if he violated the conditions of his juvenile sentence, was not excessive in light of his prior criminal history, including the fact that he was on probation for robbery when he committed the crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Writ of habeas corpus denied Ligon v. Jones, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 59678 (N.D. Ill., Aug. 14, 2007)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Ligon, 392 Ill. App. 3d 988, 910 N.E.2d 1252, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 531, 331 Ill. Dec. 496 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by People v. Ligon, 2014 IL App (1st) 120913, 2014 Ill. App. LEXIS 426 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01CR2559. The Honorable Henry R. Simmons, Jr., Judge Presiding.
People v. Ligon, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 440 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Mar. 24, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of aggravated vehicular hijacking, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-4(a)(3) (2000). The trial court sentenced defendant to natural life in prison, pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33B-1 (2002), because of defendant's criminal record. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim identified defendant as the person who stole the victim's truck through the use of a gun. Defendant was later found in possession of the truck. The victim identified a BB gun found in the truck as the weapon defendant used. On appeal, the court found that (1) the evidence was sufficient because the jury's finding that the BB gun could have been used as a dangerous weapon was not erroneous; (2) defendant's contention that his conviction required reversal as the proof at trial showed that he was armed with a firearm while the indictment alleged that he was armed with a bludgeon was without merit; (3) defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel failed as counsel's decision not to present a witness was a matter of sound trial strategy; (4) defendant's contention that he was denied a fair trial by the cumulative effect of the prosecutor's comments was without merit as none of the prosecutor's closing comments were erroneous; and (5) defendant's enhanced sentence under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33B-1 was constitutional as the timing and sequence of defendant's prior convictions were inherent in the convictions themselves and did not need to be submitted to a jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Barnes


No. 1-03-2334


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


364 Ill. App. 3d 888; 847 N.E.2d 679; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 218; 301 Ill. Dec. 669



March 24, 2006, Decided  
March 24, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 24, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 31619. The Honorable Catherine M. Haberkorn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial, defendant was convicted of attempted murder, two counts of aggravated battery with a firearm, and two counts of unlawful use of a weapon by a felon. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to 17 years' imprisonment for the attempted murder conviction, plus concurrent terms of 6 years' imprisonment for each of the battery counts and 5 years' imprisonment for each weapons count. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was not proved guilty of the charged offenses beyond a reasonable doubt because the identification testimony against him was insufficient. The appellate court concluded that none of the claimed identification shortcomings, such as the fact that the gunman wore a hood or the fact that the incident happened quickly, rendered the testimony against defendant sufficiently unreliable that his convictions must be disturbed. Among other things, the appellate court noted that the witness' identification of defendant was consistent and that the identification was bolstered by the fact that the witness had encountered defendant on multiple occasions prior to the night of the shooting. The appellate court also concluded that the evidence was sufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had an intent to kill, as he filed several shots at the victims. Next, the appellate court conclude that defendant's sentence was not an impermissible violation of the prohibition against sentence increases. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the trial court should have inquired further into defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed. The case was remanded for further proceedings on defendant's ineffective assistance claim.

People v. Andrews


No. 2-03-0959


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


364 Ill. App. 3d 253; 845 N.E.2d 974; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 228; 301 Ill. Dec. 109



March 24, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 21, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 02--CF--2360. Honorable Timothy Q. Sheldon, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Andrews, 358 Ill. App. 3d 744, 831 N.E.2d 66, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 617, 294 Ill. Dec. 543 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty in a second trial of aggravated vehicular hijacking while carrying a firearm in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-4(a)(4) (2002). The trial court then sentenced him to 14 years in prison. Defendant's first trial had ended in a mistrial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A woman and her passenger drove the pickup of the woman's mother to a store. Just then, a black man with a goatee approached. He pulled out a gun, told them he was going to take the pickup, let them get out, jumped in, and drove away. The woman later identified defendant in a photo array. Defendant's first jury trial ended when the trial court declared a mistrial after it was informed that the jury had deadlocked at 7 to 5. In defendant's second jury trial, the trial court instructed the jury on the charged offense of aggravated vehicular hijacking while carrying a firearm, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-4(a)(4) (2002), and on the lesser-included offense of vehicular hijacking, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-3(a) (2002). The jury found defendant guilty of the aggravated vehicular hijacking charge. It then sentenced defendant. On appeal, the appellate court found that the second jury trial did not violate defendant's double jeopardy rights, that his sentence violated the proportionate penalties clause and rendered 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-4(a)(4) (2002) void ab initio, and that a conviction of vehicular hijacking, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-3(a) (2002), was proper.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of conviction entered for aggravated vehicular hijacking was reversed and the sentence imposed thereon, 14 years in prison, was vacated. Also, the appellate court ordered that judgment be entered on a conviction of vehicular hijacking and the cause was remanded to the trial court to have defendant resentenced based on that conviction.

People v. Boyd


No. 2-03-1358


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


363 Ill. App. 3d 1027; 845 N.E.2d 921; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 199; 301 Ill. Dec. 56



March 16, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 14, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Boyd, 221 Ill. 2d 646, 857 N.E.2d 675, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1186, 306 Ill. Dec. 276 (2006)
Subsequent appeal at, Petition denied by People v. Boyd, 233 Ill. 2d 568, 919 N.E.2d 356, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1352, 335 Ill. Dec. 637 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 03--CF--890. Honorable Robert J. Anderson, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Boyd, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 22 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Jan. 20, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of one count of aggravated battery, one count of aggravated battery with a firearm, and four counts of home invasion and acquitted defendant of two counts of armed robbery. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) merged the charges into two counts of home invasion and imposed concurrent terms of 55 and 45 years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was initially charged with all but two counts of home invasion. The two additional counts were not added until 116 days after the original charges were filed. On appeal, defendant argued that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to invoke his speedy-trial rights. The appellate court held that the State was responsible for the 116-day delay in filing the additional home invasion charges and that defendant was not responsible for any subsequent delay that defense counsel agreed to before the filing of the new charges and that did not actually delay the scheduled trial date. The appellate court concluded that the speedy-trial period expired three days after the new charges were filed, at which time counsel should have requested a speedy-trial discharge; counsel's failure could not be justified as a matter of trial strategy. Next, the appellate court concluded that any error in the trial court's jury instructions regarding identification testimony was not serious in light of the overwhelming evidence against defendant. Finally, the appellate court concluded that defendant was not entitled to a new trial, but merely a new sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions of and sentences for the two home invasion counts were reversed on speedy-trial grounds. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed, and the cause was remanded for the trial court to sentence defendant on the jury's guilty verdicts on aggravated battery and aggravated battery with a firearm.

Yakubinis v. Yamaha Motor Corp., U.S.A.


No. 1-05-1752 & 1-05-1772, Consol.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


365 Ill. App. 3d 128; 847 N.E.2d 552; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 185; 301 Ill. Dec. 542



March 16, 2006, Decided  
March 16, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 24, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Yakubinis v. State Motor Vehicle Review Bd., 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 438 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Apr. 13, 2006)
Appeal denied by Yakubinis v. Yamaha Motor Corp., U.S.A., 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1360 (Ill., Sept. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 04L50209. The Honorable Nancy J. Arnold, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, State of Illinois Motor Vehicle Review Board and a vehicle manufacturer, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which reversed the Board's dismissal of a protest filed by plaintiff dealership franchisee and remanded the protest to the Board for a hearing on the merits. The protest was filed under the Illinois Motor Vehicle Franchise Act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 710/4(e)(8), 12(c) (2002).


OVERVIEW: The statutory sections provided that a franchisor violated the Act if it relocated a dealership into the relevant market area of an existing franchisee without good cause and placed the good cause determination with the Board. The instant versions of the sections became effective in 1995. The court reversed. Prior versions of the statutory sections had been found unconstitutional and were void ab initio. There was no public policy basis for departing from the void ab initio doctrine to apply the earlier versions to plaintiff's 1989 franchise agreement. Thus, under plaintiff's agreement the manufacturer was not statutorily prohibited from relocating dealerships into plaintiff's relevant market area. Sections §§ 4(e)(8) and 12(c) of the Act created a substantive right to challenge relocations. They could not be applied retroactively. Plaintiff had no common law right to protest dealer relocations on a good cause basis. Plaintiff had no third-party beneficiary rights under the manufacturer's contract with the relocated franchisee. Finally, applying the statutory sections to post-1995 franchise agreements but not to pre-1995 agreements did not violate equal protection concepts.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed.

People v. Gray


NO. 4-05-0470


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


363 Ill. App. 3d 897; 845 N.E.2d 113; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 195; 300 Ill. Dec. 692



March 14, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 13, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 02CF1051. Honorable Jeffrey B. Ford, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which resentenced him to an extended-term of seven and a half years in prison on his admission to violating probation that was imposed on a guilty plea to aggravated battery. The extended term was imposed after a prior three-year sentence, which was ordered by a different judge, was vacated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant received probation on a guilty plea to aggravated battery. He later admitted to a revocation petition (RP) before a judge who set a resentencing date. Before that date, a different judge, while sentencing defendant on two other matters, resentenced him on the RP to three years in prison. The judge who originally heard the RP vacated that sentence and resentenced defendant. On appeal, defendant argued it was improper to vacate the three-year sentence as it was imposed by a judge with jurisdiction. The State responded that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-1(b) (2004) mandated that the judge who accepted the plea on the RP had to impose a sentence. The court found that, if § 5-4-1(b) was mandatory rather than directory, it would encroach on a constitutionally authorized court rule at Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 21(b) conferring power to the circuit's chief judge to assign judges and would thereby violate the separation of powers under Ill. Const. art. II, § 1. Allowing the first judge to increase the three year sentence would violate the prohibition against increasing a lawfully imposed sentence under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(c) (2004).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded with directions to reinstate the three-year sentence.

Eagle Marine Indus. v. Union Pac. R.R.


NO. 5-05-0038


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


363 Ill. App. 3d 1166; 845 N.E.2d 869; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 171; 301 Ill. Dec. 4



March 9, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Eagle Marine Indus. v. Union Pac. R.R., 221 Ill. 2d 634, 857 N.E.2d 670, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1191, 306 Ill. Dec. 271 (2006)
Reversed by, Cause remanded by Eagle Marine Indus. v. Union Pac. R.R., 2008 Ill. LEXIS 2 (Ill., Jan. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 03-CH-1040. Honorable Richard A. Aguirre, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee business operators filed suit in the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), to enjoin appellant railroad from stopping its trains at a crossing and thereby obstructing a public road for more than 10 minutes in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18c-7402(1)(b) (2002). The circuit court granted a permanent injunction that prevented the railroad from obstructing the crossing for greater than 10 minutes. The railroad appealed.


OVERVIEW: The business operators alleged that the railroad crossed a public road which was the only means to get to and from the operators' business facilities, that the railroad's trains often blocked the public road to motor vehicles for 15 to 45 minutes at a time, that the repeated obstruction of the public road deprived the operators of the right to use their properties and compromised public health and safety, and that the operators had sustained irreparable harm and had no adequate remedy at law. The railroad claimed that the operators did not have a private right of action under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18c-7402(1)(b) and that the action was preempted by the Federal Railroad Safety Authorization Act of 1994, 49 U.S.C.S. §§ 20101 - 20153 (2000); the ICC Termination Act of 1995, 49 U.S.C.S. §§ 10101 - 16106 (2000); and the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. On appeal, the court found that the operators had an implied private right of action under § 18c-7402(1)(b), that the operators' action was not preempted by federal law, and that there was sufficient testimonial evidence to satisfy the requirements for a permanent injunction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Hauschild


No. 2-03-0857


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


364 Ill. App. 3d 202; 845 N.E.2d 74; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 176; 300 Ill. Dec. 653



March 8, 2006, Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of home invasion, attempted first-degree murder, armed robbery, and criminal damage to property. The trial court then sentenced defendant on each of those offenses. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of attempted first-degree murder, home invasion, armed robbery, and criminal damage to property. The trial court then sentenced defendant to consecutive sentences of 35 years' imprisonment for home invasion, 18 years' imprisonment for attempted first-degree murder, and 12 years' imprisonment for armed robbery. In addition, the trial court imposed a concurrent term of two years' imprisonment for criminal damage to property. Defendant appealed, and challenged his convictions of home invasion, armed robbery, and criminal damage to property. The appellate court found that due to the recent Sharpe decision, defendant's sentences for armed robbery and attempted first-degree murder had to be vacated, and a remand was required for resentencing on those offenses. However, the appellate court found that lla of the convictions had to be affirmed and all of the remainder of defendant's sentences were proper.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments of conviction on home invasion, attempted first-degree murder, armed robbery, and criminal damage to property were affirmed. Defendant's sentences for armed robbery and attempted first-degree murder were vacated, and the cause was remanded to the trial court for resentencing on those offenses. The remainder of defendant's sentences were affirmed.

 

1229 of 2788 DOCUMENTS



Turner v. Firstar Bank, N.A.


NO. 5-04-0548


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


363 Ill. App. 3d 1150; 845 N.E.2d 816; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 142; 300 Ill. Dec. 927



March 6, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 02-L-357. Honorable Ralph J. Mendelsohn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant note holder appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) awarding plaintiff borrower $ 500,000 in punitive damages in the borrower's action against the note holder alleging conversion.


OVERVIEW: The borrower sued the note holder for conversion after the note holder caused the borrower's car to be repossessed after the borrower had paid the car loan in full. The note holder was unresponsive to the borrower's attempts to seek the return of items stolen from her car during the repossession. The trial court awarded $ 25,000 in compensatory damages. The $ 500,000 punitive damages award was excessive and violated due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. With regard to the reprehensibility of the note holder's conduct, the harm was economic rather than physical. There was no evidence that the note holder was aware of the borrower's financial vulnerability. The borrower presented evidence that the note holder had committed wrongful repossessions more than one time, but there was no specific evidence as to how many times. There was no evidence of intentional malice, trickery, or deceit. The punitive damages award was 20 times larger than the amount of compensatory damages. A punitive damages award of $ 225,000 was constitutional, as the award would have been less than the double-digit ratio between punitive and compensatory damages against which case law had cautioned.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as modified. The case was remanded for a remittitur to reduce to the judgment to $ 225,000, unless the borrower did not consent, in which case there was to be a new trial on the issue of the amount of punitive damages.

Arnett v. Markel


NO. 5-04-0082


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


363 Ill. App. 3d 1136; 845 N.E.2d 752; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 145; 300 Ill. Dec. 863



March 2, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Alexander County. No. 02-MR-35. Honorable Stephen L. Spomer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; judgment entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Alexander County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that denied plaintiff prisoner's motion to disqualify the Attorney General's office from representing defendant government representatives. It also held that they did not violate his First Amendment right to freedom of speech by refusing to allow him to mail an internal investigative report out of the prison where he was confined. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner and two other inmates tried to escape from a prison operated by the State. An internal investigations department prepared a report. The report included several escape details. He was criminally charged. He made the prison officials aware that he had a copy of the report, which had been included in the criminal case file. The prisoner pled guilty. The prisoner then tried to mail the report to a community activist. Defendant captain and defendant warden refused to allow him to do so. The prisoner filed a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action and claimed that the refusal violated his First Amendment rights. The Attorney General's office represented the government representatives. The prisoner's attorney moved to disqualify the Attorney General's office, but the motion was denied. The trial court granted summary judgment to all of the government representatives, including the captain and warden. On appeal, the appellate court affirmed the denial of the motion to disqualify, but agreed with the prisoner as to the captain and warden that the refusal to allow him to mail the report, under circumstances where the report was part of a public record, violated his First Amendment rights.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment denying the prisoner's motion to disqualify the Attorney General's office from representing the government representatives was affirmed. Its judgment granting summary judgment to them on his First Amendment claim seeking damages was also affirmed. However, the summary judgment grant to the captain and warden regarding the prisoner's right to mail the report was reversed.

People v. Hampton


No.1-03-0067


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


363 Ill. App. 3d 293; 842 N.E.2d 1124; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 131; 299 Ill. Dec. 772



February 27, 2006, Decided  
February 27, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 3, 2006.
Appeal granted by People v. Hampton, 219 Ill. 2d 578, 852 N.E.2d 243, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 633, 303 Ill. Dec. 836 (2006)
Vacated by, in part, Cause remanded by People v. Hampton, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 451 (Ill., Apr. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 16875. Honorable Preston L. Bowie, Judge Presiding.
People v. Hampton, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1188 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 5, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of eight counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault and two counts of home invasion with a firearm.


OVERVIEW: During a home invasion, a gun was used, and a victim was sexually assaulted. Defendant was convicted of various crimes, and he sought review. On appeal, the reviewing court determined that it was unclear whether or not defendant waived his rights under the Confrontation Clause. An evidentiary hearing was required to determine if defendant had forfeited the privilege to confront a witness because he wrongfully procured his silence by writing a letter regarding his testimony. Next, the reviewing court held that the sentence did not violate the prohibition against double enhancement. The firearm factor under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-14(a) (2002) was used only once, which was to enhance defendant's sentence. However, the 15-year mandatory add-on provision under § 12-14(d) violated Ill Const. art. I, § 11 because aggravated criminal sexual assault was punishable more severely than the identical offense of armed violence predicated on a sexual assault. Finally, a similar challenge to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-11(a)(3) (2002) was rejected because the cross-comparison test under Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 was no longer used, and no other viable ground was asserted.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were vacated and remanded with instructions to determine whether defendant waived his rights under the Confrontation Clause. If he did waive the rights, the trial court was directed to reinstate convictions for four sexual assaults and one home invasion. Resentencing was required on the sexual assaults only. If defendant did not waive his constitutional rights, a new trial was required.

People v. Brown


No. 1-02-3276


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT


363 Ill. App. 3d 838; 842 N.E.2d 1141; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 87; 299 Ill. Dec. 789



February 16, 2006, Decided  
February 16, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 3, 2006. As Modified upon Denial of Rehearing and as Corrected March 17, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94 CR 4624. Honorable Reginald Baker, Judge Presiding.
People v. Brown, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1254 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 15, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of murder, attempted murder, two counts of armed robbery, and attempted armed robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was allegedly involved with two codefendants in the attempted robbery of a grocery store. Multiple charges resulted including a murder charge because one person was shot to death during the attempted robbery. Each of the codefendants was tried in a separate trial regarding the attempted robbery. Defendant was then tried. The trial court, pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. On appeal, the appellate court found that while 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Watson v. Waste Mgmt. of Ill., Inc.

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


363 Ill. App. 3d 1101; 845 N.E.2d 730; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 55; 300 Ill. Dec. 841



February 3, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Rehearing denied by Watson v. Waste Mgmt. of Ill., Inc., 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 325 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., Apr. 7, 2006)
Appeal denied by Watson v. Waste Mgmt. of Ill., Inc., 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1245 (Ill., Sept. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois, No. 03-CH-277. Honorable J. Scott Swaim, Judge Presiding.
Karlock v. Waste Mgmt., 361 Ill. App. 3d 992, 839 N.E.2d 128, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1120, 298 Ill. Dec. 141 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois, that dismissed his injunction and declaratory judgment action against defendants, a county board and a sanitation company, pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-615 (2002) on the sole basis that he was required to bring his action in quo warranto under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-101 (2002).


OVERVIEW: The citizen alleged that the county board adopted an ordinance that changed the method of electing its members and that the board failed to hold a referendum to approve the change in method of electing board members as required by Ill. Const. art. VII, § 3(b). The appellate court held that because the citizen's complaint challenged the validity of the board's authority to act, a proceeding in quo warranto was an appropriate and adequate remedy. Because neither 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-101 (2002) nor case law expressly made quo warranto an exclusive remedy, the trial court erred in dismissing the citizen's complaint on that basis under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-615 (2002).


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Johnson

CASE SUMMARY:

OVERVIEW: Following the trial court's Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 605(b) admonishments, defense counsel indicated that defendant wanted to file a motion for reconsideration of sentence and to correct a void sentence. The motion was denied. On appeal, defendant argued that remand was necessary because defense counsel failed to file an Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d) certificate. The State argued that no Ill. Sup. Ct. OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the appellate court's opinion.

People v. Hofer


NO. 5-05-0332


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


363 Ill. App. 3d 719; 843 N.E.2d 460; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 43; 300 Ill. Dec. 202



January 31, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Bond County. No. 05-MR-11. Honorable John Knight, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant village trustee challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Bond County (Illinois), which, following a hearing on appellee State's quo warranto complaint, ordered him removed from office and barred from assuming the office of board of trustees president because, as a convicted felon, he was ineligible for an elective municipal office under § 3.1-10-5(b) of the Illinois Municipal Code, 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3.1-10-5(b) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Following a hearing on a quo warranto complaint, the circuit court ordered the trustee removed from office and barred from proceeding to the office of president of the village's board of trustees. On appeal the trustee argued 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3.1-10-5(b) (2002) violated equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV because the statutory scheme allowed a convicted felon to run for a constitutional office after completion of the sentence, but it did not restore the same rights to a felon seeking a nonconstitutional elective office. The court found there was a rational basis for the distinction that was related to the legitimate state interest in maintaining the public trust in local elective offices, which had much more freedom over fiscal decisions and were subject to less oversight than constitutional office holders. Requiring a pardon by the governor under Ill. Const. art. V, § 12, before a felon could have the right to seek elective office restored was a legitimate way to meet that goal. Since a rational basis existed for the legislature's distinction between qualifications for office holders, there was no equal protection violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

People v. Adams


No. 1-04-2680


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


363 Ill. App. 3d 34; 842 N.E.2d 1187; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 26; 299 Ill. Dec. 835



January 24, 2006, Decided  
January 24, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 3, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Adams, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 897 (Ill., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable James D. Egan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of involuntary manslaughter, usually considered a Class 3 felony. Because the victim was defendant's son, the offense was elevated to a Class 2 felony. 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3(f) (2000). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to 12 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3(a) (2000) was unconstitutional because it violated his right to due process. Defendant contended that the statute bore no rational relationship to the legislature's stated purpose, to fight and deter domestic violence. Defendant alleged that § 9-3(f) was not reasonably designed to implement the legislature's purpose because involuntary manslaughter is an unintentional act, and an unintentional act could not be deterred by an enhanced penalty. The appellate court concluded that § 9-3(f) was constitutional. The appellate court concluded that the plain language of § 9-3(f) made it clear that the legislature intended the penalty for involuntary manslaughter to be more severe under certain circumstances. The appellate court saw no reason why the legislature could not have created an additional offense of involuntary manslaughter against a family or household member, imposing a Class 2 penalty. The appellate court also found no merit in defendant's challenge to the compulsory extraction and perpetual storage of his DNA, as such had previously been held constitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction, sentence, and entry of the DNA order were affirmed. The costs and fees order was amended to reflect a credit of $ 5,000 against defendant's $ 5,000 fine, and the mittimus was amended to reflect a 1,226-day sentencing credit.

People v. Boyd

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 22



January 20, 2006, Filed
