 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, Opinion withdrawn by People v. Boyd, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 225 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Mar. 16, 2006)
Substituted opinion at People v. Boyd, 363 Ill. App. 3d 1027, 845 N.E.2d 921, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 199, 301 Ill. Dec. 56 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Mar. 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 03--CF--890. Honorable Robert J. Anderson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The DuPage County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of one count of aggravated battery, one count of aggravated battery with a firearm, and four counts of home invasion. The trial court merged the charges into two counts of home invasion and then sentenced defendant. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Two men broke into the home of the victims one morning. One of the men repeatedly pistol-whipped the victims also shot one of the victims twice. A jury found defendant guilty of aggravated battery, aggravated battery with a firearm, and four counts of home invasion. The trial court merged the charges into two counts of home invasion and imposed sentences accordingly. On appeal, defendant argued that the State's delayed filing of the home invasion charges violated his speedy-trial rights and, thus, his trial attorney was ineffective for failing to move for their dismissal, that the trial court erred in instructing the jury regarding eyewitness identification testimony, and that the two convictions of home invasion violated the one-act, one crime principle. The State conceded the one-act, one-crime violation. The appellate court then found that the State's delayed filing of the home invasion charge violated his speedy-trial right and, thus, his counsel was ineffective for not seeking dismissal of those charges. It also found that defendant waived the jury instruction issue by not objecting at trial and that the plain-error doctrine did not entitle him to relief.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed defendant's two convictions of and sentences for the home invasion counts on speedy trial counts. It then affirmed the remainder of the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court to sentence defendant on the jury's guilty verdicts on aggravated battery and aggravated battery with a firearm.

United Disposal of Bradley, Inc. v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 3-04-0536


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


363 Ill. App. 3d 243; 842 N.E.2d 1161; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 8; 299 Ill. Dec. 809



January 13, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 22, 2006.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by United Disposal of Bradley, Inc. v. Ill. Pollution Control Bd., 549 U.S. 955, 127 S. Ct. 407, 166 L. Ed. 2d 273, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 7550 (2006)
Related proceeding at Liberty Disposal, Inc. v. Scott, 648 F. Supp. 2d 1047, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 76486 (N.D. Ill., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Review of Order of the Illinois Pollution Control Board dated June 17, 2004. No. PCB 03--235. Appeal from a Decision of the Illinois Pollution Control Board.



DISPOSITION: Confirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought to have a geographical limitation removed from its development permit for a local waste transfer station. Appellee agency denied the application. On review, appellee Illinois Pollution Control Board granted summary judgment in favor of the agency. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation filed a document with the agency which the corporation called an application for modification of its operating permit. The appellate court found that, in reality, the corporation was trying to transform its "local" pollution control facility into a "regional" pollution control facility. The application was correctly denied by the agency and board as an attempt to operate a regional pollution control facility without first obtaining the necessary siting approval. The corporation challenged the limitations contained within a special condition of its permit, which it requested and failed to object to for approximately 10 years. The slight burden the permit imposed on interstate commerce did not outweigh the benefits that the permittees and the village enjoyed when the facility was established. This case involved a private entity that made a choice to forego the siting process more than 12 years earlier when it had that option. The special condition was not unconstitutionally vague. The corporation had no problem deciphering the condition for 10 years, and seemed to clearly understand the terms when it applied for a permit that did not require siting approval.


OUTCOME: The determination was confirmed.

People v. Brockman


NO. 5-04-0433


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) summarily dismissing the inmate's postconviction petition.


OVERVIEW: In 1991, the inmate was convicted of armed robbery, armed violence, and aggravated robbery. The inmate was sentenced to serve consecutive 30-year prison terms. The instant postconviction petition was the fourth filed by the inmate. The inmate filed the instant petition pro se in 2004. The inmate alleged that the State failed to disclose the victim's statement made at the hospital after the alleged attack and that this statement differed substantially from the victim's testimony at trial. In dismissing the petition, the trial court found that the petition did not comply with 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1(f) (2004). Section 122-1(f) required the inmate to obtain leave of court before filing a successive postconviction petition. Thus, the trial court could have properly dismissed the inmate's successive postconviction petition on the basis that the inmate had failed to obtain leave of court before filing the petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. James


NO. 4-04-0414


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


362 Ill. App. 3d 1202; 841 N.E.2d 1109; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 16; 299 Ill. Dec. 377



January 12, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 10, 2006.
Rehearing denied by People v. James, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 79 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., Feb. 10, 2006)
Appeal denied by People v. James, 219 Ill. 2d 580, 852 N.E.2d 244, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 979, 303 Ill. Dec. 837 (2006)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. James, 2013 IL App (4th) 120494-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2023 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 03CF769. Honorable Dennis L. Schwartz, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) sentencing him to concurrent prison terms of 45 years for armed robbery, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-2(a)(1) (2002), seven years for unlawful use of a weapon by a felon, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.1(a) (2002), and 45 years for home invasion, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(a)(3) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was represented in the trial court by a public defender. Nevertheless, defendant filed several pro se, pretrial motions. On appeal, defendant argued that his Fifth Amendment right to due process and his Sixth Amendment right to self-representation were violated when the trial court refused to hear the pro se motions. Defendant was not entitled to representation of counsel and to self-representation at the same time. As a result, defendant was not permitted to file the pro se, pretrial motions that addressed strategic matters under counsel's control. While a defendant was permitted to file a pro se ineffective assistance of counsel claim, none of defendant's pro se motions at issue raised claims of ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant argued that his 15-year sentence enhancement under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(c) (2002) for home invasion violated the proportionate penalties clause. The enhancement was not declared unconstitutional when defendant was sentenced. 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(a)(3) was not vague. That provision clearly applied a 15-year sentence enhancement to home invasion as prescribed by 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(a)(3).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Yancy


No. 1-04-2605


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


368 Ill. App. 3d 381; 858 N.E.2d 454; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1298; 306 Ill. Dec. 657



December 29, 2005, Decided  
December 29, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 18, 2006.
Rehearing denied by People v. Yancy, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1197 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 13, 2006)
Appeal denied by People v. Yancy, 223 Ill. 2d 682, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 817 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03CR8685. The Honorable Dennis J. Porter, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, following a bench trial, convicted him for aggravated robbery and sentenced him to eight years in prison for his aggravated robbery conviction and five years for violating his probation, ordered to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that: (1) the trial court committed reversible error in admitting hearsay evidence that the quality assurance department agreed with the testifying forensic scientist's conclusion that fingerprints found at the scene of the crime matched defendant's; (2) there was error in sentencing him as a Class X offender pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3(c)(8) (2002) when his presentencing investigation report (PSI) did not show he committed his first qualifying felony subsequent to the date required by the statute; and (3) § 5/5-5-3(c)(8) was unconstitutional. The court agreed that defendant waived his challenge to the admission of hearsay evidence by failing to object. Regardless, even though the testimony was inadmissible hearsay, any error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt so that reversal was not warranted. Moreover, defendant waived his right to a jury prior to trial, so any contention that a jury was required to determine beyond a reasonable doubt the facts necessary to impose Class X offender status was waived. Finally, the court found that § 5/5-5-3(c)(8) was constitutional under the recidivism exception to the Apprendi doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

Dombrowski v. City of Chicago


No. 1-05-0321


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


363 Ill. App. 3d 420; 842 N.E.2d 302; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1297; 299 Ill. Dec. 563



December 29, 2005, Decided  
December 29, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 15, 2006.
Appeal denied by Dombrowski v. City of Chicago, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 441 (Ill., Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 04 M1 450591. The Honorable Sandra Tristano, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) affirmed an administrative law judge's (ALJ) finding that plaintiff building owner was liable for violating that part of the city building code that required building exteriors to be kept free of holes, cracks, or other openings that might admit water into a building's interior. It also affirmed the fine the ALJ assessed as a result. The building owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The building owner was the owner of a building at a particular location, which defendant city's building inspector observed and alleged violated the Chicago Building Code, specifically Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 13-196-530(b) (1990). That section required that building exteriors be free of holes, cracks, or other openings that might admit water into a building's interior. At trial, an administrative law judge (ALJ) found him liable and imposed a fine of $ 500. On administrative review to the trial court, the ALJ's judgment was affirmed. The building owner appealed. The appellate court found that building owner was not deprived of his due process rights to a full and fair administrative hearing because he never requested that the ALJ force the building inspector to appear for cross-examination about what was contained in the inspector's violation report, the ALJ did not find that the city's evidence was inherently more credible that the evidence of the building owner, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 13-196-530(b) (1990) was not unconstitutional, and the ALJ did not act unreasonably in assessing the maximum daily fine, especially since only one day's fine was imposed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Wead


No. 1-02-1878


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


363 Ill. App. 3d 121; 842 N.E.2d 227; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1280; 299 Ill. Dec. 488



December 23, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 15, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Wead, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 340 (Ill., Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 99 CR 3114. Honorable Stuart E. Palmer, Judge Presiding.
People v. Wead, 355 Ill. App. 3d 586, 823 N.E.2d 192, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 29, 291 Ill. Dec. 182 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of first degree murder after a jury trial. Defendant was sentenced to 38 years in prison. Defendant's motion for a new trial was denied. The court was reconsidering its prior decision to reverse defendant's conviction by direction of the Illinois Supreme Court in light of a caselaw decision.


OVERVIEW: The record showed that defendant voluntarily accompanied two plain clothed detectives to the police station, believing he was a witness as opposed to a suspect on three separate dates, January 16, 17, and 18, 1999, with regard to the murder. Defendant asserted on appeal that the police lacked probable cause to arrest him on the 16th since the police had no warrant and did not observe him committing a crime. Defendant further asserted on appeal that his statement made on the 18th was involuntary. The court found that defendant's incriminating statement was the product of his arrest without probable cause, his poor education, his limited intelligence, his poor health, his sleeping conditions, his lack of facilities to bathe, his restricted use of the restroom, and his 54-hour illegal detention. As such, defendant's statement was not an act of free will and required suppression.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction and remanded the case for a new trial in which defendant's post-arrest statement was subject to suppression.

O'Donnell v. City of Chicago


No. 1-04-3474


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


363 Ill. App. 3d 98; 842 N.E.2d 208; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1272; 299 Ill. Dec. 469



December 21, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 15, 2006.
Rehearing denied by O'Donnell v. City of Chicago, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 97 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Jan. 18, 2006)
Appeal denied by O'Donnell v. City of Chicago, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 453 (Ill., Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Aaron Jaffe, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and its officials (the city), appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting a request by plaintiff arcade owner for permanent injunctive relief against the enforcement of Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code §§ 4-156-150, 4-156-190, and 4-156-280, which prohibited and authorized the seizure of certain illegal amusement devices. The challenges focused on overbreadth, free expression, and search and seizure.


OVERVIEW: The ordinances prohibited certain illegal amusement devices, authorized their seizure and destruction, and imposed fines for illegal possession. The trial court had permanently enjoined the ordinances' enforcement, but the court on appeal found no constitutional violations. The ordinances clearly described exactly what components would make a device illegal, so as to satisfy due process, and were narrowly tailored to limit only amusement activities involving a narrow range of machines. The procedures for seizure and subsequent proceedings were also constitutionally proper. The mechanical components prohibited were those that made the devices gambling machines, and gambling was an activity subject to regulation and complete prohibition by ordinance. Furthermore, the seizures authorized by the scheme were only temporary, and devices could only be destroyed after a full administrative hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order.

People v. Brown


No. 1-02-3276


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1254



December 15, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1]
Rehearing denied by People v. Brown, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 149 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 7, 2006)
Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Brown, 363 Ill. App. 3d 838, 842 N.E.2d 1141, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 87, 299 Ill. Dec. 789 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94 CR 4624. Honorable Reginald Baker, Judge Presiding.
People v. Brown, 318 Ill. App. 3d 1223, 789 N.E.2d 936, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 3193, 273 Ill. Dec. 762 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of murder, attempted murder, two counts of armed robbery, and attempted armed robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was allegedly involved with two codefendants in the attempted robbery of a grocery store. Multiple charges resulted including a murder charge because one person was shot to death during the attempted robbery. Each of the codefendants was tried in a separate trial regarding the attempted robbery. Defendant was then tried. The trial court, pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10.2 (2002), published to the jury the custodial statements and prior testimony of the two codefendants; neither of them testified at defendant's trial. Defendant was convicted. On appeal, the appellate court found that while 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10.2 (2002) did not facially violate the Sixth Amendment's Confrontation Clause, the admission of the custodial statements and prior testimony of the two codefendants violated defendant's rights to confront witnesses because defendant did not have the opportunity to cross-examine the codefendants either during the interrogations that resulted in their statements or during their testimony at their separate trials.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Dowrick v. Vill. of Downers Grove


No. 2-05-0054


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


362 Ill. App. 3d 512; 840 N.E.2d 785; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1257; 298 Ill. Dec. 672



December 15, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released from Publication January 13, 2006.
Appeal denied by Dowrick v. Downers Grove, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 491 (Ill., Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 04-MR-63. Honorable Bonnie M. Wheaton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The DuPage County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that reversed defendant board of commissioner's decision to terminate plaintiff firefighter's employment and ordered him to be reinstated. It found that the prior decision of defendant pension fund to deny disability benefits to him was res judicata on whether he could be terminated due to a disability. The board of commissioners, the pension fund, and other defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The firefighter sought administrative review against the board of commissioners, the pension fund, and other defendants from a decision of the board of commissioners to discharge him from his employment as a firefighter. The board of commissioners had found he was unable and unwilling to perform. The trial court reversed the decision and ordered the firefighter reinstated. The trial court reasoned that a prior administrative decision of the pension fund denying disability benefits to the firefighter was res judicata and barred the board of commissioners from discharging the firefighter. On appeal, the appellate court found that the pension fund's prior decision finding that the firefighter was not entitled to a disability pension did not bar the board of commissioners in a subsequent proceeding from finding that the firefighter could be terminated due to a disability. It so held because it found that the doctrines of res judicata and collateral estoppel did not prevent the subsequent decision since the board of commissioners, a nonparty to the earlier decision, was not bound by the earlier proceeding that involved a party to the current proceeding, the firefighter.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

Decision reached on appeal by People v. Morris (In re Det. of Morris), 2016 IL App (4th) 160236-U, 2016 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2808 (Dec. 28, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Cass County. No. 98MR17. Honorable Mark A. Schuering, Judge Presiding.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for relief from judgment (735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2000)) following his adjudication as a sexually violent person. The Circuit Court of Cass County (Illinois) denied the petition, and he appealed.

People v. Hampton


No. 1-03-0067


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1188



December 5, 2005, Decided  
December 5, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1]
Rehearing denied by People v. Hampton, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 148 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 7, 2006)
Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Hampton, 842 N.E.2d 1124, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 131, 299 Ill. Dec. 772 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 16875. Honorable Preston L. Bowie, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him on eight counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault and two counts of home invasion with a firearm, and which sentenced him to a total of 84 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions and the imposition of his sentence upon application of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14 (2002). He raised five arguments, but the court found dispositive defendant's argument that admission of a codefendant's statement as an unavailable witness violated his U.S. Const. amend. VI confrontation right. The court agreed since he never had an opportunity to cross-examine. However, the State raised a valid issue on whether defendant committed wrongdoing that caused the codefendant's unavailability, which would waive his right to raise the confrontation issue. However, whether defendant waived the right was a factual issue that required the court to vacate defendant's convictions and remand for a fact hearing on whether defendant waived his right. If defendant did not waive the right, the court ordered a new trial. If defendant waived the right, the court ordered the home invasion conviction and sentence reinstated. It also ordered four of the assault convictions reinstated, but a new sentencing hearing was required because the 15 year mandatory add-on provision of § 5/12-14(d)(1) violated the proportionality clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's convictions and remanded with directions for a hearing on whether defendant forfeited his right under the confrontation clause to challenge the admission of an unavailable witness's out-of-court statement. If he did, four aggravated criminal assault and one home invasion convictions were reinstated, along with the sentencing on the home invasion, but a new sentencing hearing was required on the assault convictions.

People v. Kveton


No. 2-04-0204


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


362 Ill. App. 3d 822; 840 N.E.2d 714; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1195; 298 Ill. Dec. 601



December 5, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 17, 2006.
Rehearing denied by People v. Kveton, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 34 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Jan. 17, 2006)
Appeal denied by People v. Kveton, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 878 (Ill., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 03-CF-244. Honorable Perry R. Thompson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with possessing 30 to 500 grams of cannabis with the intent to deliver, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 550/5(d) (2004). Defendant, who was a high school student at the time of the arrest, moved to quash the arrest and suppress the evidence. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) denied the motion, and following a stipulated bench trial, defendant was found guilty. Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: A student found with marijuana told authorities that defendant had sold him the drugs. As defendant was walking from his house to his friend's car, an unmarked police car screeched to a stop in front of the friend's car. A police officer ordered defendant to come to the police car. The officer told defendant he knew about the drugs in his backpack. The officer told defendant open his backpack, and defendant complied. The officer found marijuana in a locked box. The officers then led defendant into the home and searched the residence, uncovering more marijuana. On appeal, defendant argued that the marijuana was inadmissible because his consent to the search was involuntary. The appellate court held that defendant was seized when the officer told him that he knew defendant had marijuana in his backpack. Therefore, the appellate court found that defendant's consent to the search was not voluntary. In light of the circumstances surrounding the request to search the home, the appellate court held that a reasonable person in defendant's position would not have felt free to leave. Therefore, defendant's consent to the search of the home was deemed involuntary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Rizzo


No. 2-03-1245


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


362 Ill. App. 3d 444; 842 N.E.2d 727; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1169; 299 Ill. Dec. 690



November 22, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 01-CM-3721. Honorable William I. Ferguson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) that convicted him of disorderly conduct under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/26-1 (2000) and sentenced him to two years' probation; defendant claimed that the evidence was insufficient, that his counsel was ineffective, and that a probation condition was unreasonable and constitutionally overbroad.


OVERVIEW: After the victim saw a "flash" outside her bay window, she saw defendant standing outside the window with his shorts unzipped and his hand moving up and down rapidly near his genital area. Defendant ran away when he saw the victim go to her telephone. The police found spots containing a "milky, creamy" substance on the right edge of the porch. A condition of defendant's probation stated that he could not enter any school, park, or forest preserve. The circumstantial evidence, when considered collectively, gave rise to a reasonable inference that defendant was looking into the victim's house through the window in violation of § 5/26-1. Although defense counsel assumed that defendant looked into the window, the questions were not needed to establish the window-peeping element of the offense. Accordingly, defendant was not prejudiced by counsel's performance. The probation condition did not contain any terms or exceptions to its geographic application as required by 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-6-3(b)(14) (2002). Therefore, the condition was not narrowly drawn and was unconstitutionally overbroad.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated as to the probation condition; it was affirmed in all other respects.

Schultz v. Lakewood Elec. Corp.


No. 1-04-3393


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


362 Ill. App. 3d 716; 841 N.E.2d 37; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1159; 298 Ill. Dec. 894

November 21, 2005, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that awarded statutory interest on a judgment that appellee injured party obtained against appellant prime electrical contractor, at the rate of nine percent pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1303 (2004). The prime electrical contractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: After a trial court granted a new trial to the prime electrical contractor following a jury's verdict for the injured party, the appellate court reversed the trial court's order granting a new trial and ordered the trial court to enter judgment on the jury's verdict in favor of the injured party. People v. Brown


No. 1-04-0714


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


362 Ill. App. 3d 374; 839 N.E.2d 596; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1149; 298 Ill. Dec. 273



November 16, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 28, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Brown, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1300 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 12, 2005)
Appeal denied by People v. Brown, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 334 (Ill., Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Thomas M. Davy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of armed violence, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33A-2(a) (2002), unlawful use of a weapon, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1(a)(4), aggravated unlawful use of a weapon and aggravated fleeing or attempting to elude, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33A-2, and sentenced him to 15 years of incarceration.


OVERVIEW: Police officers saw the driver of a Lexus fire three or four shots through the passenger window at a group of people standing in front of a Blues Lounge. The officers pursued the Lexus, engaging the squad car's siren and emergency lights. The officer estimated that the Lexus' speed was approximately 70 to 80 miles per hour on a street with a posted speed limit of 35 miles per hour. Defendant was convicted of armed violence, unlawful use of a weapon, and aggravated fleeing or attempting to elude. On appeal, the court found that armed violence occurred if a defendant committed a felony while having on or about his person a dangerous weapon or if a defendant was otherwise armed, and that that clearly occurred here, where defendant was shown to have a loaded handgun in his possession while fleeing from or attempting to elude police. The court found that if ever there was a felony offense during which the use of a deadly weapon should be deterred, it was a high-speed flight from or attempt to elude police. As such, the court found that the 15 year sentence, though harsh, was not cruel degrading, or so grossly disproportionate to the offense as to shock the moral sense of the community.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Johnson

People v. Boand


No. 2-04-0387


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


362 Ill. App. 3d 106; 838 N.E.2d 367; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1164; 297 Ill. Dec. 880



November 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 2, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Boand, 218 Ill. 2d 544, 850 N.E.2d 809, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 583, 303 Ill. Dec. 4 (2006)
Related proceeding at People v. Hoerer, 375 Ill. App. 3d 148, 872 N.E.2d 572, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 769, 313 Ill. Dec. 589 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., July 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 03-CF-276. Honorable James K. Booras, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Boand, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1006 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Sept. 30, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of drug-induced homicide, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3.3(a) (2004) and involuntary manslaughter, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3(a) (2004), with regard to one victim, and the criminal sexual assault of another victim, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-13(a)(2) (2004).


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced defendant to concurrent prison terms of 20 years for drug-induced homicide, five years for involuntary manslaughter, and 11 years for criminal sexual assault. Defendant's convictions arose from a drug party at a house wherein the dead victim overdosed on methadone that belonged to defendant. The sexual assault allegedly occurred early in the morning with another victim. The court found that while the evidence was not overwhelming, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the convictions of criminal sexual assault and of drug-induced homicide or involuntary manslaughter. Because the trial court erred in failing to sever the sex offense and homicide charges, however, defendant was entitled to a new trial. The court agreed with defendant that the sex offense and homicide charges arose from distinct acts affecting two different victims and that an intervening event of defendant travelling into Chicago with the alleged sex-offense victim also added to the finding that the charges did not arise from the same comprehensive transaction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions and remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings, noting that the court's disposition considered other issues raised in the appeal that might arise again on remand.

People v. Johnson


No. 2-04-1190


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


363 Ill. App. 3d 1060; 845 N.E.2d 645; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1358; 300 Ill. Dec. 756



November 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing March 24, 2006. Released for Publication April 21, 2006.
Rehearing denied by People v. Johnson, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 244 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Mar. 24, 2006)
Appeal denied by People v. Johnson, 221 Ill. 2d 656, 857 N.E.2d 678, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1242, 306 Ill. Dec. 279 (2006)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Doe v. Jewish Child & Family Servs., 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 3329 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 03--CF--3405. Honorable George Bridges, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Johnson, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1160 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Nov. 16, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by indictment with two counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14.1 ( 2002) and three counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-16(c)(1)(i) (2002). The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of two counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse and sentenced him to four years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was entitled to a new trial due to the unconstitutionality of 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10. The appellate court found no error, noting that the victim testified at trial and was subject to cross-examination; as such, none of the statements admitted pursuant to § 115-10 were improper under Crawford. Defendant also argued that he was entitled to a new trial because 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10(b)(3) rendered the victim's hearsay statements, testified to by a respite worker and an investigator, statutorily inadmissible. The appellate court disagreed, concluding that the victim's status as mentally retarded permitted the admission of the statements. Finally, defendant contended that the State failed to establish the time, content, and circumstances of the hearsay statements at issue were reliable within the meaning of § 115-10. The appellate court found no error, noting the victim's use of terminology unexpected of a child of similar age and the consistent repetition of the child's statements; the descriptive terms used were those expected from a child and supported the conclusion that the statements were reliable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1257 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fort


No. 1-04-1937


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


362 Ill. App. 3d 1; 839 N.E.2d 1064; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1124; 298 Ill. Dec. 417



November 15, 2005, Decided  
November 15, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 28, 2005.
Appeal denied by, Vacated by People v. Fort, 223 Ill. 2d 648, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 480, 309 Ill. Dec. 27 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable William G. Lacy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from that portion of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that required him, upon conviction of drug possession, to pay a $ 500 assessment without allowing a 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/110-14 (2002) credit for pretrial incarceration. Defendant further argued that assessment of an additional five dollar assessment and a DNA sampling requirement were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction was for simple possession. That conviction called for imposition of a $ 500 assessment under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/411.2 (2002). Defendant had been jailed pending trial, and had not been able to make bail, so he argued that he should receive a credit of five dollars a day against the assessment under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/110-14 (2002). Although the State argued that the assessment was not a fine to which the credit applied, the court found no basis for that argument in either the plain language of the statute or its legislative history. The credit made it unnecessary to consider whether defendant could afford to pay the full assessment. The court further found that there was no rational relationship between an assessment of five dollars to benefit a fund benefiting victims of spinal cord injuries and a conviction of simple drug possession. Therefore, imposition of that assessment violated due process. Finally, it was already settled law that a requirement that convicted felons submit DNA samples did not violate substantive due process.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment to allow the credit for pretrial incarceration and to set aside the five dollar assessment but otherwise affirmed the judgment in all respects.

People v. Burdine


No. 1-03-3529


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


362 Ill. App. 3d 19; 839 N.E.2d 573; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1114; 298 Ill. Dec. 250



November 10, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 16, 2005. Released for Publication December 28, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Burdine, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1299 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 9, 2005)
Appeal denied by People v. Burdine, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 797 (Ill., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 9812. Honorable Fred G. Suria, Jr., Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated battery under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-4(b)(6)(2002) and required him to produce DNA evidence pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-4-3.


OVERVIEW: Members of defendant's family called the paramedics because they believed he was ill. Fire department paramedics responded to the call. Defendant was unresponsive, and paramedics believed that he was intoxicated and feigning unconsciousness. It was Chicago fire department policy that intoxicated individuals were to be transported to the hospital. As one of the paramedics wrapped his arms under defendant's armpits and attempted to grab defendant's wrists to prop him up, defendant became combative and bit the paramedic's left forearm. Defendant was convicted of aggravated battery. On appeal, the court found that the evidence clearly proved defendant guilty of aggravated battery because it showed that he knowingly bit an on-duty fireman on the arm causing him bodily harm. The court found also that the indictment clearly identified the victim, the nature of the incident, and the date and place of the incident and that the judgment could be presented to bar subsequent prosecution for the same conduct, preventing the risk of double jeopardy. Lastly, the court rejected defendant's objections to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-4-3, noting that it previously upheld the statute as constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Quinones


No. 1-04-1405


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


362 Ill. App. 3d 385; 839 N.E.2d 583; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1115; 298 Ill. Dec. 260



November 10, 2005, Decided  
November 10, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 28, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Quinones, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 598 (Ill., Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03CR10935. The Honorable Lawrence Terrell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that found defendant guilty of two counts of defacing firearm identification marks and two counts of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon. Defendant was then sentenced. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Following a bench trial, defendant was found guilty of two counts of defacing firearm identification marks and two counts of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (UUW). On appeal, defendant contended that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-5(b) (2002), regarding the defacing of firearm identification marks, contained an unconstitutional mandatory presumption that relieved the State of its burden of proving that a defendant knowingly or intentionally defaced the identifying marks on a firearm beyond a reasonable doubt, that his multiple convictions of defacing a firearm and multiple convictions of aggravated UUW violate the one-act, one-crime doctrine, that the trial court's mistaken belief that aggravated UUW was a Class 3, rather than a Class 4, felony influenced its sentencing decision, that he was prejudiced when the trial court failed to completely admonish him of his appellate rights, and that compulsory extraction of his DNA as part of his sentence violated his constitutional rights. The appellate court found that the statute was unconstitutional for the reason he described, agreed that the one-act, one-crime doctrine had been violated, and rejected his remaining contentions.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments of conviction finding defendant guilty on two counts of defacing a firearm and one of the two counts of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon were reversed. However, the trial court's judgment of conviction on the second of two counts of aggravated unlawful use of weapon and the sentence associated with that conviction was affirmed.

People v. James


NO. 4-03-1082


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


362 Ill. App. 3d 285; 838 N.E.2d 1008; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1128; 298 Ill. Dec. 115



November 10, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 8, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. James, 217 Ill. 2d 614, 844 N.E.2d 969, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 302, 300 Ill. Dec. 526 (Jan. 25, 2006)
Related proceeding at People v. James, 364 Ill. App. 3d 1064, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 3048 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., May 3, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Stay denied by, Certificate of appealability denied James v. Spiller, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 142298 (C.D. Ill., Oct. 7, 2014)
Decision reached on appeal by People v. James, 2017 IL App (4th) 160256, 2017 Ill. App. LEXIS 290 (May 3, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Vermilion County. No. 02CF141. Honorable Thomas J. Fahey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed that portion of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois) that imposed an enhanced sentence on him, under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(1) (2002), after he was found guilty of armed robbery. He argued that the sentencing statute was unconstitutional in permitting an increased sentence without a jury or even a judge having found the existence of a prior felony conviction beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction of attempted murder had occurred within 10 years before his armed robbery conviction. He never contested the records of his past felony convictions, and he received an enhanced sentence. At that point, he challenged the constitutionality of § 5-5-3.2(b)(1), arguing that earlier cases finding that the scheme did not violate the rule of Apprendi had been wrongly decided. The court adhered to its earlier holdings of constitutionality, noting that the nation's highest court had expressly reserved a recidivism exception to the rule otherwise requiring jury findings. Furthermore, the fact of the prior conviction did not have to be proved beyond a reasonable doubt because it was not an element of the armed robbery offense of which defendant was being convicted, but simply a sentencing factor. Therefore, the trial court could rely on the information in the presentence report, the accuracy of which defendant had not challenged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Reed


NO. 4-03-0674


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


361 Ill. App. 3d 995; 838 N.E.2d 328; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1104; 297 Ill. Dec. 841



November 4, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 30, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Reed, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1196 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., Nov. 30, 2005)
Appeal denied by People v. Reed, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 562 (Ill., Mar. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 02CF1800. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Champaign County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. The trial court then sentenced him. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly forced the victim, his 10-year-old stepdaughter, to perform oral sex on him. Defendant's wife investigated and called police. The victim allegedly told the wife and police that defendant had forced her to have oral sex not only on that occasion, but also on an earlier occasion. Defendant was charged with one count of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. In a pretrial hearing, the trial court ruled that the victim's out-of-court statements to her mother and the police would be admissible pursuant to the statutory exception to the hearsay rule, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10 (2002). At trial, the State called the victim as a witness and also presented her hearsay statements. The jury found defendant guilty. On appeal, the appellate court found that evidence of the uncharged sex offense was admissible pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-7.3 (2002). It also found that because the victim testified and was subject to cross-examination, the admission of her hearsay statements did not violate the Confrontation Clause. Also, it concluded that his ineffective assistance of counsel claim lacked merit and that he was entitled to a sentencing credit.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of conviction was affirmed; however, the appellate court found that defendant was entitled to an additional two days of sentence credit. As a result, it ordered that the clerk of the circuit court to enter a modified sentencing judgment reflecting 286 credits for time served.

People v. Rodriguez


No. 1-04-3546


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


362 Ill. App. 3d 44; 839 N.E.2d 543; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1071; 298 Ill. Dec. 220



November 3, 2005, Decided  
November 3, 2005, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 28, 2005.
Appeal denied by, Vacated by, Remanded by People v. Rodriguez, 223 Ill. 2d 671, 863 N.E.2d 257, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 511, 309 Ill. Dec. 27 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of possession of a controlled substance. It also ordered that, pursuant to Illinois statutory law, he pay $5 to the Spinal Cord Injury Research Fund. Defendant appealed both the conviction and the order that he pay the money to the fund.


OVERVIEW: The police officer pulled over defendant's minivan after the officer observed the minivan drive by with a broken taillight. When defendant could not produce certain documents, the officer asked defendant to walk back to the officer's squad car. While doing so, defendant dropped three small bags. The officer arrested defendant. The officer transported the items defendant had dropped to a police station; there he inventoried them and gave them to a desk sergeant. The bags' content tested positive for the presence cocaine. Defendant's attorney stipulated that a proper chain of custody was maintained over the items recovered and that the items tested positive for the presence of cocaine. Defendant was found guilty of possession of a controlled substance. The trial court ordered defendant to pay $ 5 to the Spinal Cord Injury Research Fund, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-9-1.1(c) (2004). On appeal, the appellate court found defendant's federal and state constitutional confrontation rights were not violated by his attorney's stipulation, but the sum he was ordered to pay was a fee that bore no rational relationship to his conviction for possession of a controlled substance.


OUTCOME: The trial court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance but reversed the trial court's order that defendant pay a $5 fee to the Spinal Cord Injury Research fund.

People v. Williams


Nos. 2-05-0221, 2-05-0222, 2-05-0223, 2-05-0224, 2-05-0225, 2-05-0226 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


361 Ill. App. 3d 723; 838 N.E.2d 275; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1099; 297 Ill. Dec. 788



November 3, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 2, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Williams, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 300 (Ill., Jan. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 03-CM-1971, No. 04-CM-5859, No. 04-CM-4585, No. 04-CM-4588, No. 04-CM-7692, No. 04-CM-7866. Honorable Gary V. Pumilia, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, the State challenged decisions from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which granted motions by defendants in separate cases to dismiss charges against them for mob action in violation of § 25-1(a)(2) of the Criminal Code of 1961, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/25-1(a)(2) (2004).


OVERVIEW: In separate criminal cases, defendants were charged with, among other things, mob action in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/25-1(a)(2) (2004). In all cases, defendants received dismissal of the mob action charges due to a preexisting injunction from a federal court that enjoined enforcement of § 25-1(a)(2). The State appealed and the court consolidated those appeals. The court found that the injunction was still in effect, even though a ruling that the statute was unconstitutional was reversed, and that injunction precluded the State from prosecuting each defendant for the mob action crime. The court rejected the State's contention that the injunction only applied to the parties in the federal action. A controlling decision from the state supreme court held that the injunction was still in effect and that the State had no valid basis for refusing to honor the injunction. Since that decision was controlling precedential authority, the court upheld the decisions that the mob action charges could not be enforced while the injunction was still valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of the mob action charges against defendants.

People v. Kelly


NO. 4-03-0775


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


361 Ill. App. 3d 515; 838 N.E.2d 236; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1325; 297 Ill. Dec. 749



October 31, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 29, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Kelly, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 783 (Ill., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. No. 03CF87. Honorable Harold J. Frobish, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Livingston County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty at a trial in absentia of unlawful possession of cannabis. The trial court then sentenced him. Thereafter, at a new sentencing hearing, he was sentenced to 4 years in prison with credit for a certain amount of time served. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police officers executed a search warrant at a house. One officer noticed a backpack lying on the living room floor. The backpack had protruding from it a plastic bag containing what appeared to be cannabis. A police officer who interviewed defendant asked defendant if a fingerprint analysis conducted on the plastic bag would reveal the presence of defendant's prints. Defendant then conceded that he was familiar with the bag and had been smoking the cannabis from the bag. At a trial in absentia, he was found guilty of possession of cannabis in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 550/4(d) (2002). He was sentenced and given a credit for time spent in prejudgment incarceration. Pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002), he was also required to submit to mandatory genetic testing. On appeal, the appellate court found that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction and the trial court did not err in ordering the reimbursement of attorney fees without determining defendant's ability to pay since defendant's trial was in absentia. However, it also found he was entitled to an additional day of sentence credit.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of conviction was affirmed, but the case was remanded to the trial court with directions to amend the judgment to add one additional day of sentence credit based on defendant's prejudgment incarceration; the trial court was also directed to amend the judgment to reflect the concomitant monetary credit toward the fines imposed.

People v. Ramirez


No. 2-04-0243


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


361 Ill. App. 3d 450; 837 N.E.2d 111; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1005; 297 Ill. Dec. 331



October 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing October 14, 2005.
Released for Publication November 18, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 95-CF-1399. Honorable Grant S. Wegner, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 1995, defendant pled guilty to armed violence. Because of the Safe Neighborhoods Act, his minimum sentence was 10 years. In Cervantes, the state supreme court declared the Safe Neighborhoods Act to be unconstitutional. Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1 et seq. (2002).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the lateness of his petition was not due to his culpable negligence because the basis for his petition, the Illinois Supreme Court's decision in Cervantes, did not arise until four years after his conviction. The appellate court concluded that defendant was not culpably negligent for failing to file his post-conviction petition during the period before Cervantes was decided. However, defendant was culpably negligent based on the time period that elapsed between the decision in Cervantes, issued in December 1999, and the filing of his petition on May 27, 2003. Defendant offered no reason for his delay in filing a petition until over 40 months after Cervantes was issued. Thus, the trial court should have granted the State's motion to dismiss defendant's petition as untimely. In addition, defendant's conviction and sentence were not void, but merely voidable. Thus, he could not challenge them at any time in any proceeding as he could a void judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Cortez


No. 2-04-0935


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


361 Ill. App. 3d 456; 837 N.E.2d 449; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1047; 297 Ill. Dec. 366



October 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 18, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Cortez, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 250 (Ill., Jan. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 03-CF-2197. Honorable Michael J. Burke, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) convicting defendant of driving a vehicle with a blood-alcohol concentration of 0.08 or greater in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501(a)(1) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant lost control of his vehicle as he drove down an interstate entrance ramp. The vehicle rolled over. A state trooper questioned defendant at the scene. According to the trooper, defendant had bloodshot eyes, slurred his speech, and smelled of alcohol. Defendant admitted to having consumed a couple of beers. Defendant was taken to the hospital. Shortly after defendant arrived, the trooper arrested him for driving under the influence in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501(a)(2) (2002). Based on defendant's blood test, he was charged with the offense of which he was convicted. Defendant argued that the trooper lacked probable cause to arrest him. Defendant pointed to inconsistencies in the trooper's testimony. Defendant failed to point to any inconsistencies in the trooper's testimony regarding the indicia of intoxication. The trial court's finding that the inconsistencies in defendant's testimony did not impeach the remaining testimony was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. Probable cause existed to arrest defendant, as he rolled his vehicle over, exhibited indicia of intoxication, and admitted to having consumed beer before driving.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1267 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hauschild


No. 2-03-0857


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1026



October 5, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at People v. Hauschild, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 176 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Mar. 8, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 01-CF-2403. Honorable Donald C. Hudson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) convicting him of armed robbery, home invasion, and criminal damage to property. He argued that the armed robbery provision, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-2(a)(2) (2000), and the home invasion provision, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(a)(4) (2000), he was convicted of violating were invalid under Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, as imposing disproportionate penalties.


OVERVIEW: Defendant carried a gun when he and another invaded the victims' home, and one of the victims was badly injured when shots were fired during a struggle. The robbery and home invasion statutes under which he had been charged had been amended to provide a range of very severe penalties in cases where a firearm had been used. Certain subsections of each statute had already been found to violate the proportionate penalties clause, and the court found that the subsections under which defendant had been convicted were similarly defective because the resulting sentences were far more severe than those that could be imposed for crimes that necessarily included serious injury or death from a firearm. The definitions of the offenses were not severable from the disproportionate sentence enhancements, so reversal was required. The armed robbery conviction could be replaced with a conviction of simple robbery, but home invasion had no such lesser-included offenses, so that conviction and sentence were simply vacated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the armed robbery and home invasion convictions and vacated the sentences on those offenses. It affirmed the conviction of criminal damage to property. It ordered that the trial court enter a judgment convicting defendant of the lesser-included offense of robbery and remanded for sentencing for that offense.

GMC v. State Motor Vehicle Review Bd.


NO. 4-04-0735


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


361 Ill. App. 3d 271; 836 N.E.2d 903; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1028; 297 Ill. Dec. 172; 2005-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P75,017



October 3, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 2, 2005.
Appeal granted by GMC v. State Motor Vehicle Review Bd., 217 Ill. 2d 600, 844 N.E.2d 965, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 197, 300 Ill. Dec. 522 (2006)
Appeal granted by GMC v. State Motor Vehicle Review Bd., 217 Ill. 2d 600, 844 N.E.2d 965, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 184, 300 Ill. Dec. 522 (2006)
Affirmed by GMC v. State Motor Vehicle Review Bd., 224 Ill. 2d 1, 862 N.E.2d 209, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1, 308 Ill. Dec. 611 (2007)
Costs and fees proceeding at GMC v. State Motor Vehicle Review Bd., 2013 IL App (4th) 080893-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1465 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 03MR412. Honorable Robert J. Eggers, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff manufacturer and nominal defendant new auto dealership appealing a decision of defendant Illinois Motor Vehicle Review Board sustaining defendant existing dealerships' protests to the establishment of additional dealerships in their area as unsupported by good cause under 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 710/12 (2000) challenged the affirmance by the Sangamon Circuit Court (Illinois) of the administrative decision.


OVERVIEW: The existing dealerships protested the manufacturer's decision to add two more dealerships to their saturated areas. The court, reviewing the Review Board's findings with great deference, held that the determination that good cause, as defined at 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 710/2 (2000), did not exist for adding new dealerships was not against the manifest weight of the evidence and there were no clearly erroneous findings. It then considered the manufacturer's many constitutional challenges to the Motor Vehicle Franchise Act. "Good cause" was readily understandable enough to survive a vagueness challenge, and the proceedings themselves moved slowly only because of their complexity. The Act did not unduly burden interstate commerce, and it rationally related to a legitimate state concern with preventing manufacturers from unfairly using their great economic power to burden or destroy dealerships. A related challenge under the Sherman Act, 15 U.S.C.S. §§ 1-7, failed because the Franchise Act fell within the Sherman Act's state-action exemption. Although an award of attorney fees was allowed under the Act, the award was not yet reviewable because no amount had been specified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the administrative decision in all substantive respects, but vacated an award of attorney fees because that issue was not ripe for review. It remanded the matter to the Review Board for a determination of fees and costs to be awarded.

People v. Blanks


No. 1-02-0161


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


361 Ill. App. 3d 400; 837 N.E.2d 118; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 986; 297 Ill. Dec. 338



September 30, 2005, Decided  
September 30, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 9, 2005. As Corrected November 30, 2005.
Reported at People v. Blanks, 361 Ill. App. 3d 400, 845 N.E.2d 1, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1364, 300 Ill. Dec. 580 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 22705. Honorable Shelley Sutker-Dermer, Judge Presiding.
People v. Blanks, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 239 (Ill. App. Ct., Mar. 15, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Defendant's convictions for burglary is reversed and his conviction for aggravated battery affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was found guilty of aggravated battery of one victim and the burglary of another victim's home. He was sentenced to an extended-term of six years' imprisonment for the Class 3 felony offense of aggravated battery and a concurrent term of six years imprisonment for the Class X felony offense of burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with residential burglary after he entered a home that was being remodeled and attempted to remove certain tools. He was chased from the home but returned with a 30 inch "club," which he was swinging wildly when he hit the battery victim. Because the house was being remodeled, the trial court ruled that defendant was not guilty of residential burglary but was instead guilty of simple burglary. The court reversed the burglary conviction, holding that 1) the amendment to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/19-3(a) (2002), which made burglary a lesser included offense of residential burglary, went into effect after defendant was charged, was substantive in nature, and could not be applied retroactively; 2) as the trial court had specifically ruled that defendant was not guilty of residential burglary, double jeopardy precluded his retrial on that charge; 3) the trial court properly ruled that the club defendant used was a deadly weapon; 4) defendant's prior aggravated battery conviction made him eligible for the extended sentence he received for the instant aggravated battery conviction; and 5) 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(1) (2000) was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's burglary conviction and sentence were reversed. His conviction and sentence for aggravated battery were affirmed.

People v. Clay


No. 1-03-2690


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


361 Ill. App. 3d 310; 836 N.E.2d 872; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 994; 297 Ill. Dec. 141



September 30, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 9, 2005. As Corrected December 5, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Clay, 217 Ill. 2d 609, 844 N.E.2d 968, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 164, 300 Ill. Dec. 525 (2006)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Clay, 2013 IL App (1st) 101931-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1760 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 14092 01. Honorable Thomas M. Tucker, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, following a bench trial, rejected defendant's insanity defense, found him guilty of murdering his girlfriend and his daughter, but also found him mentally ill, and which sentenced him to natural life without parole.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant did not challenge the murder findings. All appellate issues concerned his insanity defense. He argued that the insanity statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-2 (2000), violated the Due Process, Cruel and Unusual Punishment, and Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and Illinois constitutions. He also challenged findings that he was competent and that he did not prove insanity. The court found that the clear and convincing burden of proof for an insanity defense did not violate due process. The insanity statute did not make mental illness itself a crime, so there was no cruel and unusual punishment. A rational basis existed for treating insanity and intoxication defenses differently, so equal protection was satisfied. Despite evidence that defendant had delusional thoughts or recollections of the crime, evidence also showed that he was fully aware of the charges and the nature of the proceedings, and he was able to work with counsel on his defense, so he was competent to stand trial under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/104-16(b) (2000). Finally, the trial court properly weighed conflicting evidence to find defendant did not prove his insanity defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and his sentence of life without parole.

People v. Boand


No. 2-04-0387


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1006



September 30, 2005, Filed

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at People v. Boand, 362 Ill. App. 3d 106, 838 N.E.2d 367, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1164, 297 Ill. Dec. 880 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Nov. 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 03-CF-276. Honorable James K. Booras, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of the drug-induced homicide and involuntary manslaughter of one woman and criminal sexual assault of another woman. Defendant was sentenced to concurrent prison terms of 20 years for the drug-induced homicide, five years for involuntary manslaughter, and 11 years for criminal sexual assault.

The Stated addressed each of the issues raised by defendant and asserted that a remand was in order for the trial court to impose mandatory consecutive sentences. The court concluded that the trial court erred in denying the motion to sever the criminal sexual assault charge from the drug induced homicide and involuntary manslaughter charges, which error was compounded by the erroneous admission of evidence of defendant's other sex crimes and the corresponding jury instruction.

People v. Blanks


No. 1-02-0161


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


361 Ill. App. 3d 400; 845 N.E.2d 1; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1364; 300 Ill. Dec. 580



September 30, 2005, Decided  
September 30, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 9, 2005. As Corrected November 30, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 22705. Honorable Shelley Sutker-Dermer, Judge Presiding.
People v. Blanks, 361 Ill. App. 3d 400, 837 N.E.2d 118, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 986, 297 Ill. Dec. 338 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted at a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of aggravated battery, under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-4(b)(1) (2000), and burglary, under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/19-3 ( 2000). Defendant was sentenced to an extended-term of six years' imprisonment for the felony offense of aggravated battery and a concurrent term of six years imprisonment for the felony offense of burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A homeowner was having his house remodeled while he was still living in the house. Construction workers at the site noticed defendant picking up the construction company's tools in the house. An altercation ensued in which defendant used a stick that was approximately 30 inches long and two inches thick to hit a construction worker in the head. None of the homeowner's property was missing after defendant's unauthorized entry. On appeal, the court found that (1) defendant's burglary conviction was improper because an amendment to the residential burglary statute, which included burglary as a lesser-included offense of residential burglary, was not effective until after defendant's conviction; (2) sufficient evidence existed to find defendant guilty of aggravated battery beyond a reasonable doubt predicated upon his use of a deadly weapon to commit a battery; (3) 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3(c)(8) (2000) was constitutional; and (4) the extended-term sentencing provision of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(1) (2000), which allowed discretionary extended-term sentencing by the judge based on prior convictions, did not violate defendant's due process or jury trial guarantees.


OUTCOME: The conviction for burglary was reversed, and the conviction for aggravated battery was affirmed.

People v. Gilford


No. 1-01-0695


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


361 Ill. App. 3d 56; 836 N.E.2d 825; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 956; 297 Ill. Dec. 94



September 27, 2005, Decided  
September 27, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 9, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Gilford, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 157 (Ill., Jan. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 95 C4 41108. Honorable Themis N. Karnezis, Judge Presiding.
People v. Gilford, 336 Ill. App. 3d 722, 784 N.E.2d 841, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1255, 271 Ill. Dec. 287 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) determined that defendant was a sexually dangerous person under § 1.01 of the Illinois Sexually Dangerous Persons Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 205/1.01 (1996), the instant court vacated the judgment and remanded. The Supreme Court of Illinois denied the State's petition for leave to appeal but directed the instant court to vacate its opinion and reconsider its judgment in light of another case.


OVERVIEW: The case was reconsidered in light of In re Detention of Varner, which involved the constitutionality of a civil commitment proceeding under the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 et seq. (1998). The trial court never made a lack-of-control determination as required by the U.S. Supreme Court in Crane or the Illinois Supreme Court in Masterson. The State claimed, however, that defendant's diagnosis of paraphilia met the "serious difficulty" requirement under Crane and maintained that defendant's diagnosis as a pedophile necessarily implied that he lacked volitional capacity such that he had serious difficulty in controlling his behavior. The appeals court disagreed. Defendant's diagnosis as a pedophile did not necessarily imply that he lacked volitional capacity such that he had serious difficulty in controlling his behavior. Consequently, the trial court's judgment had to be vacated and remanded with directions to determine whether defendant's mental condition caused him serious difficulty in controlling his criminal sexual behavior. The "serious difficulty" finding required by the State's petition was to be made by the trier of fact.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was vacated, and the cause was remanded for a new commitment hearing wherein the parties would have a full and fair opportunity to adduce evidence pertinent to the applicable standards announced. The court retained jurisdiction for the purpose of reviewing the trial court's determination following the commitment hearing, and defendant and the State were allowed to submit supplemental briefs addressing this issue.

People v. Bartgen


No. 1-04-2095


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


361 Ill. App. 3d 336; 836 N.E.2d 798; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 943; 297 Ill. Dec. 67



September 26, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 9, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 23300. Honorable Thomas M. Tucker, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, after a motion to dismiss attempted first-degree murder charges was denied, was convicted in a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of two counts of attempted first-degree murder, pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/8-4 (2000). The circuit court sentenced defendant to two concurrent six-year terms in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appeared to have planned his attack on the victim by discovering the victim's home, timing his arrival at the victim's home to when the victim left for work, and dressing to conceal his identity. After shooting the victim, defendant chased the victim down in his car apparently to finish the job. Defendant later lied to the police about the condition of his car after the attack. Defendant argued that the attempt statute was unconstitutional, and that he was under the influence of prescription antidepressant medication and involuntarily intoxicated when he committed the offenses. On appeal, the court found that, while the state supreme court had held that the attempt statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/8-4 (2000), as amended by 1991 Ill. Laws 404, § 5, was unconstitutional as it violated the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, only the amendment to the statute was unconstitutional. Thus, the statute was properly applied as it existed before the amendment. Further, the evidence rebutted defendant's position that he was intoxicated under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-3 (2002), whether voluntarily or involuntarily, when he committed the offenses.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
