People v. Foreman


No. 1-04-1362


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


361 Ill. App. 3d 136; 836 N.E.2d 750; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 936; 297 Ill. Dec. 19



September 22, 2005, Decided  
September 22, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 9, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Foreman, 222 Ill. 2d 613, 862 N.E.2d 236, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 344, 308 Ill. Dec. 638 (2007)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Petition denied by People v. Foreman, 237 Ill. 2d 570, 938 N.E.2d 525, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1474, 345 Ill. Dec. 86 (2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied United States ex rel. Foreman v. Hardy, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 76087 (N.D. Ill., July 14, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 26300. The Honorable Diane Gordon Cannon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part; mittimus corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was found guilty of first degree murder. The jury additionally found that during the commission of the offense, defendant personally discharged a firearm that proximately caused the victim's death. The trial court sentenced defendant to two concurrent 50-year prison terms for two counts of first degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court could not say that trial counsel was ineffective in failing to question potential jurors regarding the principles articulated in Zehr. Because of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt, he could not show a reasonable probability that the outcome would have been different had such questioning taken place. Although defendant waived the argument because he failed to raise an objection to the court's failure to inform potential jurors of the principles embodied in Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 431(b) at trial or in a posttrial motion, the jurors were substantially informed in accordance with Rule 431(a) prior to the commencement of trial, and defendant was not deprived of a fair trial. Defendant contended that the trial court's admonishment to the deadlocked jury improperly coerced a holdout juror, but the trial court's instruction to the jury was a modification and clarification of the Prim instruction and was a correct statement of the law. The appeals court agreed with defendant and the State that the two convictions for counts IX and X improperly violated the one-act, one-crime doctrine and that count IX, which required a more culpable mental state, should stand.


OUTCOME: Defendant's murder conviction was affirmed under count IX and vacated under count X, and he was entitled to 911 days of credit against his sentence. The mittimus was corrected in accordance with the holding.

People v. Standley


NO. 4-03-0872


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


359 Ill. App. 3d 1096; 835 N.E.2d 945; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 945; 296 Ill. Dec. 592



September 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 24, 2005.
Appeal denied by, Vacated by People v. Standley, 217 Ill. 2d 622, 840 N.E.2d 1233, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 92, 298 Ill. Dec. 798 (2006)
On remand at People v. Standley, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 359 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., May 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 03CF574. Honorable Katherine M. McCarthy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), found defendant guilty of home invasion, a violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(a)(3) (2002). Defendant's posttrial motion was denied and he was sentenced to an enhanced sentence under § 12-11(c). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that there was insufficient evidence to find him guilty of home invasion and that his 15-year sentence enhancement, mandated by § 12-11(c) was unconstitutional. The court affirmed. Two eyewitnesses identified defendant as one of two men who invaded their home. One of witnesses was at an arm's length from defendant for at least 10 minutes. The fact that the eyewitnesses failed to describe defendant as having facial hair did not negate their identifications. Further, the jury had the right to believe the eyewitnesses testimony over that of defendant's alibi witnesses. As to the sentence enhancement, the court applied a cross-comparison analysis to determine if home invasion with a firearm was a less serious offense than aggravated battery with a firearm but was punished more severely. The court concluded that both offenses shared the same statutory purpose. As home invasion could cause emotional and psychological trauma greater than that caused by an aggravated battery with a firearm, the legislature had determined that home invasion with a firearm was a greater evil than aggravated battery with a firearm. Therefore, the sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Knauerhaze v. Nelson


No. 1-03-3370


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


361 Ill. App. 3d 538; 836 N.E.2d 640; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 924; 296 Ill. Dec. 889



September 19, 2005, Decided  
September 19, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 9, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 00 L 010323. Honorable Thomas L. Hogan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1008 (2004) special representative of original defendant deceased doctor and his incorporated practice, appealed and plaintiff patient cross-appealed from a judgment on jury verdict of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) awarding the patient millions of dollars on his malpractice claim.


OVERVIEW: The patient sued the doctor after an operation on his ear resulted in severe disability. The doctor died during the trial and rather than delay, the patient elected to have a special administrator appointed under § 2-1008, and was awarded a large sum which was, however, under § 2-1008(b), limited by the amount of the doctor's malpractice coverage. The court held that the evidence was ample to support the jury's findings both that the doctor was negligent in failing to abort an operation that was going wrong and that the negligence proximately caused the injuries. The evidence adduced at trial did not, however, adequately establish vicarious liability of the practice, because it was based solely on extrajudicial admissions in unverified pleadings. The patient argued that he should be allowed to pursue the doctor's estate, which had since been opened, for any deficiency after malpractice coverage had been exhausted, but the court held that the statute meant what it said, and that the plain meaning comported with legislative intent of allowing an expedited process as long as plaintiffs were willing to accept the limits the legislature had placed on the statutory right it had created.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and for a new trial on the issue of negligence but reversed the order denying a new trial on the issue of the practice's liability under agency principles. It affirmed the trial court on matters of statutory interpretation raised in the cross-appeal.

Marconi v. Chi. Heights Police Pension Bd.


Nos. 1-04-1725 & 1-04-2390 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


361 Ill. App. 3d 1; 836 N.E.2d 705; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 925; 296 Ill. Dec. 954



September 19, 2005, Decided  
September 19, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 9, 2005.
Appeal granted by Marconi v. Chi. Heights Police Pension Bd., 217 Ill. 2d 566, 844 N.E.2d 39, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 2036, 300 Ill. Dec. 367 (2005)
Reversed by, in part, Vacated by, in part Marconi v. Chicago Heights Police Pension Bd., 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1648 (Ill., Oct. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 02 CH 04584 & 02 CH 213000. Honorable David R. Donnersberger, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer applied to defendant pension board for a disability pension. During the board's review of the application, he brought an action for declaratory judgment, mandamus, and other relief. While this action was pending before the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), the board denied the pension. The circuit court affirmed and then granted summary judgment in the declaratory action in the board's favor. The officer appealed.


OVERVIEW: All of the mental health professionals who were consulted agreed that at the time of his removal from active duty the officer had a psychiatric impairment rendering him unable to function as a police officer. Therefore, under Hahn, the board's denial of the pension was clearly erroneous. It was significant that he did not leave active duty on his own accord but was removed from active duty by his superiors. The board argued that its decision had to be affirmed pursuant to the 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-115 (2002) "three certifications" requirement. However, in the event that the board's doctors did not unanimously certify an applicant as disabled, whatever meritorious arguments the applicant might raise at a hearing would have no bearing on the outcome of his case because just one unfavorable certificate rendered the entire proceeding pointless. Accordingly, the § 3-115 certification requirement, as it was currently drafted, was unconstitutional as applied to the officer and did not bar him from receiving a pension. As to the declaratory judgment action, even if the court were to agree with the officer that his due process rights were violated, it would not change the outcome.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment in the declaratory action was affirmed, but the circuit court's affirmance of the pension board's decision to deny the officer a pension was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the board for further proceedings because the board did not make a determination as to whether the officer was entitled to a "line of duty" pension or a "not on duty" pension.

Wieland v. Lawyers Trust Fund of Ill.


NO. 5-03-0419


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


359 Ill. App. 3d 1147; 836 N.E.2d 166; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 950; 296 Ill. Dec. 751



September 15, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 02-L-822. Honorable Michael J. O'Malley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed a class action complaint against defendants, the Lawyers Trust Fund of Illinois and the Justices of the Supreme Court of Illinois, alleging that Ill. Sup. Ct. R. Prof. Conduct 1.15, which established a program to provide for interest on lawyers' trust accounts (IOLTA), violated the Fifth Amendment. The Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) granted defendants' motion to dismiss. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, plaintiffs raised numerous issues. In Brown, the United States Supreme Court found that Washington's IOLTA rule resulted in a per se taking of private property for public use. However, because "just compensation" was measured by the property owner's loss, rather than the government's gain, and because if the Washington rule was followed, only funds that could not generate net interest for the client were to be placed in IOLTA accounts, the amount of compensation due was zero. The appellate court found no meaningful difference in the language of the Washington rule and the language of the Illinois rule. Accordingly, it found the holding of the United States Supreme Court in Brown to be apposite. The just compensation due a client under the terms of the Illinois rule was zero. Therefore, there had been no violation of the Just Compensation Clause of the Fifth Amendment, and the trial court was not in error when it dismissed plaintiffs' complaint.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Kostusik


No. 1-05-1196


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


361 Ill. App. 3d 103; 836 N.E.2d 147; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 904; 296 Ill. Dec. 732

September 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 31, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 04 D 330661. Honorable Veronica B. Mathein, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Petition for leave to appeal granted; affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father petitioned for leave to appeal an interlocutory order entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which awarded temporary custody of the father's child to respondent mother, during the pendency of the parties dissolution of marriage proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Temporary custody of the child had initially been granted to the father. Custody was transferred to the mother pursuant to a motion filed by the child's representative. The motion indicated that the father was failing to cooperate in necessary providing the child with necessary therapeutic services. The court granted leave to appeal but affirmed the trial court's decision, holding that 1) the proper method for bringing an interlocutory appeal of a custody order was to follow the procedures in Ill. Ann. 5/506(a)(3) endowed a child's representative with the authority to file motions for changes in temporary custody; and 5) as the father never requested an evidentiary hearing on the motion filed by the child's representative, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/603(a) (2004) did not require that the court conduct one.


OUTCOME: The father's petition for leave to appeal was granted and the trial court's order was affirmed.

People v. Dixon


NO. 4-04-0381


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


359 Ill. App. 3d 938; 835 N.E.2d 925; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 944; 296 Ill. Dec. 572



September 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 19, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Dixon, 217 Ill. 2d 575, 844 N.E.2d 42, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 2050, 300 Ill. Dec. 370 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Dixon v. Pfister, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 49825 (N.D. Ill., Apr. 10, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 03CF1384. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted him on a jury verdict of guilty to first degree murder in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a)(1), (a)(2) (2002), and which sentenced him to 65 years' imprisonment after including a 25 year sentence enhancement under § 5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii) of the Unified Code of Corrections, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed the victim. The 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii) 25 year sentence enhancement was imposed for defendant's use of a firearm. On appeal, defendant challenged only the enhancement. He argued it did not apply to him because § 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii) required the firearm be discharged at a person other than the victim. He challenged § 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii) under the due process clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, under the proportionate penalties clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, and as an impermissible double enhancement. The plain language of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii) applied the enhancement when a firearm harmed anyone other than defendant, including the victim. The enhancement was consistent with, and furthered, the legislative goal of deterring gun violence, so it satisfied due process. A comparative proportionality review was inappropriate since the enhancement deterred gun violence in addition to murder, and defendant had no other proportionality argument. Since the firearm, and not the victim's death, triggered § 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii), there was no double enhancement to the existing enhancement for a first degree murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction and the 65 year sentence.

 

1282 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Green


1-04-0944


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


359 Ill. App. 3d 730; 835 N.E.2d 403; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 880; 296 Ill. Dec. 369



August 31, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 7, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 P 7243. Honorable Jane L. Stuart, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian ad litem (GAL) sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied pro se petitioner individual's petition to be appointed guardian of a 13-year-old minor.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was the biological father of the minor's half-sister. The minor had resided with petitioner and his sister for two years prior to the filing of the petition. Neither his biological mother or father were capable of or wanted to care for the minor. It was clear that the minor had benefitted from living with petitioner and he wanted petitioner as his guardian. The probate court agreed that appointment of petitioner as the guardian was in the minor's best interest. However, the petition was denied under 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-3(a) (2004) due to petitioner's felony conviction 10 years earlier. The court reversed. Courts in Illinois had the inherent authority under the common law to appoint guardians where doing so was in the best interests of a minor. Strict application of § 11-3(a) was not required where such application would lead to unjust consequences by forcing a probate court to ignore its own conclusion and subordinate a minor's interest to the generic criteria contained in § 11-3(a). As the probate court had done just that, its decision was against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The probate court's judgment was reversed and petitioner's application for appointment as the guardian of the minor was granted.

People v. Radford

August 11, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 21, 2005.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), affirmed defendant police pension board's denial of plaintiff claimant's application for a line-of-duty disability pension pursuant to 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-114.1 (2000). The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant filed an application with the police pension board for a line-of-duty disability pension pursuant to 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-114.1 (2000). After a hearing, the police pension board denied his application because, inter alia, he had failed to establish that he was disabled. DeLuna v. Burciaga


No. 1-03-1682


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


359 Ill. App. 3d 544; 834 N.E.2d 478; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 783; 295 Ill. Dec. 897



August 5, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 21, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Deluna v. Burciaga, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 963 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 8, 2005)
Rehearing denied by Deluna v. Burciaga, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 962 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 20, 2005)
Appeal granted by DeLuna v. Burciaga, 217 Ill. 2d 560, 844 N.E.2d 36, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 2042, 300 Ill. Dec. 364 (2005)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by DeLuna v. Burciaga, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1640 (Ill., Oct. 5, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 L 2085. Honorable Kathy Flanagan, Judge Presiding.
DeLuna v. St. Elizabeth's Hosp., 147 Ill. 2d 57, 588 N.E.2d 1139, 1992 Ill. LEXIS 27, 167 Ill. Dec. 1009 (1992)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, four children of a decedent, appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their legal malpractice action against defendant attorney because the complaint was filed after the repose period set forth in 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-214.3 (2000).


OVERVIEW: The attorney filed a medical malpractice action on behalf of the decedent's estate in 1986. He purposely failed to file an affidavit from a healthcare provider because the wanted to test the constitutionality of 735 Ill. Stat. Ann. 5/2-622 (2000). As expected the case was dismissed. The constitutionality of § 2-622 was ultimately upheld by the Illinois Supreme Court. The attorney's attempt at refiling a complaint on behalf of the children in 1996 was unsuccessful. The children filed their legal malpractice suit in 2000. The court reversed, holding that 1) the statute of repose applied to bar the instant action unless it had been tolled; 2) 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-214.3(e) (2000) did not toll the statute of repose; 3) the children's fourth amended complaint sufficiently pled fraudulent concealment by the attorney, as their fiduciary, of the cause of action against him, which tolled the statute of repose; and 4) the allegations in the fourth amended complaint adequately established a reasonable reliance by the children on the attorney's representations about the status of their case such that the attorney was equitably estopped from raising the statute of repose as a defense.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Malin


No. 2-04-0757


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


359 Ill. App. 3d 257; 833 N.E.2d 440; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 810; 295 Ill. Dec. 607



August 5, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 2, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Malin, 844 N.E.2d 44, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1928 (Ill., Dec. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 02-CF-517. Honorable Ward S. Arnold, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) following a partially negotiated guilty plea. Under the plea, defendant was convicted of four counts of reckless homicide, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3(a), (c)(1), (e-5) (2002) and was sentenced to four concurrent terms of 10 years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed, challenging the propriety of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed four people in a vehicle accident. When he was charged, § 9-3(e-5) elevated the offense to a Class 2 felony if two or more people were killed. Prior to sentencing, that portion of § 9-3 was removed from the statute. Similar language was added to the aggravated driving under the influence (DUI) statute, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501 (2002). Defendant argued that he should have been told he could be sentenced to a Class 3 felony under amended § 9-3. The court affirmed, holding that 1) defendant was actually attacking his plea agreement, in which he agreed to be sentenced for a Class 2 felony, and his failure to file a motion to withdraw his plea was fatal to his appeal; 2) defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to advise defendant he could be sentenced under either the old or new version of the reckless homicide statute as he continued to be subject to a Class 2 felony under the amended DUI statute; 3) the sentence was not based on improper aggravation; 4) Apprendi did not apply to the sentence; and 5) the trial court properly ruled that the sentence was subject to the truth-in-sentencing provisions of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1-1-1 et seq. (2002).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Wade v. City of N. Chi. Police Pension Bd.


No. 2-04-0047


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


359 Ill. App. 3d 224; 833 N.E.2d 427; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 793; 295 Ill. Dec. 594



August 3, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 2, 2005.
Appeal granted by Wade v. City of N. Chicago Police Pension Bd., 222 Ill. 2d 603, 861 N.E.2d 665, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1677, 308 Ill. Dec. 334 (2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by Wade v. City of N. Chicago Police Pension Bd., 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1694 (Ill., Nov. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 03--MR--987. Honorable Raymond J. McKoski, Judge, Presiding.
Wade v. City of N. Chicago Police Pension Bd., 215 Ill. 2d 620, 828 N.E.2d 282, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 716, 293 Ill. Dec. 312 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retired police officer appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) that, after remand, adhered to its original finding that defendant police pension board had properly interpreted 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-114.1 and 3-115 (2002) in denying him line-of-duty disability benefits because of his failure to present certifications from three physicians as to his disability.


OVERVIEW: The officer had pre-existing problems, but there was little doubt that his career-ending injury occurred in the line of duty. Two of the three physicians he consulted certified him as disabled in the line of duty. The third physician did not certify him as disabled at all. After instruction by the state's highest court, the trial court and the instant court considered whether the dissident physician's opinion was against the manifest weight of the evidence. They decided that it was. All the same, this did not change the result. Section 3-115 clearly required certifications from three physicians. There was nothing that stopped the officer from obtaining permission to seek a fourth opinion, and there was every likelihood that the fourth opinion would have found him disabled. But in the absence of three certifications, there was nothing a court could do to help. The legislative mandate was clear.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Myers


NO. 4-03-0757


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


359 Ill. App. 3d 341; 833 N.E.2d 421; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 789; 295 Ill. Dec. 588



August 2, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 31, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. No. 02CF181. Honorable Harold J. Frobish, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois), to a charge of child pornography, violating 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-20.1(a)(1)(vii) (2002)). He was sentenced to four years in prison. Defendant appealed, arguing that, as applied to him, the mandatory minimum four-year sentence for child pornography was unconstitutional because it violated the proportionate-penalties clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with child pornography after he photographed his 13-year-old stepdaughter in a pose involving a lewd exhibition of her unclothed genitals and buttocks. On appeal, defendant contended that (1) his four-year prison sentence was "wholly disproportionate" to the offense he committed and (2) the offense of child pornography violated the proportionate-penalties clause when compared to the similar offense of sexual exploitation of a child, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-9.1(a-5) (2002). The court disagreed. The victim had suffered serious psychological injuries even though she suffered no physical injury, and the fact that defendant committed the offense against a member of his family made his actions even more serious. Considering the ongoing psychological issues that were affecting the victim, the court concluded that the statutorily mandated statute was not grossly disproportional to an offense that shocked the moral sense of the community. Further, as child pornography contained an element not found in the sexual exploitation statute, photographing the victim, the two statutes did not have identical elements and different sentences could be imposed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

People v. Bernice T. (In re S.F.)


No. 1-04-1231


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


359 Ill. App. 3d 63; 834 N.E.2d 453; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 750; 295 Ill. Dec. 872



August 1, 2005, Decided  
August 1, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 21, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96 JA 4026. Honorable Rena Marie Van Tine, Judge Presiding.
In re S.F., 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 969 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 21, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which terminated her parental rights to her minor son under § 1(D)(f) of the Illinois Adoption Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(f) (1998). The mother challenged the constitutionality of § 1(D)(f).


OVERVIEW: The mother was found unfit under § 1(D)(f) based on her conviction for the death of another of her children by physical child abuse. Section 1(D)(f) did not provide for any rebuttal of the presumption that subsection created that the mother was unfit. Based on a prior ruling by the Illinois Supreme Court that § 1(D)(q) violated the equal protection clause, the court ruled that § 1(D)(f) was also unconstitutional. Both subsections denied a parent any right of rebuttal of the presumption of unfitness, while a finding of unfitness under § 1(D)(i)(2), which dealt with convictions for first or second degree murder, was rebuttable. There was no apparent reason for the difference in the two procedural safeguards and thus, an equal protection violation existed.


OUTCOME: The termination order was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Magnus v. Dep't of Prof'l Regulation


No. 1-03-0732


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


359 Ill. App. 3d 773; 835 N.E.2d 77; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 742; 296 Ill. Dec. 222



July 29, 2005, Decided  
July 29, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 7, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Magnus v. Dep't Prof'l Regulation, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1023 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John K. Madden, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff clinical social worker sought administrative review to reverse an Illinois Department of Professional Regulation decision that suspended his license 60 days and placed him on probation based on the Department's determination that he exhibited professional incompetence and committed malpractice. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied administrative review and affirmed the Department's decision. The social worker appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Director of the Department determined that the social worker violated 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 20/19(1)(e) and (f) of the Clinical Social Work and Social Work Practice Act by encouraging a client's adolescent sexual activity with other minors, instructing the client on sexual technique, and failing to report the client's sexual activity. On appeal, the social worker claimed that the Department's determination was clearly erroneous. The appeals court found that under the holding in In re T.W. and the definition of "abused child" in 325 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3 of the Abused and Neglected Child Reporting Act, 325 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1 et seq. (1998), the clinical social worker's client and the other minors with whom the client engaged in consensual sex could all be considered to be abused children. This fact could then trigger the requirements of the Reporting Act, compelling the social worker to report the client's sexual activity to the Department. Contrary to the social worker's claim, nothing in the Practice Act required that the charge against him specifically allege that he was mentally or physically impaired before he could be required to submit to an examination.


OUTCOME: The decision upholding the Department's finding that the social worker violated the Practice Act was reversed. The matter was remanded to determine whether the client or other minors were to be considered an "abused children" under the Reporting Act and, if so, whether the social worker was required to report the client's sexual activities. The Department was to consider whether the parties should be allowed to present new evidentiary matters.

Lapp v. Vill. of Winnetka


No. 1-04-1920


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed a complaint challenging Winnetka, Ill., Mun. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered an order and memorandum opinion granting defendants' motions for summary judgment, denying plaintiffs' cross-motions, and entering judgment for defendants. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Beauchamp v. Zimmerman

July 21, 2005, Modified Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 8, 2005.

Appeal denied by Beauchamp v. Zimmerman, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1969 (Ill., Dec. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 L 7503. Honorable Susan Zwick, Judge Presiding.
Beauchamp v. Zimmerman, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 642 (Ill. App. Ct., June 30, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff patient's petition for relief from judgment pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2002) in the patient's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: The patient's original complaint was filed without a 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-622(a)(1) (2002) affidavit and health professional report. That complaint was voluntarily dismissed. It was refiled pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-217 (2002), again without an affidavit and report. The case was dismissed for want of prosecution (DWP) when the patient, who was acting pro se at the time, failed to appear at a status conference. The patient then filed the 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2002) petition. The court reversed. To obtain relief under § 2-1401, the patient had to show that he had a meritorious claim. As he had never filed the required affidavit and health professional report, he had not established a meritorious medical malpractice claim. Thus, the trial court's grant of § 2-1401 relief was an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order.

People v. Banks


No. 1-04-0801


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


358 Ill. App. 3d 924; 833 N.E.2d 928; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 697; 295 Ill. Dec. 722



July 20, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 8, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Eddie A. Stephens, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted after a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on a charge of delivery of a controlled substance. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged after a police officer observed him delivering what turned out to be cocaine to another individual. The cocaine was recovered from that individual. At trial, the parties stipulated that a proper chain of custody was maintained at all times of the item recovered and that a forensic chemist would testify that the item did in fact test positive for cocaine. After defendant was convicted, he was ordered to submit a DNA sample pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002). Defendant argued the stipulation violated his right to confrontation and that § 5-4-3 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed. Defense counsel could waive defendant's right to confrontation so long as defendant did not object and the waiver was part of sound trial strategy. Defendant had not voiced an objection, and trial counsel's decision to enter into the stipulation in order to concentrate on other aspects of the case was a sound decision. The purpose of § 5-4-3 was to create a database of recidivist criminal offenders, and it had been repeatedly upheld as constitutional under the balancing test.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

People v. Peacock


NO. 4-03-0605


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


359 Ill. App. 3d 326; 833 N.E.2d 396; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 775; 295 Ill. Dec. 563



July 19, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 16, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 02CF1816. Honorable Jeffrey B. Ford, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part as modified and judgment vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) convicting him on jury verdict of home invasion in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(a)(2) (2002), aggravated battery in violation in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-4(b) (2002), and domestic battery in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-3.2(a)(1) (2002) and imposing extended sentences for the latter two offenses.


OVERVIEW: The charges arose out of defendant's invasion of a former girlfriend's home and his administration of a savage beating upon her. The court held, first, that since aggravated battery, involving a deadly weapon, and domestic battery, which required a prior conviction as charged as well as a victim who was a household member, were distinct offenses, conviction on all three charges did not violate the one-act, one-crime rule. It was improper, however, for the trial court to have enhanced the sentences for the battery offenses since they were part of the same series of acts as the most serious offense, the home invasion. The domestic battery statute was not unconstitutionally vague in adopting a definition of "family or household member" that included persons whom a defendant had formerly dated because the definition was readily understandable without any time limit. Defendant's post-verdict, pre-sentence letter to the trial judge was sufficient to establish a pro se motion for a new trial based on ineffective assistance of counsel, so that motion should not have been denied without a preliminary investigation into the claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, modified the judgment to allow credit for defendant's presentence confinement, remanded with directions to issue a written amendment of judgment to that effect, vacated the extended term sentences for aggravated battery and domestic battery and reduced those sentences to the maximum non-extended terms, and directed the trial court after remand to investigate defendant's counsel ineffectiveness claims.

 

1296 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Klebba v. O'Connor (In re Estate of Phillips)


No. 1-03-3685


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT


359 Ill. App. 3d 114; 833 N.E.2d 895; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 687; 295 Ill. Dec. 689



July 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 9, 2005. Released for Publication September 8, 2005.
Appeal denied by Klebba v. O'Connor (In re Estate of Phillips), 844 N.E.2d 38, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1842 (Ill., Dec. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 P 8475. Honorable Robert E. Cusack, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nephew sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee estate administrator on the nephew's petition to admit a lost or destroyed will to probate of the decedent, the nephew's uncle. A 1965 will had been filed for probate.


OVERVIEW: The nephew presented a copy of the decedent's 1987 will, indicating that the original was no longer accessible because it was last seen when it was sent to a bank for safekeeping, and the bank's files and records had been subsequently seized by the federal government. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment, holding that 1) the only competent evidence concerning the custody of the 1987 will came from the decedent's secretary, who stated it was last seen in the decedent's possession; 2) as the original could not be found, the presumption was that the decedent had destroyed the 1987 will; 3) testimony from the nephew about what transpired at a photocopier after the secretary last saw the will was barred by the Dead Man's Act, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/8-201(a) (2002); 4) evidence about the settlement of a claim against the estate was irrelevant to the case; 5) no other competent admissible evidence existed that could establish an issue of material fact; and 6) under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/8-501 (2002), the nephew could not disclaim his interest under the 1987 will in order to testify as to what transpired at the photocopier.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed.

 

1297 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Raymond C.S. (In re R.S.)


No. 3-04-0140


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


358 Ill. App. 3d 781; 833 N.E.2d 885; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 684; 295 Ill. Dec. 679



July 11, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 24, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Whiteside County, Illinois. No. 00--JA--14. Honorable Vicki Wright and Honorable Timothy Slavin Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Whiteside County, Illinois, which found him to be an unfit parent and terminated his parental rights. The father argued that the trial court erred when it found him unfit pursuant to § 1(D)(q) of the Adoption Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(q) (2002), because that provision was violative of equal protection and due process.


OVERVIEW: The State sought to terminate the father's parental rights to three children. The State alleged, inter alia, that he had been convicted of aggravated battery of a child. The State moved for summary judgment, alleging that the father's aggravated battery conviction rendered him an unfit parent as a matter of law pursuant to 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(q) (2002). The trial court granted the motion. The Illinois Supreme Court had determined that there was no rational basis for treating persons subject to fitness proceedings under § 1(D)(q) differently from those facing the same proceedings under § 1(D)(i). Accordingly, it held that § 1(D)(q) was unconstitutional as violative of equal protection. The court also held that the proper remedy for that constitutional violation was to extend the opportunity to rebut to persons subject to § 1(D)(q) proceedings. The appellate court held that since the trial court granted the State's motion for summary judgment without affording the father the opportunity to rebut the presumption of unfitness arising from his aggravated battery of a child conviction, he was denied equal protection of the law.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1298 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


XLP Corp. v. County of Lake


No. 2-04-0255


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


359 Ill. App. 3d 239; 832 N.E.2d 480; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 724; 295 Ill. Dec. 329



July 8, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 12, 2005.
Appeal denied by XLP Corp. v. County of Lake, 844 N.E.2d 48, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1715 (Ill., 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Xlp Corp. v. Lake County, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3899 (U.S., May 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 98-CH-1106. Honorable Raymond J. McKoski, Judge, Presiding.
XLP Corp. v. County of Lake, 317 Ill. App. 3d 881, 743 N.E.2d 162, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 1040, 252 Ill. Dec. 588 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the owners of three adult entertainment establishments and one such establishment, appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which upheld the constitutionality of Lake County, Ill. Ordinance 6:1-15 (eff. October 9, 2001). The ordinance regulated adult establishments within defendant Lake County.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance required the establishments to obtain a license, limited their hours of operation, prohibited nude dancing, set out setback limitations for dancers, and prohibited anyone under 21 years of age from being on an establishment's premises. Plaintiffs argued the ordinance violated the First and Fourteenth Amendments. The court affirmed, holding that 1) as the ordinance did not give the County "unbridled discretion" to grant or deny license applications, the ordinance did not constitute an unconstitutional prior restraint on speech; 2) as the ordinance did not ban all adult establishments, it was properly analyzed as a time, place, or manner restriction; 3) in enacting the ordinance, the County relied on both studies of the effects of adult establishments conducted elsewhere and information received from law enforcement representatives, and therefore, the ordinance was content-neutral; 4) the evidence at trial showed that the ordinance served a substantial government interest and also showed a nexus between the ordinance and the harm it sought to alleviate; and 5) plaintiffs argument regarding the age restriction in the ordinance was waived.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1299 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Horvath v. White


No. 1-03-1726


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


358 Ill. App. 3d 844; 832 N.E.2d 366; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 632; 295 Ill. Dec. 215



June 30, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 12, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CH 8673. Honorable Richard J. Billik, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the holder of an Illinois license, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld an order of defendant Illinois Secretary of State that suspended plaintiff's driver's license pursuant to recommendations and findings issued by defendant hearing officer. Plaintiff challenged the constitutionality of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-206(a)(10) (2000).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's license was suspended after he was arrested for public intoxication in Iowa and was found to be in possession of his older brother's Illinois identification card. The older brother was above the legal drinking age, but plaintiff was not. Plaintiff alleged that § 6-206(a)(10) violated his right to due process and that his simple possession of the card created an unconstitutional presumption that he intended to use the identification card for purposes of obtaining alcohol. The court affirmed holding that § 6-206(a)(10): (1) did not violate due process because it was rationally related to the State's interest in fostering safe and legal operation of motor vehicles; (2) was not unconstitutional on its face and was not applied unconstitutionally to plaintiff; and (3) did not violate Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970). Further, the hearing officer's decision in the case was not against the manifest weight of the evidence where the evidence established that plaintiff was not of legal drinking age, he was intoxicated when arrested, he was in possession of the identification card during a time he was illegally consuming alcohol, and he held a valid Illinois driver's license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment and the Secretary's order.

 

1300 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jackson


1-03-1489


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


358 Ill. App. 3d 927; 832 N.E.2d 418; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 670; 295 Ill. Dec. 267



June 30, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 8, 2005. Released for Publication August 12, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Jackson, 844 N.E.2d 43, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1784 (Ill., Dec. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Mary Maxwell Thomas, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of violating the Illinois Harmful Materials statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-21 (2002). He argued that the statute was unconstitutional and that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was employed at a residential treatment center for teen-aged boys. He brought a purported sports video into the center that turned out to show defendant engaged in sex acts with various women. One of the women shouted out a greeting to the boys at the center in one of the episodes. Except for a few seconds the first time one boy viewed the tape, the evidence indicated that the boys viewed the tape, which defendant had not removed, when defendant was not present. The court held, first, that there was no First Amendment violation, in part because the usual standards for determining whether material was obscene did not apply in the case of reasonable exercises of the police power to protect minors. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague either, since the phrases it used, such as "prurient interest," had already been approved as sufficiently precise in decisions of the highest courts in both Illinois and the nation. Finally, the evidence was sufficient to support conviction even though defendant had not been present for most of the viewings since he knew he had brought the video to the center, did not remove it, and had one of the participants greet the boy viewers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1301 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hunter


NO. 4-03-0957


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


358 Ill. App. 3d 1085; 831 N.E.2d 1192; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 673; 294 Ill. Dec. 867



June 30, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 1, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Hunter, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 748 (Ill., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Vermilion County. No. 02CF550. Honorable Craig H. DeArmond, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of possession of a substance containing cocaine and sentenced him to probation with various terms and conditions. One condition was that he submit to genetic testing pursuant to § 5-4-3(a)(3.5) of the Unified Code of Corrections, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3(a)(3.5) (2002) (as amended by 2001 Ill. Laws 829), at his own expense and pay a $ 200 analysis fee. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the compulsory extraction and storing of his deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) violated the Sixth Amendment and that the trial court lacked authority to order him to pay the cost of DNA collection in addition to the analysis fee. The appeals court found that as a convicted felon sentenced to probation, defendant had a diminished expectation of privacy and agreed with courts that applied the balancing test when reviewing the constitutionality of § 5-4-3(a)(3.5). Collection and cataloguing of DNA assisted the State in identifying repeat offenders who could conceal or alter their identity and could assist the State in solving past and future crimes. Thus, the State had a compelling interest in genetic-marker collection of felons. Because the State's interest outweighed a convicted felon's diminished privacy rights and due to the fact that DNA sampling was only minimally intrusive, § 5-4-3(a)(3.5) did not violate the Fourth Amendment's prohibition against unreasonable searches and seizures. However, until the statute was amended, trial courts were limited to imposing the $ 200 analysis fee under § 5-4-3(j) of the Unified Code (730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3(j) (2002)).


OUTCOME: The requirement that defendant submit to genetic testing was found constitutional. However, the trial court lacked the authority to order defendant to pay the cost of DNA collection. The case was remanded with directions to modify the order of probation to vacate the condition that defendant pay the cost of DNA collection.

People v. Traynoff (In re Traynoff)


No. 2-01-0880


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


358 Ill. App. 3d 430; 831 N.E.2d 709; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 638; 294 Ill. Dec. 759



June 28, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 29, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 98-MR-456. Honorable Philip L. DiMarzio, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Traynoff (In re Traynoff), 338 Ill. App. 3d 949, 789 N.E.2d 865, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 574, 273 Ill. Dec. 691 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court found that sufficient evidence existed that respondent was a sexually violent person. After the court remanded the case to the trial court with directions to conduct a Frye hearing to determine the admissibility of the actuarial instruments used to measure the likelihood of reoffense, the Supreme Court of Illinois directed the court to vacate its opinion and reconsider its judgment in light of its decision in In re Commitment of Simons.


OVERVIEW: Based on expert testimony, the trial court concluded that respondent suffered from mental disorders that made it substantially probable that he would engage in acts of sexual violence. The court went beyond what Varner had interpreted Crane to require. Thus, there was no due process violation, and respondent's constitutional challenge to the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 et seq. (1998), failed. All three experts agreed that respondent suffered from paraphilia not otherwise specified and posed a moderate to high risk to reoffend. This testimony, in conjunction with respondent's refusal to undergo treatment, his denial of self-blame, and his placing blame on the victim, established that he lacked the ability to control his sexually violent behavior. Compelling him to submit to an evaluation did not violate his 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/25(c)(2) (1998) right to remain silent. In light of Simons, holding that actuarial risk assessment had gained general acceptance in the psychological and psychiatric communities and was therefore admissible, the trial court properly admitted the expert testimony of two psychologists.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Cannon


No. 1-04-0094


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


358 Ill. App. 3d 313; 832 N.E.2d 312; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 622; 295 Ill. Dec. 161



June 27, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 12, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Cannon, 223 Ill. 2d 644, 865 N.E.2d 971, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 509, 310 Ill. Dec. 251 (2007)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied, Motion granted by United States ex rel. Cannon v. Hardy, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 66391 (N.D. Ill., June 22, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 18290. Honorable Daniel P. Darcy, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him guilty of 12 counts of predatory criminal sexual assault, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and aggravated criminal sexual abuse, with the lesser offenses merging into the greater, as well as counts of sexual exploitation of a child and unlawful restraint, and sentenced him to natural life in prison.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10 (2002), which allowed for the introduction of the victim's statements to third persons at his trial, was unconstitutional on its face and that the wrongfully admitted statements resulted in his conviction. The appellate court concluded that 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10(b)(1) and (b)(2)(A) interacted to specifically provide that a victim's hearsay statements should be admitted only when there were sufficient safeguards of reliability surrounding the statements and the victim actually testified at trial. Thus, in requiring the appearance of the victim at trial, the statutory procedure was wholly consistent with the holding of Crawford and, in and of itself, suffered no constitutional impediment. The appellate court found 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10(b)(2)(A) to be severable from any other allegedly unconstitutional provisions in 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10. In addition, defendant's confession corroborated the victim's account of the sexual abuse, and these sources of evidence alone provided overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Andrews


No. 2-03-0959


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


358 Ill. App. 3d 744; 831 N.E.2d 66; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 617; 294 Ill. Dec. 543



June 22, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 22, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Andrews, 217 Ill. 2d 569, 844 N.E.2d 40, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1755, 300 Ill. Dec. 368 (2005)
Appeal denied by People v. Andrews, 217 Ill. 2d 569, 838 N.E.2d 3, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1764, 297 Ill. Dec. 516 (2005)
Appeal denied by, Vacated by, Remanded by People v. Andrews, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1107 (Ill., Jan. 25, 2006)
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at People v. Andrews, 364 Ill. App. 3d 253, 845 N.E.2d 974, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 228, 301 Ill. Dec. 109 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 02-CF-2360. Honorable Timothy Q. Sheldon, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) convicting him of aggravated vehicular hijacking while carrying a firearm in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-4(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-4(a)(4). The first trial ended in a mistrial and defendant objected. Defendant was retried and convicted. Defendant appealed first contending that the second trial violated his double jeopardy rights under the United States and Illinois Constitutions. The court noted that where a mistrial was declared over defendant's objection, retrial was permitted where there was a manifest necessity for declaring the mistrial. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding a manifest necessity for a mistrial because the jury could not collectively agree, they deliberated for a sufficient period of time, the trial was sufficiently long, the issues presented to the jury were not complex, the judge properly communicated with the jury, and further deliberations would have been exhausting and coercive in nature. Therefore, retrial did not offend defendant's double jeopardy rights. Defendant also argued that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-4(a)(4) was unconstitutional. The court held, however, that the crime charged did not exist at the time of defendant's trial, thus reversal of the conviction was mandated.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and remanded.

People v. Carrie


NO. 5-03-0422


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


358 Ill. App. 3d 805; 832 N.E.2d 863; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 604; 295 Ill. Dec. 413



June 16, 2005, Decision Filed


NOTICE:

 [***1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lawrence County. No. 02-CF-61. Honorable Robert M. Hopkins, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lawrence County (Illinois) convicting defendant of two counts of threatening a public official in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-9(a) (2002).


OVERVIEW: After defendant was arrested for a domestic disturbance, he threatened a municipal police officer and a county dispatcher who was acting as a correctional officer. Defendant was improperly convicted of two counts of threatening a public official because the police officer and dispatcher did not hold positions created by statute as required under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-9(b)(1) (2002). A statute creating the office had to expressly create the office. A statute or ordinance creating a department or department head was insufficient to create a subordinate office. The record did not reflect any statute or ordinance that expressly created the offices of the municipal police officer, the county dispatcher, or the county correctional officer. While 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/10-2.1-4 (2002) provided for the appointment of municipal police officer by a board of police commissioners, the statute did not expressly create the office of the municipal police officer for the municipality at issue. Likewise, none of the statutes cited by the State created the offices of dispatcher and correctional officer for the county at issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Alhambra-Grantfork Tel. Co. v. Ill. Commerce Comm'n


NO. 5-04-0333


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


358 Ill. App. 3d 818; 832 N.E.2d 869; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 605; 295 Ill. Dec. 419



June 16, 2005, Decision Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Alhambra-Grantfork Tel. Co. v. Ill. Commerce Comm'n, 844 N.E.2d 35, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1722 (Ill., Dec. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Illinois Commerce Commission. No. 04-0040.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Commerce Commission (state commerce commission) entered an order that cancelled petitioner telephone company's wireless termination tariff on the grounds that the telephone company failed to give proper notice of the tariff to affected commercial mobile radio service telecommunications carriers. The telephone company petitioned for review of the state commerce commission's order.


OVERVIEW: The state commerce commission entered a decision that canceled the telephone company's wireless termination tariff on the grounds that the telephone company failed to give proper, actual notice of the tariff to affected customers known as commercial mobile radio service telecommunications (CMRS) carriers. On appeal, the telephone company claimed that the CMRS carriers were not customers entitled to individual notice of its proposed tariff. It also argued that the Illinois Administrative Code and state statutory law, which allowed out-of-state attorneys to petition to appear pro hac vice in state commerce commission proceedings, impermissibly encroached on the powers of the state judiciary. The appellate court rejected both claims. It found that since the tariff would change the rates for the CMRS carriers, actual notice was required pursuant to Ill. Admin. Code tit. 83, § 745.110(c)(1). It also found that neither the Illinois Administrative Code provision nor the state statutory provision allowing out-of-state attorneys to appear before the state commerce commission were unconstitutional, as the state commerce commission had the discretionary authority to permit them to appear.


OUTCOME: The state commerce commission's order was affirmed.

People v. Taylor


No. 2-01-0494


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


357 Ill. App. 3d 1033; 830 N.E.2d 855; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 593; 294 Ill. Dec. 443

Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 et seq. (2000). Defendant had pled guilty to the charge of aggravated criminal sexual assault in 1992 and was sentenced to 18 years' imprisonment.

Du Page County Airport Auth. v. Dep't of Revenue


Nos. 2-04-0769 & 2-04-0770 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


358 Ill. App. 3d 476; 831 N.E.2d 30; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 595; 294 Ill. Dec. 507



June 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 20, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Du Page County Airport Auth. v. Dep't of Revenue, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 733 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., July 20, 2005)
Appeal denied by DuPage County Airport Auth. v. Dep't of Revenue, 844 N.E.2d 36, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1859 (Ill., Dec. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 03-MR-1208. Honorable Edward R. Duncan, Jr., Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Department of Revenue, its director, a county board of review, and school, park, library, and fire protection districts, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) reversing a decision of the Department and ruling that certain property belonging to plaintiff Du Page County Airport Authority fulfilled an airport authority purpose and was thus tax exempt.


OVERVIEW: The Authority owned, operated, and maintained a general aviation airport and owned property leased to various tenants, including private, for-profit, commercial entities. The appeal involved 65 tax parcels, which the Authority claimed were exempt under § 15-160 of the Property Tax Code (Code), 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/15-160 (2000), as fulfilling an "Airport Authority purpose." The trial court concluded that an amendment to the Airport Authorities Act (Act), 70 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1 et seq. (2000), changed the definition of "Airport Authority purpose." However, the appeals court, in considering the Code, did not believe that a Code amendment evinced a clear intent on the legislature's part to overrule the holding of Harrisburg-Raleigh Airport Authority that private leases that fulfilled an airport purpose could be exempt under the Code. After considering the language of the Code and the Act (as amended), the appeals court concluded that the legislature did not intend to change the definition of "Airport Authority purposes" from that articulated in Harrisburg. It was clear that the disputed property did not meet the standard for "Airport Authority purposes" under the Code.


OUTCOME: The appeals court reversed the order of the trial court ruling that the Authority was entitled to a tax exemption for all the disputed property.

People v. Cordero


No. 2-03-0702


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


358 Ill. App. 3d 121; 830 N.E.2d 830; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 586; 294 Ill. Dec. 418



June 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 15, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. Nos. 01-DT-4519, 01-TR-142078. Honorable Patrick N. Lawler and Thomas R. Smoker, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the denial of his motion to quash his arrest and suppress evidence, defendant stipulated to a bench trial. The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of driving under the influence (DUI), 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501(a)(2) (2000) and operating an uninsured vehicle, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-707 (2000), imposed concurrent terms of conditional discharge, and fined defendant a total of $ 1,250.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was illegally seized. Defendant argues that the officer's activation of her squad car's lights removed her actions from the realm of her community caretaking function, thereby requiring a reasonable suspicion in order to justify her stop of defendant. The appellate court noted that there was nothing in the record to suggest that the officer's stop of defendant's vehicle was justified on any basis other than reasonable suspicion. The officer did not testify that she observed the car drive off rapidly or recklessly, but merely that it began to pull up, whereupon she activated her lights and stopped it. The officer indicated that the mere presence of the car in the parking lot after hours led her to suspect criminal activity. The appellate court held that, under the circumstances, the officer lacked a reasonable and articulable basis to justify her decision to perform a Terry stop. Thus, the trial court should have granted defendant's motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence. The appellate court further concluded that the State would have been unable to prove defendant's guilty without the fruits of the stop.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed.

 

1310 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brown


No. 1-03-3078


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


358 Ill. App. 3d 56; 831 N.E.2d 24; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 568; 294 Ill. Dec. 501



June 8, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 14, 2005.
Appeal granted by People v. Brown, 217 Ill. 2d 572, 844 N.E.2d 41, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1698, 300 Ill. Dec. 369 (2005)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Cause remanded by People v. Brown, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 449 (Ill., Apr. 5, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 98 CR 6579. Honorable William G. Lacy, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which summarily dismissed as frivolous and patently without merit the inmate's second postconviction petition.


OVERVIEW: The inmate entered a negotiated guilty plea to attempted first degree murder of a peace officer after his juvenile case was transferred to adult court. Subsequently, 1994 Ill. Laws 680, which added the transfer statute, 705 Ill. Stat. Ann. 405/5-4 (3.3) (1996), and amended the sentencing statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/8-4 (1996), was held unconstitutional. The circuit court dismissed the petition, finding that the inmate's sentence was appropriate even though the sentencing statute had been held to be void. The circuit court did not address the inmate's claims that he had a right to a new transfer hearing and trial. The inmate argued that as the transfer and sentencing statutes were void, so were his transfer hearing, his plea, and his sentence. The court agreed. Because 1994 Ill. Laws 680 had been ruled unconstitutional, the judgment had to be voided, and the case remanded to the juvenile court. On remand, the presumptive transfer provisions of 1997 Ill. Laws 590, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5-805(2)(b) (2002), would be applied. Application of the statute to the inmate's case would not violate the ex post facto clauses in U.S. Const. art. I, §§10 and Ill. Const. art. I, § 16 (1970).


OUTCOME: The court vacated the inmate's conviction and remanded the case, with instructions, for a new transfer hearing.

 

1311 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Huseman v. Barton (In re Huseman)


NO. 5-03-0563


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


358 Ill. App. 3d 299; 831 N.E.2d 1147; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 580; 294 Ill. Dec. 822



June 7, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Perry County. No. 01-P-33. Honorable Lloyd A. Karmeier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed from stipulated orders entered by the Circuit Court of Perry County (Illinois). The orders appealed from were agreed to by the mother and petitioner father, the mother's ex-husband. The orders found the parties' adult child to be disabled, ordered that attorney fees be paid from the daughter's social security disability benefits, and mandated joint custody and visitation.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the daughter's disability benefits were exempt under 42 U.S.C.S. § 407(a) from the claims of the daughter's creditors and, therefore, could not be used to pay her attorney or guardian ad litem (GAL). The mother also argued that the parties could not stipulate that the daughter was disabled or to the trial court's authority to award visitation. The court disagreed. While § 407(a) protected the disability payments from attachment, garnishment, or other legal process, it did not extend to situations in which the person receiving the benefits voluntarily agreed to the payments. All of the parties, including the GAL, the mother as guardian of the daughter's person, and the father as guardian of the daughter's estate, had agreed to the payments. Further, the appointment of the GAL and the daughter's attorney had been in her best interests. The parties' stipulations regarding the daughter's disability and visitation were in the nature of a consent decree. They could not be amended or varied without the consent of all of the parties unless they were contrary to public policy. That being the case, the court declined to find them unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Dobbs


NO. 5-03-0644


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


358 Ill. App. 3d 308; 831 N.E.2d 1154; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 582; 294 Ill. Dec. 829



June 7, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. No. 90-D-62. Honorable E. Kyle Vantrease, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (Illinois), which held her in indirect civil contempt for her interference with visitation between her Down's syndrome daughter and respondent father, in violation of the parties' 1991 divorce decree, and which required that the daughter continue visitation with the father.


OVERVIEW: The daughter was 38 years old. At the hearing, the mother testified that the daughter no longer wanted to visit with the father, that she was doing nothing to discourage the daughter from participating in visitation, and that she would like the daughter to maintain a relationship with the father. The mother testified that she was willing to make the daughter available for visitation anytime the daughter wished to visit with the father but that she did not want to force the daughter to do so. The trial court found that the mother's denial of visitation was wilful and without cause or provocation. The court held that the order of visitation was void because the daughter was 24 years old at the time and the trial court had no jurisdiction over a child who had reached the age of majority. In turn, the mother could not have been held in contempt for violating a void order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order.

 

1313 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jennings


No. 1-03-3207


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


364 Ill. App. 3d 473; 846 N.E.2d 934; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 551; 301 Ill. Dec. 331



June 2, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CR 20215. Honorable William S. Wood, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of possession with intent to deliver cocaine and heroin and sentenced to concurrent prison terms of seven and four years. He appealed from both his convictions and sentences, contending, among other things, that the State's evidence was insufficient to support his convictions and that the trial court relied on improper evidence in finding him guilty.


OVERVIEW: The trial court heard unchallenged testimony of an officer and a forensic scientist as to the chain of custody. Defendant stipulated to that testimony and, by consenting to its admission, could not object to its admission for the first time on appeal. The forensic scientist's stipulated testimony did not lack an adequate foundation. The evidence was sufficient to support his conviction as defendant was observed retrieving a small object from a bag and handing it to another individual in exchange for cash. A bag containing individual packets of cocaine and cash were found on his person, and he was observed dropping another bag containing 25 individual packets of a suspected controlled substance. It was not unreasonable for the trial court to infer that defendant intended to deliver the narcotics found in his possession, and the evidence adequately supported such an inference. However, because there was no indication from the record that the parties agreed to a specific sentence, the State and defendant were without authority to waive the written presentence investigation report requirement, and the trial court was without authority to accept their purported waiver.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court as to defendant's convictions was affirmed, but his sentences were vacated and remanded for a new sentencing hearing in accordance with the appeals court's instructions.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 86 CR 16841. Honorable James B. Linn, Judge Presiding.
People v. Sargent, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1187 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 30, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that summarily dismissed petitioner's postconviction petition for relief at the second stage of postconviction review. Petitioner had been seeking relief from his conviction for first-degree murder after a jury found him guilty. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was sentenced to 80 years in prison after he was found guilty by a jury of first-degree murder. His direct appeal was then denied. Several years later, he filed a postconviction petition for relief and alleged that the sentence in his case violated the recent Apprendi decision. The trial court allowed the petition to proceed to the second stage of review. It then summarily dismissed the petition on the ground that retroactive application of Apprendi was barred where direct appeals had been exhausted as of the date of the Apprendi decision. The appellate court found that even if those provisions were violated, the violations amounted to no more than harmless error because petitioner could not show prejudice due to the fact that in any event, his Apprendi claim was barred due to the fact that he had exhausted his appeals before Apprendi had been decided.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.
