People v. Sole


No. 1-03-1701


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


357 Ill. App. 3d 988; 831 N.E.2d 18; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 521; 294 Ill. Dec. 495



May 26, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 14, 2005.
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Sole, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 605, 2012 IL App (1st) 92798U (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Thomas M. Davy, Judge Presiding.
People v. Sole, 215 Ill. 2d 615, 833 N.E.2d 8, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 921, 295 Ill. Dec. 526 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (UUW) in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6 (2002) and sentencing him to 14 years in prison. He argued that the aggravated UUW statute violated substantive due process and Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, and that his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated UUW after being found with a loaded weapon by police investigating citizen reports of a person pointing a weapon at cars. Adhering to previously decided case law, the court found no due process violation in the aggravated UUW statute because it provided for a level of scienter--knowing action--and the enhanced penalties it allowed bore a rational relationship to the evils the statute sought to prevent. Although the statute criminalizing reckless discharge of a firearm provided for far less severe penalties, there was no violation of the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, because the two statutes had very different purposes as well as distinct levels of required scienter. Defendant also argued that the trial court had abused its discretion in giving his failure to show up at his sentencing hearing undue weight in imposing sentence. The court did not have to resolve that issue because it found that defendant's prior felony history, which had also been considered, more than justified an enhanced sentence under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2 (2002).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Reynolds


NO. 5-03-0493


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


358 Ill. App. 3d 286; 831 N.E.2d 1103; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 511; 294 Ill. Dec. 778



May 24, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by People v. Reynolds, 216 Ill. 2d 722, 839 N.E.2d 1034, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1502, 298 Ill. Dec. 387 (2005)
Affirmed by People v. McCarty, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1649 (Ill., Oct. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. No. 01-CF-405. Honorable Patrick L. Duke, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of unlawful manufacture of more than 900 grams of a substance containing methamphetamine, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/401(a)(6.5)(D) (2000), and unlawful possession of more than 30 grams of cannabis with intent to deliver, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 550/5(d) (2000). The Circuit Court of Marion County (Illinois) sentenced him to 15 years for manufacturing and 5 years for possession, to run concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In response to defendant's arguments as to the validity of the search warrant, the appellate court found that there was sufficient probable cause to support issuance of the warrant based on the informant's testimony that he tried to buy drugs from another person and saw that person making methamphetamine. While the affidavit and warrant did not list the specific postal address of the premises, the search was executed at the correct location. Thus, the warrant sufficiently described the place to be searched. The appellate court further concluded that the items listed in the warrant were easily identified by a trained officer as contraband and thus, the descriptions were sufficient to satisfy the particularity requirement. Defendant's ineffective assistance claim failed due to the fact that the warrant was of sufficient particularity such that any failure to challenge the warrant would have been futile. Finally, the appellate court concluded that a reasonable inference of intent to deliver was derived from the fact that the police discovered more than 30 grams of marijuana, money in a locked box, scales, a walkie-talkie, two hand-held police scanners, and drug paraphernalia.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Mercury Indem. Co. v. Kim


No. 1-04-1808


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


358 Ill. App. 3d 1; 830 N.E.2d 603; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 513; 294 Ill. Dec. 191



May 23, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 14, 2005.
Appeal denied by Mercury Indem. Co. v. Kim, 844 N.E.2d 39, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1687 (Ill., Dec. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 CH 201. Honorable Stephen A. Schiller, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife, individually and as special administrator of the estate of her late husband, appealed the Circuit Court of Cook County's (Illinois) grant of summary judgment to appellee insurer in its declaratory judgment action where it sought a declaration of no coverage as to the wife's underinsured motorist claims.


OVERVIEW: The wife and the husband were passengers involved in a car accident. The driver was insured through the insurer. The insurer attempted to prorate the $ 300,000 per accident bodily injury maximum between six accident victims. The wife, however, also sought to recover $ 28,500 each under the driver's underinsured motorist coverage, so that she and her husband's estate would each receive the $ 100,000-per-person limit provided for bodily injuries. The insurer contended that underinsured motorist coverage was unavailable as the driver's car was not an underinsured vehicle as defined in a policy exclusion. The appeals court agreed with decisions from other jurisdictions that allowing a person to receive benefits under both the liability and underinsured motorist provisions of a single policy would amount to an impermissible rewriting of the policy to increase the liability coverage. Since liability and underinsured motorist limits were coextensive in an insured's policy under the scheme envisioned by 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/143a-2(4) (2000), a situation would not arise where that insured's vehicle would be underinsured as to itself. Legislative intent also supported this conclusion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Jones


1-03-2421


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


357 Ill. App. 3d 684; 829 N.E.2d 897; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 498; 293 Ill. Dec. 972



May 19, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 28, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Jones, 217 Ill. 2d 615, 844 N.E.2d 969, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 27, 300 Ill. Dec. 526 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 8223. Honorable Lawrence P. Fox, Judge Presiding.
People v. Jones, 351 Ill. App. 3d 1168, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 5707 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a direct appeal after he was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on a first degree murder charge. Defendant was give a 65 year prison term, which included a 25 year enhancement under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii) (2000) (enhancement statute).


OVERVIEW: The sentence enhancement was based on defendant's use of a firearm in committing the murder. On appeal, he argued that the enhancement should not have been applied because it was based on the victim's death when it should only have been applied only in the event of the injury or death of a person other than the victim. Defendant also argued that the enhancement constituted improper double enhancement and that it violated the proportionality clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970). The court disagreed on all points, holding that 1) as used in the enhancement statute, causing the death "of another" referred to a person other than defendant, not other than the victim of the crime; 2) the 25-year enhancement did not constitute a double enhancement because it was based not on the victim's death itself, which was the basis for the murder conviction, but on the use of a firearm to cause the death; 3) the enhancement statute did not violate the proportionality clause because the statute had the legitimate statutory purpose of deterring the use of firearms in the commission of murder, which the legislature had deemed to be a threat to the public's health, safety, and general welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Valstad v. Cipriano


NO. 4-04-0223


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


357 Ill. App. 3d 905; 828 N.E.2d 854; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 449; 293 Ill. Dec. 544



May 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 8, 2005.
Appeal denied by Valstad v. Cipriano, 216 Ill. 2d 736, 839 N.E.2d 1038, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1481, 298 Ill. Dec. 391 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 03CH377. Honorable Donald M. Cadagin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, National Pollutant Discharge Elimination System (NPDES) permit holders, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which dismissed their complaint against defendants, the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency (Illinois EPA), its director, and the state treasurer. The complaint alleged, in part, that 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12.5 (Supp. 2003) violated portions of the Illinois Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Section 12.5 required the Illinois EPA to collect fees from certain NPDES permit holders, including plaintiffs. The court affirmed dismissal of the complaint, holding that 1) § 12.5 did not violate the uniformity clause, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970) where defendants submitted a legally sufficient justification for imposing fees on aggregate mines holding NPDES permits, imposing a fee on school districts holding such permits would not advance the objective of increasing state revenues, and the imposition of fees only on point sources of pollution was reasonably related to that legislative purpose; 2) as the uniformity clause was not violated, there was no violation of either the equal protection clause or the substantive due process clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970); 3) 2003 Ill. Laws 32 (eff. June 20, 2003) did not violate either the appropriations clause or the single-subject clause in Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d); 4) the federal Clean Water Act did not preempt state laws regarding NPDES permit programs; 5) there was no violation of the regulations promulgated under the Clean Water Act; and 6) the trial court properly refused to allow plaintiffs to amend their complaint.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Bowman

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION

April 20, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 25, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Bowman, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 543 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., May 18, 2005)
Appeal denied by People v. Bowman, 216 Ill. 2d 697, 839 N.E.2d 1027, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1507, 298 Ill. Dec. 380 (2005)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Bowman, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 4044 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 2, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Bowman, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2147, 2011 IL App (1st) 93493U, 2011 IL App (1st) 093493U (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CR 7103. Honorable Kenneth J. Wadas, Judge Presiding. HOFFMAN and SOUTH, JJ., concur.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment on jury verdict of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of reckless homicide and aggravated driving under the influence. He challenged jury instructions, the admission of certain evidence, comments made during closing argument, and imposition of a maximum extended term sentence pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2 (2002).


OVERVIEW: Lay witnesses testified that defendant was very drunk when they saw him run a red light and hit an old man as he crossed the street with his three-year-old grandson. Defendant argued that the jury charge should not have included a modification of the pattern instructions for his offenses regarding fact findings about the victims' ages, but the court found no abuse of discretion in that the trial court had to modify the instruction to permit the jury to find facts needed to support sentencing enhancement. Photographic evidence was not more prejudicial than probative, and the lay witnesses were qualified by ordinary experience to comment on defendant's intoxication. A comment by the prosecutor during closing did not rise to the level of an attack on defense counsel's ethics. Since there was no evidence that prosecutors had any idea that one witness was falsely claiming to have given a statement to them soon after the offense, there was no showing of knowing reliance on perjured testimony. Finally, the trial court had properly weighed factors in both aggravation and mitigation in determining what sentence to impose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Ann. 200/22-45 (2002) did not violate the United States Constitution's equal protection clause.

Davis v. Brown


No. 2-04-0397


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


357 Ill. App. 3d 176; 827 N.E.2d 508; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 372; 292 Ill. Dec. 979



April 13, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 20, 2005.
Appeal granted by Davis v. Brown, 216 Ill. 2d 682, 839 N.E.2d 1022, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1361, 298 Ill. Dec. 375 (2005)
Affirmed by Davis v. Brown, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1082 (Ill., June 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County. No. 02-MR-50. Honorable Leonard J. Wojtecki, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the Circuit Court of Kendall County's (Illinois) dismissal of their declaratory judgment action against defendants, an individual and the Illinois Department of Transportation. The trial court dismissed the landowners' complaint pursuant to § 2-615 of the Code of Civil Procedure (735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-615 (2002)).


OVERVIEW: The case concerned defendants' plans for the construction of a roadway to connect two interstate highways. On appeal, the landowners contended that their second amended complaint for declaratory relief properly stated a claim sufficient to avoid dismissal under § 2-615; substantively, the landowners claimed that § 4-510 (605 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/4-510 (2002)) of the Illinois Highway Code, 605 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1-101 et seq. (2002), violated due process by allowing the State to effect a taking of the landowners' property without just compensation. The appeals court found the landowners' contention that 605 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/4-510 (2002) dispensed with the procedural requirements of eminent domain law was not borne out by the plain language of § 4-510. The court saw nothing in § 4-510 that circumvented the constitutional requirements of the exercise of the power of eminent domain. Once defendants decided to acquire the landowners' land other than by purchase, they had to employ condemnation proceedings under the eminent domain law, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-101 et seq. (2002), to accomplish their purpose.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1324 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Leroy


NO. 5-03-0333


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


357 Ill. App. 3d 530; 828 N.E.2d 769; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 369; 293 Ill. Dec. 459



April 12, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Leroy, 216 Ill. 2d 713, 839 N.E.2d 1032, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1347, 298 Ill. Dec. 385 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 01-CF-1118. Honorable Robert J. Hillebrand, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a registered sex offender, appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which revoked defendant's probation after he was found to be in violation 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-9.4(b-5) (2002) because he was residing within 500 feet of a school.


OVERVIEW: The home was owned by defendant's mother. Defendant had resided in the home for most of his 36 years of life. On appeal, defendant made several arguments about the constitutionality of § 11-9.4(b-5). The court upheld the constitutionality of the statute, holding that (1) the State had an interest in protecting children from known child sex offenders, and § 11-9.4(b-5) bore a reasonable relationship to that goal and set forth a reasonable method for furthering that goal; (2) defendant's status was based on his prior conviction for a sex offense, for which he received full due process, and he was not entitled to any further hearing to prove he had lived in his mother's home for most of his life; (3) the statute's exemption for certain sex offender homeowners created a time-specific distinction, not a class-specific one, and did not violate equal protection principles; (4) § 11-9.4(b-5) was not an ex post facto law but rather a civil, nonpunitive statute meant to protect the public rather than impose punishment; (5) § 11-9.4(b-5) did not violate defendant's self-incrimination rights; and (6) § 11-9.4(b-5) was constitutional based on overbreadth concepts.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order was affirmed.

Ill. Dep't of Revenue v. Ill. Civil Serv. Comm'n


No. 1-04-0593


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


357 Ill. App. 3d 352; 827 N.E.2d 960; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 328; 293 Ill. Dec. 79



April 8, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 8, 2005. Released for Publication May 25, 2005.
Appeal denied by Ill. Dep't of Revenue v. Ill. Civ. Serv. Comm'n, 216 Ill. 2d 686, 839 N.E.2d 1024, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1336, 298 Ill. Dec. 377 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John K. Madden, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, 13 state agencies to which defendant employees received four-year term appointments beginning in 2002, appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) judgment affirming the Illinois Civil Service Commission's decision reinstating them after their positions were terminated by an incoming governor.


OVERVIEW: In 2003, the governor fired approximately 60 employees appointed by the previous administration in 2002 to four-year terms in state government jobs. The appeals of 27 employees came before the Commission, which reinstated them. The appeals court agreed with the state agencies that the Commission lacked subject matter jurisdiction over 20 of the 27 employees since those employees were not "appointed under the rules and after examination" as required by § 11 (20 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 415/11 (2000)) of the Personnel Code, 20 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 415/1 et seq. (2000). As to the remaining employees, although the Commission had jurisdiction over their terminations, rule changes authorizing the term positions, promulgated by the Department of Central Management Services under the previous administration, were void ab initio because they contradicted the Personnel Code. When the employees were discharged, they were within the probationary period in effect previously and were subject to termination at will by the incoming administration. 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 100/5-10(c) (2000) was inapplicable, and the employees could not rely on it to validate the amendments.


OUTCOME: The Commission's order reinstating 20 employees to their government positions was vacated. The Commission's order reinstating seven employees to their state positions was reversed. The agencies' request to order all of the employees to disgorge the back pay and benefits they received since they were reinstated by the Commission was denied.

Thompson v. Gordon


No. 2-03-1322


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


356 Ill. App. 3d 447; 827 N.E.2d 983; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 339; 293 Ill. Dec. 102



April 8, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 6, 2005.
Appeal granted by Thompson v. Gordon, 216 Ill. 2d 736, 839 N.E.2d 1038, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1341, 298 Ill. Dec. 391 (2005)
Affirmed by Thompson v. Gordon, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1083 (Ill., June 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 98-L-945. The Honorable Stephen E. Walter, Judge, Presiding.
Thompson v. Gordon, 349 Ill. App. 3d 923, 813 N.E.2d 241, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 586, 286 Ill. Dec. 184 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment in a personal injury and wrongful death case which struck the affidavit of plaintiff injured party's retained expert witness because he was not qualified to render a professional opinion since he was not licensed as a professional engineer in Illinois. After denying the injured party's motion to reconsider, the trial court granted the injured party's motion for an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: The injured party alleged in her complaint that defendants' alleged design defect caused the auto accident that resulted in her injuries and the deaths of two other people. The trial court granted defendants' motion to strike the affidavit of her retained expert because he was not licensed as a professional engineer in Illinois pursuant to the Illinois Professional Engineering Practice Act of 1989, 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 325/1 et seq. (2002). The trial court granted the injured party's motion for interlocutory appeal and certified two questions for review. As to the first question, the appellate court found that it could not determine whether the engineer's retention as an opinion witness in the case constituted the unlicensed practice of professional engineering under the Act because the initial determination of that question was relegated to the Department of Professional Regulation. On the second question, it found that the Van Breemen case did not control the issue of striking the affidavit. Finally, it found that the affidavit should not have been stricken because the engineer was not required to be licensed in Illinois in order to render an expert opinion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court declined to answer the first certified question, answered the second certified question in the negative, reversed the trial court's judgment striking the engineer's affidavit, and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

Qualkinbush v. Skubisz


No. 1-03-2528


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


357 Ill. App. 3d 594; 826 N.E.2d 1181; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 299; 292 Ill. Dec. 745



March 31, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 11, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Michael J. Murphy, Judge Presiding.
Qualkinbush v. Skubisz, 822 N.E.2d 38, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1546, 290 Ill. Dec. 756 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent candidate appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which certified the mayoral election results for a city and declared petitioner contester mayor. The contester had filed a verified petition for an election contest. The candidate filed a verified counterpetition.


OVERVIEW: The contester's petition for an election contest alleged voter irregularities, including insufficient reasons given by physically incapacitated voters on their applications for absentee ballots, improper assistance given to disabled voters by members of the candidate's campaign, and illegal delivery or mailing of absentee ballots. The candidate asserted similar allegations in his petition as well as challenged the validity of 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/19-6 (2002). The court found that § 19-6 was not preempted by federal law and did not place an undue burden upon disabled voters with regard to choosing who may assist them. The court found clear evidence that the candidate's campaign worker violated § 19-6 by taking absentee ballot applications to voters, helping them fill them out and watching them do so, placing the applications in envelopes, providing stamps, and mailing the applications. That campaign worker also helped voters following receipt of their ballot by returning to their homes and helping them fill out the ballots as well as mailing them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

CH5615, 01 CH 5616, 01. CH 5617, 01 CH 5618, and 01 CH 5705 (Consolidated). Honorable Patrick E. McGann, Judge Presiding.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Illinois Health Maintenance Organization (HMO) Guaranty Association petitioned the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for review of appellee Director of the Illinois Department of Insurance's decisions that the Association was liable to appellee health care providers for services rendered an insolvent HMO's enrollees. The complaints were dismissed. After appeal, the trial court affirmed awards of interest and hearing costs.


OVERVIEW: The providers submitted claims to the Association for services rendered to an insolvent HMO's enrollees. The providers sought review of the Association's denial of their claims by the Director, under the Illinois Health Maintenance Organization Guaranty Association Law, 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 125/6-1 et seq. (2000). The hearing officers found the Association liable to 20 of the 24 providers for their principal claims and interest. The Director approved the hearing officers' decisions on the principal claims, and awarded hearing costs and interest. Rather than request any rehearings, the Association filed 24 complaints for administrative review in the trial court. On appeal, the court found that (1) the exhaustion of administrative remedies doctrine required that the Association file motions for rehearing with the Department before filing complaints for administrative review in the trial court; (2) the notices of appeal did not divest the trial court of jurisdiction to enter the monetary judgments; (3) the hearing costs assessed were proper; and (4) the trial court's refusal to impose prejudgment interest as provided by a settlement agreement was an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part as to the dismissal of the complaints, the judgments awarding the principal amounts and hearing costs, the imposition of post-judgment interest, and the imposition of prejudgment interest in favor of all but one of the providers. The imposition of prejudgment interest to one provider was vacated, and the case was remanded for recalculation of prejudgment interest owed to that provider.

Walters v. Dep't of Labor


No. 1-04-0590


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


356 Ill. App. 3d 785; 826 N.E.2d 979; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 274; 292 Ill. Dec. 543



March 24, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 11, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 CH 3562. Honorable Peter Flynn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that reversed defendant state labor department's determination that plaintiff businessman violated the Illinois Wage Payment and Collection Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 115/1 et seq. (2002), by not paying nine employees for unused vacation time. The state labor department appealed.


OVERVIEW: Nine employees filed wage claim applications with the state labor department pursuant to the Illinois Wage Payment and Collection Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 115/1 et seq. (2002) (Act), alleging that the businessman failed to pay them for unpaid vacation time. A hearing officer conducted an informal investigation and found him responsible for the payments. The state labor department then issued of wage payment demand to the businessman and indicated to him that its investigation of the matter disclosed "apparent" Act violations. Eventually, he tendered full payment in compliance with the wage payment demand and expressed a desire to appeal. The trial court treated his request as one for a common law writ of certiorari and reversed the state labor department's determination. On appeal, the appellate court found that the state labor department's wage payment demand was not subject to administrative review under the common law writ of certiorari because the wage payment demand did not adjudicate any rights and the state labor department had been acting in an investigative, but not quasi-judicial, role in its proceedings under the Act.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was vacated.

People v. McCarty


NO. 5-03-0475


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


356 Ill. App. 3d 552; 826 N.E.2d 957; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 255; 292 Ill. Dec. 521



March 22, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 4, 2005.
Appeal granted by People v. McCarty, 216 Ill. 2d 715, 839 N.E.2d 1032, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1229, 298 Ill. Dec. 385 (2005)
Affirmed by People v. McCarty, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1649 (Ill., Oct. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. No. 01-CF-404. Honorable Patrick L. Duke, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a stipulated bench trial defendant was convicted of unlawful manufacture of a controlled substance containing methamphetamine and possession with intent to deliver cannabis. The Circuit Court of Marion County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to concurrent prison terms of 15 years on the manufacturing conviction and 5 years on the intent-to-deliver conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the search warrant was unconstitutional and the items seized should have been suppressed because the place to be searched and the items to be seized were not identified with particularity. The appellate court found no error, noting that, inter alia, there was no evidence that the search was executed at the wrong location and the warrant listed the items to be seized such that the trained officer could easily identify them as contraband. Next, the appellate court found no merit in defendant's argument that the penalty provisions for unlawful manufacture of a controlled substance containing methamphetamine constituted unconstitutional disproportionate penalties, noting the conduct of a methamphetamine manufacturer was sufficiently different from that of a distributor that proportionate review was inappropriate. As for defendant's contention that his conviction for possession of cannabis with intent to deliver should have been reduced to simple possession because the State failed to prove the intent-to-distribute element, the appellate court disagreed, concluding that the evidence, when taken together, established the element of intent to deliver cannabis.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Rosenberg


No. 3-02-0759


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


356 Ill. App. 3d 219; 825 N.E.2d 720; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 220; 292 Ill. Dec. 132


April 2, 2003, Submitted  
March 7, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 13, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit, La Salle County, Illinois. No. 2000-CF-172. Honorable Chris H. Ryan, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Rosenberg, 213 Ill. 2d 69, 820 N.E.2d 440, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1671, 289 Ill. Dec. 664 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit, La Salle County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after defendant was found guilty of controlled substance trafficking. Defendant was then sentenced to 18 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a Massachusetts resident, was charged under the Controlled Substances Act (Act), 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/401.1(a) (2000), based upon a traffic stop of his accomplice's vehicle. A search revealed 5,000 vials of ketamine. At trial, the accomplice testified that he was transporting the vials cross-country to Boston and that the controlled substance belonged to defendant. Defendant claimed that he was merely passing through Illinois and did not intend to deliver the controlled substance in Illinois. He was convicted and sentenced to 18 years in prison. On appeal, the appellate court found that the language of the Act plainly intended not only to punish those who deliver drugs into Illinois but also to punish the traffickers who travel through Illinois. It also found that defendant's sentence did not violate the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, even though controlled substance trafficking was punished more harshly than possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance because those statutory offenses did not share a common purpose and, thus, the legislature could reasonably punish those offenses differently.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Sharp


NO. 4-02-0913


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


355 Ill. App. 3d 786; 825 N.E.2d 706; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 218; 292 Ill. Dec. 118


June 11, 2004, Submitted  
March 2, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 8, 2005.
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Sharp, 231 Ill. 2d 649, 899 N.E.2d 1076, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 129, 326 Ill. Dec. 425 (2009)
Substituted opinion at, On reconsideration by People v. Sharp, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 545 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., June 26, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of De Witt County. No. 02CF8. Honorable Stephen H. Peters, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of De Witt County (Illinois) of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred by admitting certain hearsay testimony in violation of the Confrontation Clause, U.S. Const. amend. VI, and 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10 (2000) and that he was denied a fair trial by the prosecutor's rebuttal argument.


OVERVIEW: The victim's mother, a child advocate, and one of the victim's friends testified at a § 115-10 hearing about statements the victim made regarding her attack. The trial court admitted the statements made to the mother and to the advocate. The victim also testified at trial. She related the events leading up to the attack and the events that occurred immediately thereafter. She did not answer questions about the attack itself, and defense counsel chose not explore the attack during cross-examination. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that (1) the Confrontation Clause was not a factor regarding the victim's statements because the victim testified and was available for full cross-examination; (2) the victim's statements were admissible under § 115-10, even though they were not made until 33 days after the attack, where the victim's lack of understanding of the term "penetration" and the consistency of her statements indicated she had not been "coached" on what to say; and (3) defendant waived his right to appeal from errors he claimed were made in the prosecution's closing argument by failing to promptly object, and the claimed errors did not constitute plain error.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

People v. Bonner


No. 1-03-2634


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


356 Ill. App. 3d 386; 826 N.E.2d 444; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 175; 292 Ill. Dec. 303



March 1, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 4, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Bonner, 215 Ill. 2d 601, 833 N.E.2d 4, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 910, 295 Ill. Dec. 522 (Ill., May 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CR 10222. Honorable Leo E. Holt, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that found defendant guilty of violating the Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/1 et seq. (2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the sexual exploitation of a child, a Class A misdemeanor. As a result, he was required to register as a sex offender and to report any change of address pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/3, 6 (2000). However, he did neither. He was then charged with failing to register as a sex offender. Failing to register as a sex offender, as required under the Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/1 et seq. (2000), was a felony. Thus, failing to register was punished more severely than defendant's underlying offense. Defendant's motion to dismiss contending that the penalty portion of the Act was unconstitutional as applied to him because of its disproportionality was denied. On appeal, the appellate court found that the Proportionate Penalties Clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, had not been violated. It so concluded because it found that the purposes of the Act and the sexual-exploitation-of-a-child statute were distinct, especially since the Act had the additional purpose of tracking the movements of sexual offenders to prevent the recurrence of attacks on adults as well as children.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Morris v. Dep't of Prof'l Regulation


Nos. 1-01-2779 & 1-03-3739: Cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


356 Ill. App. 3d 83; 824 N.E.2d 1151; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 135; 291 Ill. Dec. 901



February 18, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 13, 2005.
Appeal denied by Morris v. Ill. Dep't of Prof'l Regulation, 215 Ill. 2d 599, 833 N.E.2d 4, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 884, 295 Ill. Dec. 522 (Ill., May 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CH 13175. Honorable Richard Billik, Judge Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 CH 6025. Honorable Aaron Jaffe, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Illinois Department of Professional Regulation (IDPR) ordered plaintiff nurse to cease and desist the practice of midwifery. Defendant IDPR Director suspended the nurse's license for three years, followed by two years' probation, fined her $ 2,500, and required her to complete a 12-hour ethics course. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) affirmed these administrative orders. The nurse appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the nurse raised numerous issues. The appellate court concluded that the IDPR did not err in ordering her to cease and desist the practice of midwifery and the Director did not err in suspending her license because the nurse could only engage in midwifery and advanced practice nursing if she complied with the licensing requirements of the Nursing and Advanced Practice Nursing Act, 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 65/5-1 (2000), and she failed to comply with the requirements. In addition, the Nursing Act had previously been held not to be unconstitutionally vague. Also, the nurse's due process claims failed because she received notice of the charges and enjoyed a hearing before an impartial tribunal, at which she was represented by counsel and was allowed to cross-examine witnesses, present evidence in her own defense and inspect documentary evidence against her. Finally, the suspension of the nurse's license, followed by probation and a fine, was reasonably related to the purpose of the Nursing Act and was affirmed. However, no argument was provided explaining the relevance of the 12-hour ethics course to the purposes of the Nursing Act.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the orders requiring the nurse to cease and desist the practice of midwifery and suspending her nursing license and fining her; the appellate court vacated the requirement that the nurse complete an ethics course.

In re Marriage of Ross


NO. 5-03-0613


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


355 Ill. App. 3d 1162; 824 N.E.2d 1108; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 128; 291 Ill. Dec. 858



February 16, 2005, Decided  
February 16, 2005, Decision Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. No. 00-D-90. Honorable David L. Sauer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Marion County (Illinois), in which the trial court refused to modify the mother's child support obligation, declined to order visitation privileges to the maternal grandparents, determined the place of the exchange for the children's visitation, and reduced her visitation with the children.


OVERVIEW: Respondent father was the custodial parent. The mother paid child support. She left a job in Illinois to move to Indiana, where she accepted a lower-paying job. She claimed that she intended to pursue further education. She sought a child support reduction, and due to the fact that distance prevented her from maintaining a prior visitation schedule, she sought grandparent visitation for her parents. The court affirmed the trial court. There was no basis for modification of the support obligation. The mother voluntarily left a good paying job and accepted the lower paying job. Her educational plans were vague at best. Better paying jobs were available without leaving the state, and it appeared that the move was meant as a way to evade her financial responsibilities. As to visitation, like court ordered grandparent visitation under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607(b)(1), (b)(3) (2000), prior common law that would have authorized such visitation was also unconstitutional. Such visitation could not be ordered absent an agreement between the parties.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People ex rel. Madigan v. Baumgartner


NO. 4-04-0334


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


355 Ill. App. 3d 842; 823 N.E.2d 1144; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 155; 291 Ill. Dec. 558



February 16, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 16, 2005.
Appeal denied by People ex rel. Madigan v. Baumgartner, 215 Ill. 2d 618, 833 N.E.2d 8, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 869, 295 Ill. Dec. 526 (Ill., May 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Moultrie County. No. 03CF84. Honorable John P. Shonkwiler, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Moultrie County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of one count of felony perjury for filing a statement of candidacy in which he allegedly falsely stated under oath that his address was in a particular county when it allegedly was not. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was born and raised in the forum county. He graduated from high school there and enrolled in a university in another county. However, he continued to hold a forum county driver's license and voter's registration. For the most part, he continued to live in the county where the university was located and stayed there a number of years while he pursued multiple degrees. However, he kept his address in the forum county and spent a great deal of time there. Thereafter, defendant's father asked defendant to run for election to the county board of the forum county. Defendant filed a statement of candidacy that stated his residence was in the forum county. He was then successfully elected to the county board of the forum county. The State later filed an information against him and alleged he committed perjury by stating in his statement of candidacy that his residence was in the forum county rather than in the county where he was attending school. Defendant was convicted on that charge. On appeal, the appellate court found that he could not be convicted because he merely chose one of two plausible locations as his residence for the purpose of his statement of candidacy.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of conviction was reversed.

People v. Scott


No. 3-01-0981


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


355 Ill. App. 3d 741; 824 N.E.2d 302; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 160; 291 Ill. Dec. 726



February 16, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 22, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Scott, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 24 (Ill., Jan. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Rock Island County, Illinois. No. 97--CF--121. Honorable Larry S. Vandersnick, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Scott, 306 Ill. App. 3d 1187, 757 N.E.2d 133, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 3387, 258 Ill. Dec. 748 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 14th Judicial Circuit Court, Rock Island County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of unlawful delivery of a controlled substance in a drug-free zone. The trial court then dismissed defendant's post-conviction petition for relief. Defendant appealed from the denial of his post-conviction petition for relief.


OVERVIEW: A police officer working undercover informed defendant that he was interested in buying cocaine. Defendant led him to an apartment in a public housing complex, knocked on the door, and spoke with another man. A cocaine sale allegedly took place. Defendant was arrested. An attorney was appointed to represent defendant. The officer testified at defendant's preliminary hearing about the sale. On cross-examination, the officer testified that the other man had "denied everything." The trial court found probable cause for the charge. The attorney then notified the trial court that he had been appointed to represent the other man. The attorney was allowed to withdraw. At trial, the State introduced a lab report regarding the cocaine that had been sold. Defense counsel did not object, but stipulated to the report's contents. Defendant was convicted. His postconviction petition was dismissed. On appeal, the appellate court found that defendant did not show his counsel had a conflict of interest and that the record did not need to show that defendant was informed of and explicitly waived his confrontation rights regarding admission of the lab report without the testimony of its preparer.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. R.F.


No. 1-02-3347


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


355 Ill. App. 3d 992; 825 N.E.2d 287; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 98; 292 Ill. Dec. 31



February 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 13, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. R.F., 224 Ill. 2d 588, 871 N.E.2d 60, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 954, 312 Ill. Dec. 660 (Ill., May 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 10579. Honorable Preston Bowie, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed in part and vacated in part; mittimus corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him for criminal sexual assault and predatory criminal sexual assault of a child (PCSA) in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14.1 (2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions, arguing that the admission of certain statements by the victim violated his Sixth Amendment right to confrontation, that the State failed to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, and that he was improperly convicted of multiple crimes based upon the same conduct. The court found that the trial court properly admitted hearsay statements that the child-victim made to her mother and to her grandmother in which she accused defendant of pinching and kissing her vaginal area. The statements were made to family members and were not made to governmental personnel, so they were not "testimonial" statements. Accordingly, the indicia of reliability framework attached to their admissibility and the hearsay exception set forth in § 115-10 of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10 (2000), determined that the statements were properly admissible. Moreover, when combined with the evidence of defendant's confession, there was sufficient evidence to show the State proved defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. Finally, the State conceded that the criminal sexual assault conviction had to be vacated.


OUTCOME: The court affirm defendant's conviction for PCSA, vacated the conviction for criminal sexual assault, and corrected the mittimus.

 

1339 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Lamar Whiteco Outdoor Corp. v. City of W. Chicago


Nos. 2-03-1392 & 2-04-0575 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


355 Ill. App. 3d 352; 823 N.E.2d 610; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 94; 291 Ill. Dec. 318



February 8, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 8, 2005.
Subsequent appeal at, Dismissed by Lamar Whiteco Outdoor Corp. v. City of W. Chi., 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 991 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Oct. 8, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of DuPage County. No. 01-MR-907. Honorable Patrick J. Leston, Judge, Presiding.

Appeal from the Circuit Court of DuPage County. Nos. 99-MR-973, 99-OV-8698, 99-OV-8699, 99-OV-9644, 99-OV-9645, 99-OV-9647, 99-OV-9648. Honorable Edward R. Duncan, Jr., Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed in each case.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, plaintiff billboard owners challenged decisions in their separate cases before the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which dismissed some of their claims against defendant city for writing tickets due to failure to remove billboards. The dismissals were based on alleged time bars of the owners' claims under § 7-101 of the Eminent Domain Act (EDA), 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-101 (2002) and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: A city zoning ordinance was amended to ban billboards, though it provided a seven-year grace period. The city began enforcing the ban after the grace period by issuing tickets, which the owners received. They brought separate actions against the city, including claims under the EDA and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Those claims were dismissed in each action on statute of limitations grounds. The owners appealed, arguing the claims did not accrue until the grace period expired and tickets were issued. The court agreed that both kinds of claims accrued when the city issued the tickets, so the claims were timely and were improperly dismissed. The court found that a final determination of the applicability of the zoning ordinance to the owners' billboards did not occur until the city began issuing tickets. Since the § 1983 actions were premised on a denial of procedural due process rights, they were timely filed within the two-year personal injury period applicable to § 1983 actions. Moreover, the EDA claims did not accrue until there was a radical curtailment of the owners' property rights in the billboards. That also occurred when the tickets were issued and not when the ordinance was passed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissals in both cases.

 

1340 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. E.H. (In re E.H.)


No. 1-01-2776


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


355 Ill. App. 3d 564; 823 N.E.2d 1029; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 52; 291 Ill. Dec. 443



January 28, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 17, 2005.
Appeal granted by People v. E.H. (In re E.H.), 215 Ill. 2d 597, 833 N.E.2d 2, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 814, 295 Ill. Dec. 520 (2005)
Vacated by, Remanded by In re E.H., 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1666 (Ill., Dec. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 00 JD 6501. The Hon. Rodney H. Brooks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court reversed; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a minor, was charged in a petition for adjudication of wardship with two counts each of aggravated criminal sexual abuse and aggravated criminal sexual assault. After a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), she was found delinquent and made a ward of the court. She filed an appeal from the charges, asserting that her conviction should be reversed because she was not allowed to cross-examine one of her accusers.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether a child victim's out-of-court statements to her grandmother were admissible as evidence at trial. The U.S. Supreme Court's decision in Crawford reasoned that the testimonial statements of a witness who did not appear at trial would not be admissible unless the witness was unavailable to testify and the defendant had a prior opportunity for cross-examination. Although some uncertainty remained regarding the exact definition of "testimonial statements," the appeals court found the victim's statement to her grandmother fell within the purview of Crawford and was protected by the Confrontation Clause. The victim bore accusatory testimony against defendant which was offered to prove the truth of the matter asserted, specifically, that defendant sexually assaulted her. Because defendant did not have an opportunity to cross-examine the victim, defendant's constitutional rights were violated and she was entitled to a new adjudicatory hearing. The error was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The appeals court found Crawford rendered § 115-10 of the Illinois Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963 (725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10 (2000)) unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The finding of delinquency was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for an adjudicatory hearing consistent with the opinion. Double jeopardy considerations did not prevent retrial.

People v. Wead


No. 1-02-1878


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


355 Ill. App. 3d 586; 823 N.E.2d 192; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 29; 291 Ill. Dec. 182



January 21, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Wead, 834 N.E.2d 908, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1147, 296 Ill. Dec. 103 (Ill., 2005)
On reconsideration by, Substituted opinion at, Remanded by People v. Wead, 842 N.E.2d 227, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1280, 299 Ill. Dec. 488 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 99 CR 3114. The Honorable Stuart Palmer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court reversed; cause remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of first degree murder and imposed a sentence of 38 years' imprisonment. The trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: A police detective was told to bring defendant to the police station because his description matched that of a possible homicide suspect. The detective indicated that he saw no crime committed and had no involvement with defendant after bringing him to an interview room. The detective who interviewed defendant stated that he was investigating a murder, and that defendant was not accused of anything when he confessed. Defendant claimed that he was locked into the interview room for three days and that he was handcuffed. Further, he claimed that the police were misleading in their conversation with him. The trial court denied defendant's motions to quash arrest and to suppress evidence and statements. Defendant was convicted and he appealed. The court found that defendant was not "arrested" when he got into the police car and went to the police station. However, he was arrested while at the police station, in that he was not free to leave. The court found no probable cause to justify the arrest, which it deemed illegal. Nor was there attenuation in order to avoid suppression of defendant's statements. Accordingly, his confession should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for a new trial, in which defendant's postarrest statement was to be suppressed.

Green Party v. Henrichs


No. 3-04-0642


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


355 Ill. App. 3d 445; 822 N.E.2d 910; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 37; 291 Ill. Dec. 35



January 21, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 25, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 21st Judicial Circuit, Iroquois County, Illinois. No. 04--MR--27. Honorable Clark E. Erickson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a political party and party officials (party), appealed an order from the Circuit Court for the 21st Judicial Circuit in Iroquois County (Illinois), which denied their motion to force defendant county election officials to place the candidates' names on the ballot in the general election for county positions despite opposition by defendant objector.


OVERVIEW: The party filed a nominating petition for three candidates for county positions. The objector opposed, alleging that the petition violated 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/10-2 (2004) because it did not nominate candidates for other open county positions. The circuit court found that for that reason, the party's petition was insufficient and invalid. On appeal, the party argued that the petition did not violate the wording of 5/10-2 and that if the statute were interpreted to require a new political party to field a candidate for every office, it was unconstitutional. The court found that 5/10-2 plainly required a new political party to field a candidate for each open position in a political area and the party's petition did not nominate candidates for all open positions. Therefore, the petition was insufficient under 5/10-2 and was properly rejected. Also, the full-slate requirement in 5/10-2 was reasonable and nondiscriminatory in that it insured that a new party had sufficient support to be considered a party. Finally, candidates were not prevented from running for office because they could run as independents. The statute was properly interpreted and it was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to deny the party's and the candidates' motion.

People v. Chamberlain


No. 3-03-1005


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


354 Ill. App. 3d 1070; 822 N.E.2d 914; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 36; 291 Ill. Dec. 39



January 21, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 25, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Chamberlain, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 679 (Ill., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Henry County, Illinois. No. 03--CF--223. Honorable Ted J. Hamer, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 14th Judicial Circuit Court, Henry County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after defendant pled guilty to two counts of aggravated battery. It then sentenced him to two concurrent four-year prison terms, with 29 days of credit spent in presentence custody. It also ordered him to submit to genetic marker testing pursuant to Illinois statutory law. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with several battery counts arising out of incidents while he was in the state-run youth center's custody. Thereafter, he pled guilty to two counts of aggravated battery. He indicated to the trial court that he was 19 years old, and was able to read and write. However, he also stated he was taking "a lot" of psychotropic medication for bipolar disorder, mood swings, and an anxiety disorder. Eventually, he indicated that he knew the charges to which he was pleading guilty and that he had received enough time to speak with his attorney about his plea. The trial court found the plea was knowing and voluntary, accepted the plea, and sentenced defendant. In so doing, it gave him 29 days of credit for time in presentence custody. In addition, defendant was ordered to submit to DNA testing. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court was not required to have sua sponte ordered a fitness hearing to determine defendant's fitness to plead guilty, as it could have determined that no bona fide doubt existed as to his fitness. It also found defendant was entitled to 15 days of additional presentence credit and that the DNA testing statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed, but the mittimus was modified to grant defendant an additional 15 days of presentence jail credit for the time between when he was charged and was being detained at the youth center, until the time he was transferred to the county jail.

James E. v. People (In re James E.)


NO. 5-05-0407


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


363 Ill. App. 3d 286; 843 N.E.2d 387; 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1330; 300 Ill. Dec. 129



January 13, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to Publish Granted January 13, 2006. As Corrected January 27, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 05-MH-91. Honorable Barbara Crowder, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner patient filed an emergency petition, naming respondent State of Illinois, for a declaratory judgment seeking his discharge from a mental health facility under the Illinois Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Code. The Circuit Court of Madison County, Illinois, found the petition to be moot due to the patient's subsequent discharge from the facility and denied his posttrial motion. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient was purportedly admitted to the facility as a voluntary inpatient. In his first petition, he alleged he was being held unlawfully because more than five days had passed since he expressed his desire to be discharged but the State had neither released him nor filed a petition for involuntary admission. The motion was denied. He then filed the instant petition, asserting the same arguments. The appellate court held that despite the patient's release after filing the petition, the appeal was not moot since the scenario was capable of repetition and incapable of resolution on appeal within a constricted time frame. As there was no evidence the facility's director fulfilled his mandatory duty under 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-404 (2004) of the Illinois Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Code to request, at the end of the patient's first 30 days of hospitalization, that he reaffirm his desire to continue voluntary treatment, the patient had been entitled to a declaratory judgment. The trial court committed reversible error by finding that the patient had been obliged to make a demand for discharge under 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-403 (2004).


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of a declaratory judgment was reversed.

Related proceeding at Nienhouse v. Nienhouse, 2005 Ky. App. Unpub. LEXIS 177 (Ky. Ct. App., Feb. 18, 2005)

In re Nienhouse, 337 Ill. App. 3d 1150, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 2348 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2003)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, in entering judgment dissolving his marriage to petitioner wife, denied his motion to vacate a non-paternity order, denied his petition for sibling visitation, and ordered the husband to pay attorney fees for a guardian ad litem.


OVERVIEW: The parties had one daughter before the wife sought a divorce. She then gave birth to a second daughter. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/506 (2002).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Powell


1-03-1008


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


355 Ill. App. 3d 124; 822 N.E.2d 131; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1566; 290 Ill. Dec. 849



December 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 15, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Powell, 217 Ill. 2d 585, 844 N.E.2d 45, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1664, 300 Ill. Dec. 373 (Ill., Dec. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Colleen McSweeney-Moore, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder committed while personally discharging a firearm. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to consecutive terms of 30 years for first degree murder and 20 years for personally discharging a firearm during the commission of the murder pursuant to Illinois' "15/20/25-to-life" mandatory sentencing enhancement provision, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(ii) (2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the 20-year sentence enhancement violated the proportionality clause of the Illinois Constitution because it punished first degree murder committed while personally discharging a firearm more severely than similar offenses that constituted greater threats to the health and safety of the public, aggravated battery with a firearm and aggravated discharge of a firearm. The appellate court found no merit to that argument, noting that the legislative purpose behind the statutes differed; thus, comparative proportionality review was inappropriate. The appellate court held that the aggravated battery and aggravated discharge offenses constituted a less serious threat to publish health and safety. Therefore, the more severe punishment for defendant's crime was proper. The appellate court also found no reason to depart from judicial precedent to find that the enhancement violated due process. Finally, that appellate court found no merit to defendant's argument that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to request that the trial court inquire about potential gang bias amongst the venire members, as gang evidence permeated the trial and both sides utilized it.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Qualkinbush v. Skubisz


No. 1-03-2528


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


822 N.E.2d 38; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1546; 290 Ill. Dec. 756



December 28, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 15, 2005.
Opinion replaced by Qualkinbush v. Skubisz, 357 Ill. App. 3d 594, 826 N.E.2d 1181, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 299, 292 Ill. Dec. 745 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2005)
Opinion withdrawn by, 03/31/2005


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Michael J. Murphy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) certifying mayoral election results for a city in which the court declared petitioner mayor.


OVERVIEW: Respondent first claimed the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss with respect to 38 votes because § 19-6 of the Election Code, 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/19-6 (2002), was preempted by and violated the Voting Rights Act and the Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990 since it restricted the individuals with whom an absentee voter could entrust their ballot for mailing. The appeals court found the trial court did not err in denying the motion to dismiss, as § 19-6 prevented a candidate or his or her agent from asserting undue influence upon a disabled voter and from manipulating that voter into voting for the candidate or the agent's candidate, and was designed to protect the rights of disabled voters. Respondent had not established that the federal legislature intended to preempt the rights of state legislatures to restrict absentee voting, and, particularly, who could return absentee ballots. Section 19-6 did not violate equal protection principles, as the burden placed upon absentee voters by the restriction on who could mail an absentee ballot was slight and nondiscriminatory and substantially contributed to the integrity of the election process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Pickens


No. 1-04-0403


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 904; 822 N.E.2d 58; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1543; 290 Ill. Dec. 776



December 28, 2004, Decided; Nunc Pro Tunc 11/30/04


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 15, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Pickens, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 131 (Ill. App. Ct., Jan. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 MC6-23544. The Honorable Christopher J. Donnelly, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with domestic battery in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-3.2(a)(2) (2002). Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found defendant guilty and sentenced him to conditional discharge for a period of 12 months. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State did not succeed in proving him guilty of domestic battery beyond a reasonable doubt because the State failed to show that he intentionally or knowingly closed a door on his wife's foot. Defendant maintained that he only tried to close the door between the garage and the house one time and that he did not intentionally smash his wife's foot in the door. The appellate court declined to overrule the trial court's finding that the wife's testimony that defendant tried to close the door twice was more plausible. Defendant also argued that the statutory penalty for domestic battery violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution because it permitted judges to grant supervision to defendants convicted of a Class A misdemeanor such as simple battery, but denied the judge that same discretion for those defendants convicted of domestic battery, which was also a Class A misdemeanor. The appellate court held that there was no proportionality violation as battery and domestic battery did not share identical elements; battery applied to any individual, and domestic battery applied to all family or household members.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Engelkens


No. 3-03-0842


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


354 Ill. App. 3d 790; 821 N.E.2d 799; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1559; 290 Ill. Dec. 487



December 28, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 3, 2005.
Appeal denied by Engelkens v. Engelkens, 214 Ill. 2d 529, 830 N.E.2d 2, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 580, 294 Ill. Dec. 2 (Ill., Mar. 30, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the Fourteenth Judicial Circuit, Whiteside County, Illinois, No. 98-D-024. The Honorable Timothy Slavin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former husband sought to terminate respondent former wife's visitation with his son from a previous relationship. The Circuit Court of the Fourteenth Judicial Circuit, Whiteside County, Illinois, found that the stepparent visitation statute, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607(b)(1.5), was constitutional as applied to the facts of the case and denied the husband's petition. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the settlement agreement, the husband allowed the wife to visit his son. The wife made seven reports to the State alleging the child was abused. The appellate court noted the visitation agreement was based on 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607(b)(1.5), which allowed a trial court to grant visitation to a step-parent if it would be in the best interest of the child. Section 607(b)(1.5) was facially unconstitutional, as it a placed a fit parent on equal footing with the step-parent in their attempts to convince the trial court that visitation was or was not in the child's best interest. As the statute was void ab initio, the trial court erred in finding an "exception" to its unconstitutionality - the husband's unfitness. There was no common law right to step-parent visitation in Illinois, and estoppel by remarriage did not apply because the wife's challenge was not to the judgment of dissolution as a whole, but only that portion granting her visitation. Equitable estoppel did not apply, as the wife did not claim she was induced to provide health care coverage for the child based on the husband's representations. The visitation agreement lacked consideration and was unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.
