GMAC v. Johnson


No. 1-04-0633


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 885; 822 N.E.2d 30; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1544; 290 Ill. Dec. 748



December 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 15, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 M1 164531. Honorable Leon Wool, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a finance company, sued defendants, purchasers, to recover money owed on a motor vehicle. The purchasers filed a third-party complaint against third-party defendant, an automobile dealership, alleging violations of the Illinois Consumer Fraud Act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/2B (2002). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the dealership's motion to stay the litigation pending arbitration, and the purchasers appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the purchasers bought a car from the dealership, one of the purchasers signed an arbitration agreement. The purchasers attempted to return the vehicle, but the dealership refused to take the car back. In the third-party complaint, the purchasers argued that the dealership failed to give the purchasers notice of their right of rescission and refused to cancel the contract and accept return of the vehicle, in violation of the Consumer Fraud Act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/2B. The purchasers argued that the trial court erred in finding that the arbitration agreement applied to the third-party action. The appellate court held that compliance with the Consumer Fraud Act was not a condition precedent to the existence of an enforceable contract. Moreover, the mere existence of the right to cancel under 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/2B in and of itself did not indicate that the exercise of that right would render the contract void or unenforceable. Accordingly, the trial court properly found that the issue of whether the Consumer Fraud Act was violated by the dealership was arbitrable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1351 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rexroat (In re Rexroat)


No. 3-03-0835


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


354 Ill. App. 3d 447; 821 N.E.2d 362; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1531; 290 Ill. Dec. 311



December 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 31, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit, LaSalle County, Illinois. No. 99--MR--32. Honorable William P. Balestri, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act (Act), 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 et seq. (2002), defendant was committed to an agency for control, care, and treatment. He subsequently filed a petition for conditional release, and a motion challenging the constitutionality of the Act. Both pleadings were denied without evidentiary hearings by the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit, LaSalle County (Illinois), and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was placed in a prison facility after the sexually violent person adjudication, the only facility approved for sexually violent persons. In a periodic reexamination, a doctor found that defendant had not received the proper care for his condition, and suggested that he be transferred to another facility where appropriate treatment could be rendered. Under the Act, the trial court had only two options regarding defendant's commitment: institutional care in a secure facility, or conditional release, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/40(b)(2) (2002). The appellate court found that because defendant's request would not have removed him from care in a secure facility, he was not asking for conditional release at all. Defendant asked the trial court to do more than identify goals for his treatment; he wanted an order telling the agency where to hold him, thus encroaching on the agency's statutory authority to determine the nature of the facility. As to defendant's claim that the Act was unconstitutional as applied to him, the appellate court held that defendant could seek appropriate relief through a properly drafted petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1352 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Rodimel v. Cook County Sheriff's Office


No. 1-03-2967


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 744; 822 N.E.2d 7; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1530; 290 Ill. Dec. 725



December 23, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 7, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CH 22174. Honorable Patrick McGann, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from a Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) order dismissing his declaratory judgment action against defendants, the Cook County sheriffs office, the Cook County State's Attorney's office and the Illinois State Police. His complaint sought a declaration that the Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act (Registration Act) (730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/2 (2002)) did not require him to register as a sex offender in Illinois.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was convicted of indecent assault under the Uniform Code of Military Justice, an offense not explicitly listed in § 2(B) of the Registration Act. He was required to register as a sex offender in Illinois only if indecent assault was substantially equivalent to any of the offenses listed in § 2(B). Defendants claimed the trial court properly dismissed his declaratory judgment action under § 2-619 of the Illinois Code of Civil Procedure, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-619 (2002), because indecent assault was substantially equivalent to the listed offense of criminal sexual abuse. Plaintiff was convicted of indecent assault for kissing the victim on the mouth, straddling her, and touching her breasts for sexual gratification. Proof of these facts also satisfied the elements required for criminal sexual abuse. Therefore, indecent assault was substantially equivalent to criminal sexual abuse and the conviction for indecent assault required him to register in Illinois as a sex offender. The trial court properly dismissed his § 2-619 action. Contrary to plaintiff's claim, criminal sexual abuse did not require that the offense be committed against a child under 13.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1353 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Woodrum


Nos. 1-00-4124 & 1-00-4125 (Consolidated)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 629; 821 N.E.2d 787; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1535; 290 Ill. Dec. 475



December 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 7, 2005.
Appeal granted by People v. Woodrum, 214 Ill. 2d 551, 830 N.E.2d 8, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 550, 294 Ill. Dec. 8 (2005)
Reversed by People v. Woodrum, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1633 (Ill., Oct. 5, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 00 CR 19545, 00 CR 19546. Honorable.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of child abduction in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/10-5 (2000). He argued that the statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him especially in the absence of a bill of particulars, that his 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/103-5 (1998) speedy trial rights were violated, and that he should not have been ordered to undergo certain tests.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with child abduction after videotaping neighborhood children playing and then inviting them to his parents' condominium. He admitted to prurient thoughts while doing the videotaping, but there was no evidence indicating he ever tried to act on them. When defendant sought a bill of particulars regarding the actual unlawful purpose he was alleged to have had, an essential element of the offense, his motion was denied. That action was an abuse of discretion and resulted in § 10-5 being unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant, since it subjected him to a mandatory presumption of an unlawful purpose that he could not rebut. Furthermore, the State had not even amended the indictment to allege an unlawful purpose, a required element for criminal liability, until after the 120-day statutory speedy trial period had expired, so none of the delays that occurred during the period of an invalid indictment could be charged to defendant, and the amended indictment was subject to dismissal. Finally, the State conceded that ordering of HIV/AIDS and genetic marker tests was not warranted where there was no allegation of intent to engage in actual sexual conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter for further proceedings which were to include dismissal of the indictment and expungement of the order requiring HIV/AIDS and genetic marker testing.

People v. Mendoza


No. 1-03-2059


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 621; 821 N.E.2d 740; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1532; 290 Ill. Dec. 428



December 22, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 7, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Mendoza, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 118 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 1, 2005)
Appeal denied by People v. Mendoza, 215 Ill. 2d 611, 833 N.E.2d 6, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 820, 295 Ill. Dec. 524 (2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Mendoza, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 3107 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable David P. Sterba, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of reckless homicide, reckless homicide of an unborn child, and aggravated fleeing and attempting to elude a police officer. He was sentenced to 24 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who had been using marijuana and cocaine, drove away when a police car approached his vehicle. The officer gave chase, and defendant reached speeds of up to 80 miles per hour. He ran through a red light and collided with another vehicle. The occupants of the other vehicle were killed, as was the unborn fetus of one of the occupants. Defendant was convicted of reckless homicide. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that although at the time of defendant's trial, the Illinois Supreme Court had not yet found unconstitutional the mandatory statutory presumption in § 9-3(b) of the Criminal Code of 1961, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3(b) (2000), which provided that being under the influence of alcohol or other drugs at the time of an alleged violation would be presumed to be evidence of a reckless act, another district appellate court had held the § 9-3(b) mandatory presumption to be unconstitutional. Accordingly, the court found that it could assume that the trial judge was aware that the presumption was mandatory and thus unconstitutional and that the trial court did not rely on it in finding defendant guilty of reckless homicide.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Foster


No. 1-03-1289


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 564; 821 N.E.2d 733; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1515; 290 Ill. Dec. 421



December 20, 2004, Decided  
December 20, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 7, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Foster, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 117 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Jan. 28, 2005)
Appeal denied by People v. Foster, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 691 (Ill., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CR 18239. Honorable James J. Moran, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him following a bench trial for unlawful delivery of a controlled substance within 1,000 feet of a church (UDC) in violation of § 407(b)(2) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/407(b)(2), and which sentenced him to six years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his UDC conviction, arguing that the State did not show he sold drugs near a place used for worship, a chain of custody was not established for evidence, and 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-4-3(a)(3.5), which required him to give a DNA sample to the State, violated his right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. The court found that a rational trier of fact could have inferred the structure was used primarily for religious worship based solely on the fact that the name included the word "church." The State satisfied its burden to show that reasonable measures were taken to protect the evidence from the time it was seized, and that it was improbable that the evidence was altered, so the chain of custody was established. Finally, defendant, as a convicted person, had a diminished protected privacy interest, his identity was a matter of state interest, and he lost any legitimate expectation of privacy in the identifying information derived from bodily sampling, such as DNA. In balancing the State's strong interest in identifying and deterring felons against defendant's diminished privacy rights, the court held that § 5-4-3(a)(3.5) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful delivery of a controlled substance within 1,000 feet of a church.

 

1356 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Alexander


NO. 5-03-0410


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


354 Ill. App. 3d 848; 822 N.E.2d 509; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1525; 290 Ill. Dec. 924



December 17, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. No. 01-CF-169. Honorable Terry H. Gamber, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a guilty plea to criminal sexual assault, defendant sought a declaration from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (Illinois) that the statute under which he was to be sentenced was unconstitutional because it failed to provide a probation option. The trial court denied the motion. Thereafter, defendant filed a motion to reconsider and asked the trial court to reduce his sentence. Defendant appealed from the denial of that motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the sentencing scheme violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution (Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970)), as well as the equal protection. Under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3(e) (2000), prior to its amendment, whether or not a defendant was eligible for probation depended on whether or not he was a family member of the victim. Probation could be imposed so that if a defendant was a major financial provider for the family, he or she could continue to do so. Thus, the distinction within the sentencing statute made for family members was not unconstitutional under the proportionate penalties clause. Since defendant and others similarly situated were not members of a suspect class, equal protection required only that there be a rational basis for a legislative classification that differentiates between them. If the defendant complied with certain conditions of probation, this might allow the defendant to continue providing financial support for the family, who could be victimized again if this support was extinguished. Accordingly, a rational basis existed to offer "family member" probation. No equal protection violation was found.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1357 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Alexander v. Pearson


1-02-2432


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 643; 821 N.E.2d 728; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1504; 290 Ill. Dec. 416



December 16, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 7, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. HC 50233. Honorable William S. Wood, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing his habeas corpus petition. The Illinois State Appellate Defender sought to withdraw as counsel and to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: In 1993, the inmate was convicted of two counts of armed robbery and was sentenced to concurrent extended prison terms of 55 years. One of the convictions was vacated. The inmate filed two unsuccessful pro se postconviction petitions. The second petition alleged that his 55-year extended term sentence was unconstitutional under Apprendi. That claim was rejected. The Illinois State Appellate Defender was permitted to withdraw as counsel for the inmate. There was no right to appointed counsel in a habeas corpus proceeding since such a proceeding was civil in nature. Under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 105/10(a) (2002), appointment of the State Appellate Defender was only in criminal and delinquent minor proceedings. As a result, there was no authority to appoint the State Appellate Defender as counsel in the appeal from a habeas corpus proceeding. There was no reason to dismiss the appeal due merely to the erroneous appointment of the State Appellate Defender as counsel. Dismissal, however, was appropriate. Apprendi did not apply because the inmate's direct appeal process was completed before Apprendi was decided.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Leave was granted to the Illinois State Appellate Defender to withdraw as the inmate's counsel.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of first degree murder. Defendant was sentenced to 20 years in prison. The court further sentenced defendant to a consecutive 25-year prison term for personally discharging the firearm that caused the victim's death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from the shooting death of a 17-year-old in a public housing complex, apparently after a series of arguments took place between the pair. During the final confrontation, defendant drew a gun and shot the victim twice. The trial judge found defendant guilty of first degree murder and of personally discharging the firearm that caused the victim's death, after rejecting defendant's assertions that the shooting was in self-defense or constituted second degree murder based upon an unreasonable belief in self-defense. The court agreed that the mittimus required correction to reflect one conviction of a single count of first degree murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and corrected the mittimus.

People v. Voit


No. 1-03-1126


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


355 Ill. App. 3d 1015; 825 N.E.2d 273; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1481; 292 Ill. Dec. 17



December 10, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 13, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Voit, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 345 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Mar. 14, 2005)
Appeal denied by People v. Voit, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1187 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 8131. Honorable Garritt Howard, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's convictions affirmed; Defendant's sentence for solicitation of murder for hire vacated and case remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment on jury verdict of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting her of solicitation of murder for hire and attempted first-degree murder of her husband, and sentencing her to concurrent terms of 23 and 10 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's primary defense after she was arrested for soliciting an undercover officer to kill her husband was that she had been rendered vulnerable to entrapment as defined at 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-12 (1998) by a pattern of spousal abuse. The appellate court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's exclusion of expert evidence to that effect, as it carried great potential to confuse the jury. Disclosure by a prosecutor to a potential defense witness, defendant's boyfriend, of matters that the People intended to raise on cross-examination did not unconstitutionally interfere with defendant's right to defend herself. The severe sentences mandated by statute for murder for hire did not violate defendant's rights to proportionality in sentencing or to due process, but it was error to sentence her to any term of imprisonment above the statutory minimum where the only factors cited by the trial court as aggravators were inherent in the offense. There was no violation of the "one-act, one-crime rule" where the acts giving rise to each conviction were distinct. Finally, a conceded error in the mittimus required correction on remand.


OUTCOME: The court ordered resentencing, as well as correction of the mittimus to reflect the correct number of attempted murder counts, but otherwise affirmed. It remanded the matter for resentencing.

City of Chicago v. Vill. of Elk Grove


No. 1-03-1441


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 423; 820 N.E.2d 1158; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1478; 290 Ill. Dec. 91



December 10, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 14, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Richard J. Billik, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Village of Elk Grove Village appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted judgment on the pleadings in favor of plaintiff City of Chicago in the City's action seeking a declaration that an ordinance enacted by the Village, imposing a fee on any property owner who sought to disconnect property from the Village, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The City sought to purchase Village properties to use in reconfiguring an airport. That required disconnection of the properties from the Village. The Village passed Elk Grove Village, Ill., Ordinance no. 2901, which imposed a fee for disconnecting property from the Village. The appellate court found that the ordinance was invalid. Elk Grove Village, Ill., Ordinance no. 2901 on its face applied to any disconnection. Because disconnection necessarily involved other municipalities than merely the Village, disconnection was solely within the power of the state to regulate pursuant to Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6. The Village argued that the ordinance did not regulate disconnection and did not conflict with statutory disconnection procedures, as it merely attempted to allocate the costs of its services. Elk Grove Village, Ill., Ordinance no. 2901 imposed notice requirements and filing fees for disconnection. The fee imposed by the Village, when multiplied by the minimum disconnection area of 20 acres under 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-3-6 (2002), amounted to $ 2.7 million. The Village was not permitted to burden access to the courts for disconnection proceedings to such an extent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1361 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Chen


No. 2-03-0824


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


354 Ill. App. 3d 1004; 820 N.E.2d 1136; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1496; 290 Ill. Dec. 69



December 9, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 7, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 96--D--238. Honorable James W. Jerz, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) ordered defendant employer to pay a penalty for knowingly failing to pay child support from its employee's wages pursuant to § 35 of the Income Withholding for Support Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 28/35 (2002). On appeal, petitioner argued the trial court miscalculated the penalty owed under the statute. The employer cross-appealed, arguing it owed no penalty and that § 35 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered the employer to pay $ 38,100. Petitioner claimed the § 35 penalty should be assessed on all eight paychecks the employee received from the employer. The appellate court found the first four paychecks, issued prior to service of a 2000 support order, were not subject to the penalty provision. The trial court correctly determined that only the last three paychecks were subject to the penalty. As to the final three paychecks, the court agreed with petitioner that the trial court erred in calculating the penalty, and that $ 90,600 was the proper penalty, as service of a 1997 support order on the employer was valid. The trial court expressly found the employer knowingly failed to pay amounts withheld from the final three paychecks. The employer's actions raised the presumption of a knowing violation. Section 35 was not unconstitutionally vague as applied because the $ 100-per-day penalty was not included in § 50 (750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 28/50 (2002)), entitled "Penalties,"; the legislature chose to include the penalty provision in the section detailing the duties of an employer to withhold and pay over income upon being served with an income withholding notice.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment assessing a $ 38,100 penalty was reversed and a penalty of $ 90,600 was imposed.

People v. Jordan


No. 1-03-2135


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 294; 820 N.E.2d 1083; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1470; 290 Ill. Dec. 16



December 8, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 14, 2005.
Appeal granted by People v. Jordan, 214 Ill. 2d 543, 830 N.E.2d 6, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 488, 294 Ill. Dec. 6 (2005)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by People v. Jordan, 218 Ill. 2d 255, 843 N.E.2d 870, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 4, 300 Ill. Dec. 270 (Ill., Jan. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03-1-435645. Honorable Donald D. Panarese, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of endangering the life and health of a child, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-21.6 (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from his act of leaving his child in his vehicle while he attempted to go to a bookstore. Defendant appealed his conviction, arguing that the State failed to meet its burden of proving that the child's life or health was endangered by defendant's actions, and that the child endangerment statute under which he was convicted was unconstitutional. The court found that there was testimony that an ambulance was called to the scene after the child was discovered and that the child's vital signs were checked. However, there was no testimony that the child suffered probable physical or mental damage as a result of being left in the vehicle. There was no testimony regarding the internal temperature of the vehicle, which may have been conclusive evidence that defendant placed the child in circumstances that endangered her life or health. As a result, the court held that the State failed to meet its burden of proof in this case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

People v. Schrader


No. 1-02-1565


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


353 Ill. App. 3d 684; 820 N.E.2d 489; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1471; 289 Ill. Dec. 713



December 8, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 13, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Schrader, 214 Ill. 2d 547, 830 N.E.2d 7, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 473, 294 Ill. Dec. 7 (2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Schrader v. Illinois, 546 U.S. 879, 126 S. Ct. 189, 163 L. Ed. 2d 179, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 5873 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Schrader v. Chandler, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 76498 (N.D. Ill., Aug. 28, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Leo E. Holt, Judge Presiding.
People v. Schrader, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1195 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 30, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in 1983, petitioner was convicted of murder, armed robbery, and armed violence for his involvement in a store robbery. Petitioner appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County's (Illinois) denial in 2002 of his pro se petition for relief from judgment filed pursuant to § 2-1401 of the Illinois Code of Civil Procedure, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued his extended-term sentence, based upon the brutal or heinous behavior, violated Apprendi. The appellate court found the § 2-1401 petition raised only a pure question of law - whether his extended-term sentence violated Apprendi. At the time of the claim's summary dismissal De La Paz, which held Apprendi did not apply retroactively to cases on collateral review, was the controlling authority. Therefore, the circuit court properly found the Apprendi challenge frivolous and without merit. Petitioner disputed the extended-term portion of his sentence since this "enhanced" offense was uncharged in the indictment and not proved beyond a reasonable doubt. However, Ring, like Apprendi, which required proof of an aggravating factor to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt, did not embody a substantive rule to be applied retroactively. Petitioner's challenge to the sufficiency of the indictment, for failure to charge him with "brutal or heinous" conduct, also failed. Where the State brought separate charges, each of which would support a separate conviction and were not lesser-included offenses of the other, the convictions for armed robbery and armed violence were proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Mitchell


1-02-1244


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 396; 820 N.E.2d 1052; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1448; 289 Ill. Dec. 977



December 3, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 14, 2005. As Corrected February 3, 2005.
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Mitchell, 216 Ill. 2d 717, 834 N.E.2d 907, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1125, 296 Ill. Dec. 102 (2005)
On reconsideration by, Adhered to People v. Mitchell, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 687 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Aug. 4, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 99 CR 19684 (02). Honorable Stanley J. Sacks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of first degree murder and sentenced him to 100 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: An eight-year-old girl was shot and killed while standing inside a food store. Police arrested defendant at 2 p.m. on August 1, 1999, and he was interviewed by two detectives who initially asked him for his help in the investigation. Defendant was shown the videotape of the shooting four times and repeatedly told that he was identified by a witness as the shooter. Finally, 91 hours after the arrest, and 85 hours after the custodial detention began, defendant gave his videotaped statement, the first videotaped statement ever taken in Illinois. Then, on August 6, 1999, more than 110 hours after his arrest, defendant was presented before a judge for a probable cause determination. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress his statement, and he was convicted. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, finding that even if the statement were found to be voluntary under the Fifth Amendment, the State failed to show an emergency or extraordinary circumstance that would explain the violation of defendant's U.S. Const. amend. IV rights in delaying the probable cause hearing. Accordingly, the court found that the failure to suppress defendant's confession was reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for a new trial.

People v. Keller


No. 2-03-0820


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


353 Ill. App. 3d 830; 819 N.E.2d 1205; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1456; 289 Ill. Dec. 405



December 3, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 5, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Keller, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 6 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Jan. 5, 2005)
Appeal denied by People v. Keller, 216 Ill. 2d 712, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1141 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 00--CF--1530. Honorable Richard W. Vidal, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Circuit Court vacated; matter remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a plea agreement, defendant pled guilty to armed robbery whiled armed with a firearm and was sentenced to 12 years. Defendant filed petition for declaratory judgment, naming the warden, the chairman of the Prisoner Review Board, and the Director of Corrections as respondents. The Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) summarily dismissed the petition pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-2.1 (2002). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the summary dismissal of his petition for declaratory judgment was improper under the Illinois Code of Civil Procedure, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1-101 et seq. (2002). The State argued that the pleading was in substance a post-conviction petition. The appellate court disagreed, noting that the pleading conformed in substance to the requirements for a complaint for declaratory judgment far better than to those for a postconviction petition. The core of the pleading was that the Department of Corrections misinterpreted his sentence, a claim not cognizable under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, as it did not relate to any flaw in the proceedings before his conviction. The appellate court further concluded that summarily dismissing defendant's pleading was an error that was not harmless, as it eviscerated defendant's right to be heard, the most basic procedural safeguard.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was vacated, and the case was remanded for further proceedings on defendant's petition.

Wade v. City of N. Chicago Police Pension Bd.


No. 2-04-0047


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT

December 3, 2004, Decided

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 7, 2005.
Appeal denied by, Vacated by, Remanded by Wade v. City of N. Chi. Police Pension Bd., 215 Ill. 2d 620, 828 N.E.2d 282, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 716, 293 Ill. Dec. 312 (Ill., May 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 03--MR--987. Honorable Raymond J. McKoski, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which affirmed the decision of defendant city police pension board denying him a disability pension.


OVERVIEW: The police officer was hired as a full-time police officer in 1982. In 1989, he injured his right knee playing football. A doctor examined him in 1991 and again in 1992, when his knee problems continued. In 1997, he twisted his right knee playing softball and underwent arthroscopic surgery. His knee problems continued. In 2002, he injured the same knee when he tumbled down an embankment while escorting a prisoner. Thereafter, he filed an application seeking a disability pension. The board denied the officer a line-of-duty disability pension under 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-114.1 (2002), in part because one of the three doctors selected by the board to examine the officer did not certify him as disabled pursuant to § 3-115 of the Illinois Pension Code, 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-115 (2002). On appeal, the court found that the board correctly interpreted § 3-115 as requiring that three physicians chosen by the police pension board file certificates of disability on an applicant's behalf in order to entitle an applicant to a disability pension. The court noted that whether the applicant was seeking line of duty or a non-duty pension was not pivotal to the question under § 3-115.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

People v. Stackhouse


No. 1-02-0281


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION

November 30, 2004, Decided  
November 30, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 14, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 11168(02). The Honorable Stanley J. Sacks. Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed after he was found guilty in a bench trial before the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on a charge of robbery and was sentenced to an extended prison term.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction stemmed from the robbery of a victim as the victim attempted to board a city bus. The victim, the bus driver, and the arresting police officers all testified at trial. The driver identified defendant although the victim did not. Defendant made several arguments on appeal. The court affirmed his conviction, holding that (1) the trial court erred in permitting the State to augment a defense stipulation offered to impeach the driver's identification of defendant under either the completeness doctrine or as a means of rehabilitating the driver's testimony, but because of the overwhelming non-hearsay evidence against defendant, the error did not constitute plain error; (2) it was also error to allow a police officer to testify that the victim identified defendant at the scene when the victim had testified he did not identify defendant, but the error was harmless based on the extent of the evidence against defendant; (3) defendant's extended term under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(1) (2000), based on a prior felony conviction, did not offend Apprendi; and (4) § 5-5-3.2(b)(1) did not violate the Illinois constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

People v. Teran


No. 2-02-1408


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


353 Ill. App. 3d 720; 818 N.E.2d 1278; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1398; 289 Ill. Dec. 75



November 19, 2004, Filed


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 17, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Teran, 213 Ill. 2d 573, 829 N.E.2d 793, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 303, 293 Ill. Dec. 868 (2005)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at, Motion granted by People v. Teran, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1059 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Sept. 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 98--CF--1856. Honorable George J. Bakalis, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of committing first-degree murder in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a)(1) (1998). In finding defendant guilty, the jury rejected defendant's claim that he was insane under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-2(a) (1998). After denying defendant's motion for a new trial, the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) sentenced him to 45 years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the insanity statute was unconstitutional in that it violated equal protection, due process, and the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, §§ 2, 11. The state supreme court had previously held that requiring a defendant to prove insanity did not violate due process. As to equal protection, defendant argued that the insanity statute impermissibly denied him an opportunity to escape criminal responsibility based on his inability to conform his conduct to the requirements of law, while the intoxication statute permitted the defense. The appellate court concluded that the availability of an affirmative defense was not a suspect classification under the equal protection clause, and that the Illinois General Assembly had a rational basis for amending the definition of insanity. Thus, defendant's equal protection and due process rights were not violated. The appellate court also rejected defendant's claim that the insanity statute violated the proportionate penalties clause because defendant lacked standing to make such a claim where defendant was unable to show that he was actually an aggrieved party.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Butler


No. 1-03-1978


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 57; 819 N.E.2d 1133; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1378; 289 Ill. Dec. 333



November 17, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 7, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Butler, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 653 (Ill., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CR 24658. Honorable Kenneth J. Wadas, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; mittimus corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting defendant of retail theft of merchandise valued in excess of $ 150 and of aggravated battery of a merchant, sentencing defendant to concurrent terms of five years in prison, and ordering defendant to submit a biological sample for genetic marker testing pursuant to former 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002).


OVERVIEW: The victim was struck by defendant multiple times when an altercation between defendant and the victim occurred after the victim tried to prevent defendant from shoplifting. The victim testified that he did not receive any injuries. A police officer testified, however, that the victim had contusions on his face after the fight. The victim's testimony did not preclude a finding that he suffered bodily harm as required to satisfy the elements of aggravated battery under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-4(b)(15) (2002). The officer's testimony that defendant suffered contusions on his face was sufficient to establish bodily harm under § 12-4(b)(15), as evidence of bruises was sufficient. The order that defendant submit a biological sample for genetic marker testing pursuant to former 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002) did not violate the Fourth Amendment. The State's interest in maintaining a bank of DNA samples to more accurately conduct criminal investigations exceeded defendant's expectations of privacy under U.S. Const. amend. IV, which were diminished due to defendant's incarceration. The search involved in taking a blood sample was not intrusive and was common.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The clerk of the trial court was ordered to amend the mittimus to reflect 242 days of credit.

People v. Henderson


No. 1-02-1016


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 8; 820 N.E.2d 108; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1377; 289 Ill. Dec. 600



November 16, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 7, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Henderson, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 286 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 95 CR 18154. The Honorable Joseph Urso, Judge Presiding.
People v. Henderson, 295 Ill. App. 3d 1110, 726 N.E.2d 227, 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 2160, 244 Ill. Dec. 631 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was resentenced by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on four counts of attempted murder of a police officer and nine counts of unlawful use of a weapon (UUW) because the statute under which he was sentenced had been ruled unconstitutional. Defendant appealed his new sentence.


OVERVIEW: On resentencing, the trial court imposed concurrent 35-year terms on the attempted murder convictions and a concurrent five-year term on the UUW charges. The sentence was basically the same sentence as had previously been imposed. Defendant asserted that the attempted murder sentences violated the proportionality clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970) because the penalty for attempted murder of a police officer was harsher than the penalty for second degree murder. The court disagreed. A comparative proportionality review of the two statutes was inappropriate because the statutory enhancement for attempted first degree murder of a police officer served a specific purpose that the second degree murder statute did not. It sought to both deter the intentional killing of police officers and to protect police officers who were performing their official duties. Further, the sentencing range for the attempted murder charges was not cruel, degrading, or wholly disproportionate to the crime. Finally, the record showed that the trial court carefully considered all of the mitigating and aggravating factors presented and the court could not say that the sentences were excessive.


OUTCOME: The trial court's sentencing judgment was affirmed.

 

1372 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Cargill v. Czelatdko


NO. 4-04-0278


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


353 Ill. App. 3d 654; 818 N.E.2d 898; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1369; 288 Ill. Dec. 963



November 12, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 10, 2004.
Appeal denied by Cargill v. Czelatdko, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 379 (Ill., Mar. 30, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Coles County. No. 03L44. Honorable Gary W. Jacobs, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant health care providers' motion to dismiss a medical malpractice action by plaintiffs, a patient and his wife, the Circuit Court of Coles County (Illinois) certified questions for interlocutory appeal regarding whether all requirements of former 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-622 (1996) were resurrected upon reenactment in 1998 Ill. Laws 49, and if so, whether the patient's complaint should have been dismissed with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: The patient's earlier complaint had been voluntarily dismissed. When he and his wife filed a new complaint, it was again accompanied by affidavits, as required by § 5/2-622, relating to expert certification and delays in obtaining it, but there was no affidavit to the effect that no prior action had been voluntarily dismissed. That requirement had been added in the 1996 version. Although that version of § 2/622 had later been held unconstitutional, the highest court in Illinois had explicitly found no fault with § 2/622 itself, and had authorized reenactment by the legislature. It was clear that this was what the legislature had intended in a prompt reenactment, so the 1996 requirements, including an affidavit regarding voluntary dismissals, continued to apply. Although the trial court normally had discretion to determine whether a dismissal was to be with or without prejudice, it had no discretion in the patient's case because the deficiency could not be cured in a refiling. The previous voluntary dismissal was a matter of record, so it would not be possible to attach an affidavit that it had not occurred.


OUTCOME: The court held that the requirements had been resurrected, and that since the complaint had not and could not have satisfied the requirements, dismissal with prejudice was required.

People v. Nitz


NO. 5-98-0657


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


353 Ill. App. 3d 978; 820 N.E.2d 536; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1357; 289 Ill. Dec. 760



November 10, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 7, 2005.
Appeal granted by People v. Nitz, 214 Ill. 2d 545, 830 N.E.2d 7, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 363, 294 Ill. Dec. 7 (2005)
Reversed by, Judgment entered by People v. Nitz, 219 Ill. 2d 400, 848 N.E.2d 982, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 611, 302 Ill. Dec. 418 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County. No. 88-CF-162. Honorable John Speroni, Judge, presiding.
People v. Nitz, 345 Ill. App. 3d 1167, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 2450 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After vacating an appellate court order modifying a natural life sentence imposed on defendant after his conviction, at a second trial, of first-degree murder, the Supreme Court of Illinois issued two supervisory orders directing the appellate court to determine whether failure to have the jury make the findings justifying enhanced sentencing was harmless error and also directing the court to decide all other issues raised in defendant's appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's original conviction and death sentence were reversed. A jury at his second trial also convicted him of first-degree murder, but with the least of three possible levels of culpability. Finding heinousness and brutality, the judge sentenced him to life in prison. The appellate court held, first, that since subsequent case law had vindicated use of anti-anxiety drugs, defendant could not argue that his right to testify was chilled by the possibility that his earlier testimony would be used to impeach him. The evidence did not support a lesser-included offense instruction. A juror's affidavit regarding misgivings felt and expressed in the jury room could not be used to impeach the verdict in the absence of any showing that jurors lied during voir dire. Most evidentiary rulings were within the judge's discretion, and one abuse was harmless error. With reluctance, since the Blakely decision suggested such error was never harmless, the court undertook, as directed, harmless error review of the trial court's imposition of a life sentence. It held that the jury in question, which struggled to reach a guilty verdict, would never have found facts supporting an enhanced sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction, but once again modified his sentence to one of 60 years' imprisonment.

County of Kendall v. Rosenwinkel


Nos. 2-03-1028 & 2-03-1216 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


353 Ill. App. 3d 529; 818 N.E.2d 425; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1349; 288 Ill. Dec. 737



November 5, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Released for Publication December 3, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County. Nos. 02--CH--77, 02--OV--19, 02--OV--20, 02--OV--38, 02--OV--39. Honorable Leonard J. Wojtecki, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Case No. 2--03--1028, reversed and remanded with directions; Case No. 2--03--1216, affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In related cases, defendants, property owners and tenants, challenged orders from the Circuit Court of Kendall County (Illinois), which were in favor of plaintiff county on charges that they violated Kendall, Ill., County Zoning Ordinance (CZO) § 7.00(H)(3)(b), which imposed fines on them, and which ordered them to remove a grain bin that was constructed too close to a roadway.


OVERVIEW: The county filed complaints alleging that the owners committed zoning violations on their property. Identical complaints were filed against the tenants. The complaints alleged that the location of a grain bin on the property was in violation of setback provisions in CZO § 7.00(H)(3)(b). Following hearings, the trial court entered orders for an injunction to remove the bin and for convictions of the owners and the tenants for violating the CZO. After fines were assessed, the owners and the tenants appealed. The court found that the record did not show that the trial court balanced the equities, so it abused its discretion in issuing an injunction. Moreover, the evidence did not show that the tenants had knowledge that the location of the grain bin violated the CZO, or that they had the power to cure the violation, so the tenants could not be found to have violated the CZO. Finally, the fines imposed on the owners were partially invalid because there was not a clear preponderance of the evidence that the owners were subject to multiple fines. A remand for findings as to the proper sentencing of the owners was required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders on the complaints against the tenants for a mandatory injunction and for a conviction of the tenants. The court affirmed the convictions on the complaints against the property owners, but the court remanded for resentencing.

People v. Robert H. (In re Robert H.)


Nos. 2-04-0341 & 2-04-0342 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


353 Ill. App. 3d 316; 818 N.E.2d 406; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1345; 288 Ill. Dec. 718



November 4, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 3, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 99--JA--87. Honorable Thomas C. Dudgeon, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) entered an order which found that it was in a child's best interests to remain under the care of the subsidized guardians appointed in a separate probate proceeding, discharged an agency as the child's guardian, terminated the wardship of the child, and closed the juvenile case. Respondents, the child's parents, appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued that the order improperly permitted the subsidized guardianship to continue indefinitely and prevented them from making further efforts to accomplish reunification with their child. The parents claimed that the order was akin to an order terminating their parental rights. The appellate court held that 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2-28(2) (2002) of the Illinois Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/1-1 et seq. (2002), specifically authorized the permanent transfer of guardianship when other options were unavailable. The trial court found that none of the permanency goals detailed in the statute were appropriate. Under these circumstances, the trial court was authorized pursuant to 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2-28(2)(E) to enter a permanency goal of subsidized guardianship. Additionally, after the trial court selected this goal, the agency was statutorily prohibited from providing further reunification services pursuant to 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2-28(2). As the trial court was statutorily authorized to take the action that it did in this case, the appellate court held that the parents' allegations of error were without merit.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted him on eight counts of official misconduct in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33-3(a), (c) (1998), in connection with a delinquent debt defendant owed as a former town supervisor to a township for his mother-in-law's care at the county nursing home.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a former town supervisor, was charged with several counts of official misconduct for failing to pay a debt to the town. Ann. 1/70-15(c)(v) (1998) was too ambiguous to supply a mandatory duty that defendant allegedly failed to perform, and that the State failed to prove the counts beyond a reasonable doubt. Finally, the court held that three of the counts were not properly filed within six years, as required by 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6(b) (1998), though the other counts were timely charged.


OUTCOME: The court reversed five of the eight convictions of official misconduct, but affirmed on three of the counts.

People v. Tolbert


No. 1-02-3514


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


354 Ill. App. 3d 94; 820 N.E.2d 6; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1293; 289 Ill. Dec. 498



October 29, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 7, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Tolbert, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1595 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 15, 2004)
Appeal denied by People v. Tolbert, 214 Ill. 2d 549, 830 N.E.2d 8, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 452, 294 Ill. Dec. 8 (2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Tolbert v. Illinois, 546 U.S. 836, 126 S. Ct. 67, 163 L. Ed. 2d 92, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 6245 (2005)

Writ of habeas corpus denied Tolbert v. Gaetz, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 73883 (N.D. Ill., July 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable J. Fleming, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder committed by personally discharging a firearm. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to a term of 40 years for the murder, with 25 years added pursuant to § 5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii) of the Unified Code of Corrections, codified at 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii) (2000), for a total sentence of 65 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction. The prosecution's case depended on the identification testimony of four witnesses. The appellate court found that all had been at the club, the scene of the shooting, for some time prior to the murder, and in the crowd they saw the murderer speak with the victim for several minutes. In addition, despite some differences, the appellate court could not say that the prosecution's witnesses gave such severely inconsistent testimony that no rational trier of fact could rely on their identifications of defendant as the shooter. Next, the appellate court concluded that defendant's ineffective assistance claim failed because counsel's decision to abandon impeachment of a prosecution witness was tactical after some testimony led to bolstering the witness's testimony. Finally, the appellate court upheld defendant's sentence, concluding that it was not disproportionate and was not double-enhanced, as defendant's personal discharge of the fatal firearm was an additional element not implicit in the included offense of murder in which defendant personally discharged a firearm.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1378 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Franz v. Calaco Dev. Corp.


Nos. 2-03-0672 & 2-03-0699 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


352 Ill. App. 3d 1129; 818 N.E.2d 357; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1319; 288 Ill. Dec. 669



October 21, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 18, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 99--LA--187. Honorable Maureen P. McIntyre, Judge, Presiding.
Franz v. Calaco Dev. Corp., 322 Ill. App. 3d 941, 751 N.E.2d 1250, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 482, 256 Ill. Dec. 413 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: In appeal No. 2-03-0672, order affirmed; in appeal No. 2-03-0699 judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff limited partner sued defendants, the general partner and the chief operating officer, for breach of a partnership agreement and breach of fiduciary duty. Defendants counterclaimed for declaratory judgment. The Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) found for the partner on his claims against the general partner and on the counterclaims, and against the partner on the claim against the operating officer. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The partner claimed that even though the operating officer was not a signatory to the agreement, he should have been found to have breached a fiduciary duty because he was so involved in the partnership that he created a fiduciary relationship between himself and the partners. The appellate court disagreed, noting that the written contract was the determinative factor. The partner also claimed that he was entitled to punitive damages for the general partner's breach. Because the appellate court determined that a reasonable person could have ruled the way the trial court did, the appellate court found no abuse of discretion. Next, the appellate court concluded that the trial court erred in failing to hold the partner liable under the Illinois Mortgage Act, 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 905/1 et seq. (2002), for failing to release the mortgage after the debt had been paid. As such, the general partner was entitled to recover statutory damages and reasonable attorney's fees. Finally, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision denying the general partner's claim for interest on loans to the partnership because the evidence showed that the loans were executed in bad faith.


OUTCOME: The trial court's holdings in favor of the operating officer on the fiduciary duty claim, that punitive damages should not be imposed against the general partner, denying interest payments to the general partner for loans to the partnership, and valuing the property were affirmed. The decision denying recovery to the general partner under the Illinois Mortgage Act was reversed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Crutchfield


NO. 5-03-0043


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


353 Ill. App. 3d 1014; 820 N.E.2d 507; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1290; 289 Ill. Dec. 731



October 19, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Crutchfield, 829 N.E.2d 790, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 181, 293 Ill. Dec. 865 (Ill., 2005)
Appeal denied by People v. Crutchfield, 221 Ill. 2d 649, 857 N.E.2d 676, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1124, 306 Ill. Dec. 277 (2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Crutchfield v. Illinois, 549 U.S. 1219, 127 S. Ct. 1274, 167 L. Ed. 2d 97, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 2260 (2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Crutchfield v. Rednour, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 111699 (S.D. Ill., Aug. 9, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County. No. 99-CF-148. Honorable John Speroni, Judge, presiding.
People v. Crutchfield, 324 Ill. App. 3d 1162, 805 N.E.2d 765, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 4310, 282 Ill. Dec. 146 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a)(1) (1996), and sentenced to natural life in the Department of Corrections. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was denied a fair trial because he was required to wear a stun belt without the trial court determining that it was necessary. While the appellate court agreed that such was a due process violation, the appellate court found that defendant failed to show that the error prejudiced him to the extent that it deprived him of a fair trial. In so deciding, the appellate court noted that defendant did not testify, the stun belt did not hamper the presentation of his defense, and there was no evidence that the jury was aware that defendant was wearing the belt. In addition, defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim failed because the evidence against him was overwhelming and thus, defendant could not prove he was prejudiced. Defendant also argued that his sentence violated the ex post facto and double jeopardy clauses of the United States and Illinois Constitutions. The appellate court found no error, noting that, inter alia, the statutory change was procedural and not substantive, and that defendant was tried for the same offense at both trials and thus, was not placed in double jeopardy for being retried following his successful appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Carroccia


No. 2-03-0465


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


352 Ill. App. 3d 1114; 817 N.E.2d 572; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1288; 288 Ill. Dec. 214



October 18, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 18, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 00-CF-1385. Honorable Grant S. Wegner, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested and charged with first-degree murder, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a) (2000). After a jury trial, he was acquitted. Defendant petitioned under § 5(a) of the Criminal Identification Act, codified at 20 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 2630/5(a) (2002), to expunge the records of his arrest. The Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) denied the petition with prejudice. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court abused its discretion in refusing to expunge his arrest records because the State failed to prove a compelling need to preserve them. The appellate court noted that under 20 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 2630/5(a) (2000), the court could, but was not required to, grant such relief to those meeting the requirements of § 5(a) of the Act. In examining the relevant factors, the appellate court noted that, in favor of expungement was defendant's age and lack of criminal history. However, the appellate court also noted that, inter alia, there was a lot of circumstantial evidence against defendant and that expungement was not necessary for employment purposes because defendant worked for a family business. As for defendant's contention that the trial court erred in denying the petition to expunge with prejudice, the appellate court found no error, noting that contrary to defendant's contention, the doctrine of res judicata did not bar him from filing a new petition for expungement alleging additional facts not extant on the date the trial court denied the initial petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1381 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Edwards


No. 1-03-1629


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


353 Ill. App. 3d 475; 818 N.E.2d 814; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1250; 288 Ill. Dec. 879



October 15, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 13, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Edwards, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 648 (Ill., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Stanley J. Sacks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant convicted on a jury verdict in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of armed robbery and vehicular invasion appealed that portion of his sentence that required him to submit a sample of blood for DNA analysis. He argued that such DNA extraction under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002) violated his Fourth Amendment guarantee against unreasonable searches and seizures.


OVERVIEW: Section 5-4-3 had originally applied only to persons convicted of sex offenses, but the version applied to defendant called for collection of samples from many kinds of convicted felons. He argued that it was unduly intrusive and applied to a group of offenders that was too broad, rather than being narrowly tailored to detection of sex offenders, for which DNA evidence was especially helpful. The appellate court applied both tests that courts had used in determining whether DNA extraction statutes violated the Fourth Amendment--the special needs test, under which a warrantless, suspicionless search could only be justified if it met a special need that went beyond normal law enforcement activities, and the balancing test, under which the State's interest was balanced against the intrusion on privacy--and found the statute constitutional under both. Building an identification database went beyond ordinary law enforcement activities but fulfilled a special need to identify felons, and the State's interest in detecting offenders far outweighed the minimal intrusion of a blood sample collection from a convicted felon whose expectation of privacy was already diminished.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.

Appeal denied by People v. Phillips, 213 Ill. 2d 571, 829 N.E.2d 792, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 219, 293 Ill. Dec. 867 (2005)
Appeal granted by People v. Phillips, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 627 (Ill., Feb. 24, 2005)
Reversed by People v. Phillips, 217 Ill. 2d 270, 840 N.E.2d 1194, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1625, 298 Ill. Dec. 759 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit Henry County, Illinois, Nos. 99--CF--317, 99--TR--5333. Honorable Jay M. Hanson, Judge Presiding.
People v. Phillips, 208 Ill. 2d 550, 804 N.E.2d 1066, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 385, 281 Ill. Dec. 771 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Conviction vacated; case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a case involving an appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Henry County (Illinois), the matter was before the appellate court pursuant to a supervisory order of the Illinois Supreme Court directing the appellate court to vacate its earlier judgment and to reconsider its decision in light of the Campbell decision to determine if a different result was warranted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of several drug charges. At trial, the State presented, by stipulation, laboratory reports establishing the contents, identity, and weight of the drugs found in defendant's car at the time of her arrest. The appellate court concluded that in order to waive defendant's Sixth Amendment right of confrontation by stipulating to the admission of evidence, there had to be some affirmative showing or indication by defendant in the record that she did not object to or dissent from the attorney's decision to stipulate. The appellate court found that the record did not demonstrate defendant's knowing agreement with or objection to the stipulation.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was vacated, and the case was remanded.

People v. Salgado


1-01-2735


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


353 Ill. App. 3d 101; 817 N.E.2d 1079; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1180; 288 Ill. Dec. 429



September 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 23, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Stuart E. Palmer, Judge Presiding.
People v. Salgado, 307 Ill. App. 3d 1075, 760 N.E.2d 1062, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 3770, 260 Ill. Dec. 289 (Ill. App. Ct., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate pled guilty to first degree murder. He did not file a motion seeking to vacate his guilty plea, a motion to reconsider his sentence, or a direct appeal from his conviction. After his pro se petition for postconviction relief was denied, he filed a pro se petition for transcripts, which the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, denied. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's petition for transcripts and common law records cited Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 606, which dealt with direct appeals; however, the time for him to have filed a direct appeal had expired. The appellate court held that his petition could not be characterized as a postconviction petition since no gist of a constitutional claim for relief was presented in it, and only issues of constitutional magnitude were cognizable under the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. (2000). He did not assert a violation of a statutory law, much less a substantial deprivation of a constitutional right. There was simply no basis presented in his petition for the transcripts he sought, and the circuit court acted within its discretion in rejecting his request for them. His petition was nothing more than a random request for free transcripts made without any pending litigation or proceedings in the circuit court. Not only was there no basis for the inmate's petition, there was no basis for his appeal. Under the circumstances, the denial of a request for free transcripts was not an appealable order and the appellate court had no jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

People v. Peppers


No. 1-03-2543


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


352 Ill. App. 3d 1002; 817 N.E.2d 1152; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1185; 288 Ill. Dec. 502



September 30, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 23, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Peppers, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 646 (Ill., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable James R. Epstein, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and possession of a controlled substance, appealed his sentence of five years from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Defendant contended, inter alia, that the trial court's order, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-4-3 (2002), which compelled defendant to provide a blood sample for DNA identification databases, violated defendant's Fourth Amendment rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of heroin. The parties stipulated to an expert's testimony that the substance recovered was heroin. The appellate court held that the Fourth Amendment was not offended by 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-4-3. Incarcerated felons had a substantially diminished expectation of privacy. The testing, by needle or swab, was minimally intrusive. The State was not investigating a particular or specific crime. It was conducting a technologically accurate identification procedure that would enhance the administration of justice, reaching back to solve past crimes and extending forward to identify future offenders, convicting the guilty and acquitting the innocent. Defendant waived his right to challenge an expert witness as he stipulated to the expert's findings. The trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied defendant's request for treatment alternatives for safe communities (TASC) probation. The trial court reviewed defendant's drug abuse, earlier probation violations, failure to complete boot camp, and the parole violation before imposing the sentence. Also, defendant failed to show that he qualified for treatment.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

Clifford v. Wharton Bus. Group, L.L.C.


No. 1-03-2932


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


353 Ill. App. 3d 34; 817 N.E.2d 1207; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1186; 288 Ill. Dec. 557



September 30, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 23, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 L 7119. Honorable Kathy M. Flanagan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an injured construction worker and his wife (worker), challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Cook Count (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant general contractor on the worker's negligence action for damages from a work related injury.


OVERVIEW: The worker was employed by a subcontractor as a carpenter on a construction site owned by the contractor. He alleged that he was injured when he fell through an opening in a floor when he tried to hold up a collapsing wall. The contractor moved for summary judgment on the worker's negligence complaint, arguing it was not liable for the acts or omissions of its independent contractors under the retained control doctrine. The circuit court granted the motion and the worker appealed. The worker argued the circuit court failed to consider premises liability law, as expressed in Restatement (Second) of Torts §§ 343 and 343A (1965). The court held that the circuit court erred by deciding purely under retained control without considering the distraction exception. It was for the jury to decide whether the contractor, as owner of the premises, exercised the care required towards the worker, as an invitee, where the worker was likely to be distracted from a known danger of a hole in the floor. Moreover, the exception applied whether or not the contractor created the hazard or could foresee the specific distraction. Since a jury question remained, summary judgment was improper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the contractor and the court remanded for further proceedings concerning the contractor's liability as the owner or possessor of the premises.

People v. Ramos


No. 1-03-2963


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


353 Ill. App. 3d 133; 817 N.E.2d 1110; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1188; 288 Ill. Dec. 460



September 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 23, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CR 17528. Honorable Catherine M. Haberkorn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of residential burglary and sentencing him to a term of 16 years' imprisonment as a Class X repeat offender. He argued that the trial court abused its discretion in imposing such a long sentence and that a requirement that he submit to taking of a DNA sample pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3(a)(3.5) (2002) violated the Fourth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: Even though defendant's eight prior felony convictions qualified him as a Class X offender subject to three strikes sentencing, he argued that the trial court had abused its discretion in failing to consider the nonviolent nature of his crimes, his educational and religious activities, and his employment and family responsibilities as mitigating circumstances. The appellate court presumed that the trial court had considered those mitigators, noting that the fact that nothing had caused defendant to stop his criminal career could be regarded as one more reason to impose a long sentence. The fact that his younger co-defendant received a shorter sentence was not determinative. Defendant then challenged the taking of a DNA sample, arguing that in cases not involving sex offenders, there was no special need warranting such an intrusion. The appellate court determined the reasonableness of the intrusion by balancing the State's interest in identifying past and future offenders (and non-sex offenders could also be identified by DNA on occasion) against a convict's limited privacy interest and the minimal physical intrusion required, and found no constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
