People v. Schrader


1-02-1565


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1195



September 30, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Schrader, 353 Ill. App. 3d 684, 820 N.E.2d 489, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1471, 289 Ill. Dec. 713 (Ill. App. Ct., Dec. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Leo E. Holt, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his pro se petition for relief from judgment pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2002).


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted in 1983 of murder, armed robbery, and armed violence. He was sentenced to an extended term of 70 years on the murder conviction. No direct appeal was taken but the inmate did file two unsuccessful postconviction petitions. He then filed his § 2-1401 petition, which was summarily dismissed. On appeal, the inmate argued that the circuit court was without authority to summarily dismiss the petition, that his extended term sentence violated Ring, and that his convictions for armed robbery and armed violence were prohibited by the one-act, one-crime doctrine. The court affirmed, holding that (1) the circuit court could summarily dismiss a § 2-1401 petition if it was frivolous; (2) the inmate's challenge to his sentence was frivolous and thus, summary dismissal of the § 2-1401 petition was proper; (3) at the time sentence was entered, the convicting court was authorized to impose the extended sentence, and Ring could not be used retroactively to make an Apprendi challenge to the sentence; and (4) the inmate was properly convicted of both armed robbery and armed violence as they involved different acts and neither was a lesser included offense of the other.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Parker v. Snyder


NO. 4-03-0745


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


352 Ill. App. 3d 886; 817 N.E.2d 126; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1206; 288 Ill. Dec. 1



September 29, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 12, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 02MR338. Honorable Robert J. Eggers, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Sangamon County (Illinois), granted summary judgment to defendants, a state official and state corrections department, after plaintiff inmate filed a pro se petition for writ of mandamus and sought the issuance of a writ of mandamus to compel them to lift recently-imposed restrictions on inmates like himself who presented an extremely high risk of escape. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state corrections department classified the inmate as an extremely high escape risk. A few years later, a correctional center warden and, soon thereafter, a warden for a different correctional center, issued bulletins that stated visitation restrictions for inmates designated as extremely high-level escape risk. The inmate filed a pro se petition for writ of mandamus against, inter alia, the state official and state corrections department. He alleged that the restrictions violated state law and his substantive due process rights. The trial court granted their motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the appellate court found that the inmate did not show that he had a clear right to legal relief, especially since the state official and the state corrections department did not violate state law in allowing the restrictions to be imposed, as those restrictions addressed safety and security concerns. It also found that he did not show his substantive due process rights were violated because the restrictions did not involve a fundamental right, and, thus, their rational relationship to safety and security concerns meant no constitutional violation occurred.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Anderson


No. 1-03-1615


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


352 Ill. App. 3d 934; 817 N.E.2d 1000; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1145; 288 Ill. Dec. 350



September 27, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 23, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Anderson, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1088 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 86 CR 16841. Honorable Michael Toomin, Judge Presiding.
People v. Anderson, 266 Ill. App. 3d 947, 641 N.E.2d 591, 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1265, 204 Ill. Dec. 367 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that summarily dismissed, sua sponte, his 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2002) motion to vacate judgments convicting him of multiple murders and sentencing him to life in prison. He argued that the sentence violated Apprendi, and that his petition should not have been dismissed without a hearing.


OVERVIEW: Although summary dismissals were permitted in Illinois post-conviction relief proceedings, the inmate, whose post-conviction relief efforts had already failed, sought relief under § 2-1401 on grounds that the sentence imposed on him, based on the heinousness and brutality of his murders of co-workers, violated the rule of Apprendi. He made this argument even though it was established that Apprendi did not apply to cases where appeals had been exhausted prior to the decision or to the imposition of an extended-term prison sentence on a death eligible person such as the inmate. The appellate court held that it was error to summarily dismiss the petition, since statutory post-conviction proceedings were exceptions to the general rule that civil proceedings could not be dismissed without notice and a hearing. Nonetheless, since the inmate's only claim was an utterly meritless Apprendi argument, his petition could not possibly have succeeded and any error was harmless.


OUTCOME: Although the court agreed that error had occurred, it affirmed the order of dismissal because any error was harmless.

People v. Carmen D. (In re Kenneth J.)


No. 1-02-3543


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


352 Ill. App. 3d 967; 817 N.E.2d 940; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1128; 288 Ill. Dec. 290



September 21, 2004, Filed; Nunc Pro Tunc August 10, 2004


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 23, 2004.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joan O'Brien, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found her unfit on the basis that she failed to make reasonable progress toward the return of her child within the nine-month period following adjudication of neglect or abuse and/or within any nine-month period thereafter. The order also terminated her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: Contrary to the mother's contention, the appellate court found that the State's petition did not fail to state a cause of action and that the mother's failure to challenge the petition at trial waived her ability to do so on appeal. The appellate court also disagreed with the mother's contention that the trial court erred in admitting the parenting assessment team report because it was irrelevant to the issue of her fitness and was not a business record. The report extensively addressed conditions or circumstances of the mother that related to her fitness and provided additional information to the court, necessary for the court to render its decision on the mother's fitness. As for the mother's contention that the finding of unfitness was against the manifest weight of the evidence, the appellate court found that the evidence was not close. While the mother complied with many of the service goals and received some satisfactory ratings, she did not comply with the most important goals, i.e., she refused homemaker services to remedy the defects in her living arrangements, she often failed to satisfy the therapy goals, and she refused visitation when it suited her needs.

People v. Uptain


NO. 4-02-0677


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


352 Ill. App. 3d 643; 816 N.E.2d 797; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1283; 287 Ill. Dec. 830


July 21, 2004, Submitted  
September 15, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 19, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Coles County. No. 01CF504. Honorable Dale A. Cini, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence reversed; cause remanded to the trial court for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Coles County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of three counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse. Defendant was sentenced to concurrent three-year terms of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from sexual intercourse with his 16-year-old neighbor. Defendant contended on appeal that the trial court erred in refusing to give the jury an instruction stating that it was a defense to the charge that defendant reasonably believed the victim was at least 17 years old. The court was unable to say that the evidence was so clear and convincing as to justify the failure of the trial court to instruct the jury on the affirmative defense claimed by defendant that he reasonably thought the victim was 17 years or older. The court noted that defendant was not required to present any evidence that he believed the victim was at least 17 because the evidence that he did present that the victim engaged in playful and flirtatious behavior on the evening in question, coupled with the evidence presented by the State that defendant had never been advised of the victim's age, was sufficient to raise the affirmative defense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and sentence and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

 

1392 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Leason


No. 1-02-3722


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


352 Ill. App. 3d 450; 816 N.E.2d 747; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1090; 287 Ill. Dec. 780



September 9, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 26, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 91 CR 4818. Honorable Henry R. Simmons, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which summarily dismissed his successive pro se postconviction petition. Defendant had been convicted of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: During a dispute with a rival gang, defendant's fellow gang member fatally shot a member of the rival gang. Defendant was found guilty of first degree murder on the theory of accountability. The court affirmed. Defendant filed a pro se postconviction petition, which the trial court summarily dismissed as frivolous and patently without merit. He then filed the instant successive pro se postconviction petition, alleging he was prejudiced by the trial court's failure to question jurors about gang bias during voir dire. The trial court summarily dismissed the petition. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that defendant failed to satisfy the requirements of the cause and prejudice test under the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, which required that a defendant show "cause" for failing to raise his issue in a prior proceeding and actual "prejudice" from the claimed error. Defendant argued that he met the cause requirement because the Illinois case that established the legal predicate for his gang bias claim was not decided until 2000; therefore, he could not raise it earlier. The court found that a lack of precedent could not serve as "cause" for failing to raise an issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

People v. Hall


No. 1-03-1276


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


352 Ill. App. 3d 537; 816 N.E.2d 703; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1063; 287 Ill. Dec. 736



September 3, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 26, 2004.
Rehearing denied by People v. Hall, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1294 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Oct. 21, 2004)
Appeal denied by People v. Hall, 219 Ill. 2d 578, 852 N.E.2d 243, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 649, 303 Ill. Dec. 836 (Ill., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 19314. The Honorable Thomas M. Tucker, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, following a bench trial, convicted him of aggravated robbery, sentenced him to 10 years in prison, and ordered him to submit DNA samples for genetic marker purposes pursuant to the Unified Code of Corrections, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-4-3(a-5) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a video store and approached the victim at the counter after all customers had left, asked him if he was wearing a bulletproof vest, questioned him with respect to whether he ever had been or presently wanted to be shot, and moved his hand to his waist in a grabbing motion two or three times while speaking to him. He then informed the victim that he was going to take property from the store, and filled two plastic bags with some 50 DVDs and two videotapes. Defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery and subjected to the compulsory extraction of DNA. On appeal, the court affirmed, first finding that the aggravated robbery statute was not ill-defined or lacking of all objective criteria; thus it was not unconstitutionally vague so as to violate defendant's due process rights. The court then found that any slight intrusion upon defendant's diminished privacy rights in providing a sample for genetic marker collection was significantly outweighed by the state's compelling interests in preventing recidivism, correctly identifying offenders, and solving past and future crimes. Therefore, the court found that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-4-3(a-5) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1394 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Teresa R. (In re Cheyenne S.)


3-03-0047


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


351 Ill. App. 3d 1042; 815 N.E.2d 1186; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1064; 287 Ill. Dec. 383



September 1, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 1, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit. Tazewell County, Illinois. No. 98--JA--16. Honorable Richard D. McCoy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed from order of the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Tazewell County, Illinois, which found her to be an unfit parent and terminated her parental rights to a four-year-old child and ordered subsidized guardianship for a 15-year-old child. The petition to terminate parental rights had been filed by petitioner State.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the mother asserted that the State failed to prove that she was an unfit parent. The court agreed. It was unclear which of two neglect proceedings the State based its termination petition on, but the court ruled that neither of the proceedings provided a basis for finding the mother unfit. The first proceeding dealt only with the 15-year-old. Although that child's father was found to have neglected the child, no finding was entered against the mother. Both children were involved in the second case. There, the mother was deemed to have neglected the children by allowing the four-year-old's father to have contact with him in violation of an order of protection the mother had been ordered to obtain. However, the trial court had no authority to order the mother to obtain the order of protection. Thus, violation of the order of protection could not, as a matter of law, be the basis for finding the mother had neglected her children. The court rejected the claim that the nine-month remedial period never began to run in the second proceeding because no dispositional hearing was held. That period began to run at the moment the children were adjudicated neglected.


OUTCOME: The trial court's ruling of unfitness, its order terminating the mother's rights, and its order for subsidized guardianship were reversed.

People v. Bushong (In re Bushong)


No. 2-02-1213


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


351 Ill. App. 3d 807; 815 N.E.2d 103; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1055; 286 Ill. Dec. 893



August 30, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 23, 2004.
Rehearing denied by People v. Bushong (In re Bushong), 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1197 (Ill. App. Ct., Sept. 23, 2004)
Appeal denied by People v. Bushong (In re Bushong), 2005 Ill. LEXIS 119 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 98--MR--381. Honorable Edward R. Duncan, Jr., Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) found defendant to be a sexually violent person pursuant to the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act (SVPA), 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 et seq. (2000), and ordered him committed to a Department of Human Services (DHS) treatment facility indefinitely. Defendant petitioned alternatively for conditional release or discharge. The trial court denied the petition, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that he was entitled to either a reversal of the original finding of sexual violence or a reversal of the denial of his conditional release petition. The appellate court declined to address the due process claim because defendant had not established that the evidence introduced at the original commitment hearing was closely balanced or that he was prejudiced. The appellate court held that persons committed under the SVPA and the Sexually Dangerous Persons Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 205/1.01 et seq. (2000), were not similarly situated and that 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/65(a)(2) (2000) and 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/60(d) (2000) did not violate equal protection guarantees by allowing the State to prove its case for continued commitment by only clear and convincing evidence. The legislature could have rationally determined that persons who had already been adjudicated sexually violent beyond a reasonable doubt posed a greater risk to society than those whose sexual dangerousness had not been established in a prior criminal proceeding. Moreover, there was a legitimate state interest in protecting the public from sexually violent persons.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court of was affirmed.

People v. Carroll


No. 1-03-0456


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT


351 Ill. App. 3d 972; 815 N.E.2d 907; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 997; 287 Ill. Dec. 263



August 27, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 16, 2004. Released for Publication October 6, 2004. As Corrected October 15, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Carroll, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1080 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 87 CR 14661 (03). Honorable Dennis J. Porter, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denying the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sentenced to an extended term of 60 years in prison for armed robbery. The inmate filed the instant petition pro se arguing that his extended-term sentence was unconstitutional under Apprendi because the factors used to extend the inmate's sentence were not alleged in the indictment or proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The trial court treated the petition as a petition for post-conviction relief under the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1 et seq., and summarily dismissed it. The petition was properly treated as a post-conviction petition because the pro se petition alleged matters cognizable under the Act. The inmate's claim was not jurisdictional in nature. Thus, a petition for habeas corpus was not the appropriate avenue for relief. The petition was properly dismissed without an evidentiary hearing, as the petition was without merit. Apprendi did not apply retroactively to the instant case. No prejudice resulted to the inmate by the trial court's decision to treat the petition as a post-conviction relief petition, as the inmate was permitted to file a post-conviction petition where fundamental fairness required.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. M.T. (In re M.T.)


No. 1-01-2314


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


352 Ill. App. 3d 131; 816 N.E.2d 354; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1001; 287 Ill. Dec. 592



August 27, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 6, 2004.
Later proceeding at In re M.T., 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1104 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Aug. 31, 2004)
Appeal granted by People v. M.T. (In re M.T.), 213 Ill. 2d 559, 829 N.E.2d 788, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 50 (2005)
Reversed by People v. M.T. (In re M.T.), 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1093 (Ill., June 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Stuart F. Lubin, Judge Presiding.
In re M.T., 209 Ill. 2d 581, 808 N.E.2d 1007, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 945, 283 Ill. Dec. 719 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of indecent solicitation of an adult pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-6.5(a)(1)(ii) (2000), found him delinquent, and sentenced him to 30 days in the juvenile detention center and 18 months' probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 16-year-old high school student, was charged with soliciting another 16-year-old student by offering him oral sex from a female student. The student accepted the offer and defendant told another student to go and get the female student. When she arrived, he pointed to the student and she began performing oral sex on him. Defendant was convicted of violating the indecent-solicitation-of-an-adult statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-6.5 (2000). The court originally affirmed, but the Illinois Supreme Court remanded for consideration of defendant's constitutional challenges. The court then reveresed the judgment, finding that the sentencing provisions in the statute violated the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970) and rendered the entire statute invalid. The court found that under the indecent-solicitation-of-an-adult statute, a nonviolent solicitation such as the one defendant was accused of was punished more harshly than a violent solitication where the solitication was accompanied with violence or the threat of violence. The court held that such a penalty was disproportionate and unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1398 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ford


No. 1-02-2067


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


352 Ill. App. 3d 55; 815 N.E.2d 872; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 981; 287 Ill. Dec. 228



August 26, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 6, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Ford, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1888 (Ill., Nov. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Michael P. Toomin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Cook County (Illinois) that summarily dismissed his third petition for post-conviction relief from that part of a judgment convicting him of attempted first-degree murder that sentenced him to an extended prison term, arguing that the sentence was disproportionately longer than a sentence for completed second-degree murder would have been, and that sentencing procedures violated Apprendi.


OVERVIEW: The attempted murder of which defendant was convicted arose out of a terrible beating he gave to a motorcyclist whose cycle had broken down. The victim never recovered. The enhanced sentence imposed on defendant far exceeded the sentencing range for second-degree murder, but the appellate court held that this did not necessarily make his sentence unconstitutionally disproportionate. The legislature was entitled to consider many factors in rating the seriousness of an offense, and the specific intent to kill, without any of the mitigating factors that might arise in a second-degree murder setting, could reasonably have been considered to make the offense more serious. Since the proportionate sentencing requirement of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 invalidated only sentences that were so disproportionate as to shock the conscience of the community, the sentence imposed on defendant passed constitutional muster. Defendant's Apprendi-based argument was without merit because the state's highest court had already ruled that Apprendi did not apply retroactively to cases, such as defendant's, in which the direct appeal process had already concluded before Apprendi was decided.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

People v. Kasp


No. 1-03-3227


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


352 Ill. App. 3d 180; 815 N.E.2d 809; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 961; 287 Ill. Dec. 165



August 20, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 6, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Kasp, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 96 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CR 17945. The Honorable James B. Linn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment on jury verdict of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of aggravated discharge of a weapon in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.2 (2002). He argued on appeal that the statute violated constitutional sentencing proportionality and substantive due process guarantees, and that he was prejudiced by the failure to instruct jurors regarding self-defense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged as a principal since he drove a car that pursued the victim's car while his passengers repeatedly shot at the victim. His primary argument at trial was that he was not accountable for their actions, although he also presented witnesses who claimed that the victim's car was chasing defendant's car. The appellate court held, first, that the more severe sentences associated with aggravated discharge as opposed to reckless discharge of a firearm did not violate Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, because the two statutes were aimed at different types of unlawful activity differentiated by very different levels of scienter. Defendant also argued that the statute violated due process guarantees against overbreadth because it criminalized potentially innocent conduct, but the appellate court held that the absence of the words "without lawful authority" from the definition of the offense did not make it overbroad, since the statute plainly had a rational basis in the public interest in preventing people from shooting at other people. Finally, there was no plain error in failing to instruct the jury on self-defense, a theory never raised at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Arndt


No. 2-03-0660


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


351 Ill. App. 3d 505; 814 N.E.2d 980; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 974; 286 Ill. Dec. 754



August 18, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 17, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 02--CF--842. Honorable Christopher C. Starck, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, defendant was found guilty of two counts of indecent seduction of a child under § 11-6 of the Illinois Criminal Code of 1951, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-6 (2002). The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to 30 months of probation with several conditions, including 12 months of periodic imprisonment, no contract with children under the age of 18, and sex offender treatment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the State failed to prove he was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court disagreed, noting that, inter alia, the conversations made it clear that she informed defendant she was only 15. In addition, there was clear evidence that defendant communicated he wanted to make love to the girl. Next, defendant argued that he was entrapped because his conduct was incited and induced by the officer, who entered an adult-only chat room and pretended to an adult role-player. The appellate court found that defendant failed to admit essential elements of the offense by denying he knew or believed the girl to be under 17 and intended to engage in sexual conduct with her. In addition, defendant's assertions that the officer initiated contact, discussions of sex, and a meeting were not supported by the record. As for defendant's contention that a fatal variance existed between the indictment and the proof at trial, the appellate court concluded that any variance was neither material nor prejudicial. Finally, contrary to defendant's contention, the appellate court held that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-6 (2002) did not violate the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
